Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Qisas When Heirs Include Minors and Adults: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Presents the dispute on whether adult heirs may execute qisas immediately when minors exist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on adult heirs executing qisas when minors exist, and explain the proof of Abu Hanifa (dalil) and the Sahibayn's counterargument.

Core Idea
A minor cannot forgive, so the right to qisas is complete for each adult heir — unlike an absent adult who may forgive.

When a person is killed intentionally and the heirs include both adults and minors, can the adults execute qisas immediately? This passage presents the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. At stake is whether qisas is a shared right that requires unanimity or an indivisible right that each heir holds independently. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens our grasp of how causation (sabab) and capacity shape rights in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the exact legal question? Adult heirs want to execute qisas immediately; some heirs are minors.
The minors cannot act yet, so the question is whether the adults can proceed alone.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa allows immediate execution; Sahibayn require waiting until minors mature.
The matn clearly attributes the immediate-kill view to Abu Hanifa and the delay to the two.
3
Trace the Sahibayn's proof
They argue qisas is shared and indivisible; partial execution impossible; if adults take all, minors' right nullified. They analogize to an absent adult heir and to two co-owners of a slave.
The analogy to absent adult: the present heir cannot act alone because the absent one may forgive. Similarly here, minors cannot forgive but may later decide.
4
Trace Abu Hanifa's proof
Qisas is established by an indivisible cause (lineage). A minor cannot validly forgive, so the possibility of forgiveness is cut off, making the right complete for each heir. Analogous to marriage guardianship. He distinguishes the absent adult case (where the absentee might forgive) and rejects the co-owners analogy (property vs blood right).
Abu Hanifa says: since the minor cannot forgive, the right is fully established for each adult, unlike an absent adult who can forgive.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, qisas is executed immediately; under Sahibayn, it is delayed, allowing the killer to live until minors mature. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view (Zahir al-Riwayah).
The commentary supports Abu Hanifa's proof as conclusive.

Source Text

ایک شخص کو قتل کیا گیا اور اس کے اولیاء میں کچھ نابالغ ہیں اور کچھ بالغ ہیں
قصاص لینے کا طریقہ کار اقوال فقہاء
قال ومن قتل وله اولياء صغا وكبار فللكبار أن يقتلو القاتل عند ابي حنيفة وقالا ليس لهم ذلك يدرك الصغار لان القصاص مشترك بينهم ولا يمكن استيفاء البعض لعدم التجزى وفي استيفا ئهم الكل
ابطال حق الصغار فيو خر الى ادراكهم كما اذا كان بين الكبيرين واحدهما غائب او كان بين الموليين
ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا اور جو شخص قتل کیا گیا اور اس کے بالغ فری با نیچے ہیں تو بالوں کو حق ہے کہ وہ قاتل کو قتل کریں ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ ان کو یہ حق نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ نیچے بالغ ہو جائیں اس لئے کہ قصاص
ان کے درمیان مشترک ہے اور بعض کو
وصول کرناممکن نہیں ہے تجری نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور بڑوں کے وصول کرنے میں پورے قصاص کو بچوں کے حق کا ابطال تو بچوں کے متصاص کو مؤخر کیا جائے گا کہ جیسا کہ قصاص دو بڑوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو اور ان دونوں میں سے ایک غائب ہو یا قصاص دو آقاؤں کے درمیان مشترک ہو۔
تشریح ایک شخص کو عمد اقتل کر دیا گیا اور اس کے ورثہ میں سے یعنی اولیاء میں سے کچھ نابالغ ہیں اور کچھ بالغ تو قصاص کا کیا ہوگا؟ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ بچوں کے بلوغ تک قصاص کو مؤخر کیا جائے گا اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک بڑے قصاص لیں گے اور بچوں کے بلوغ کا انتظار نہ ہوگا۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قصاص تو ان سب کے درمیان مشترک حق ہے لہذا سب کے وصول کرنے سے وصول ہوگا اور ان میں وصول کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہے اور یہ بھی نہیں ہو سکتا کہ کچھ قصاص بالغین وصول کرلیں اور باقی قصاص بچے بعد نبوغ وصول کر لیں کیونکہ قصاص تو غیر منظمیری ہے۔ اور اگر بالین سارا قصاص ابھی وصول کر لیں تو حق کا ابطال لازم آتا ہے لہذا اب صرف یہی صورت ہوگئی کہ بچوں کے بلوغ تک انتظار کیا جائے اور اس کی امثلہ یہ ہیں
-1
زید اور بکر دو بھائی ہیں ان کا باپ عمد اقتل کر دیا گیا اور یہ دونوں بالغ ہیں مگر زید تو یہاں موجود اور بکر غائب ہے تو جب تک بکر نہ آ جائے قصاص کو مؤخر کیا جائے گا اس طرح یہاں بھی مؤخر ہوگا۔
نی اور کرنے ایک غلام یا پر اسلام کو کس نے عد اقتل کردیا اور اتفاق سے زید بالغ ہے اور بکر نابالغ منجب تک بکر بالغ نہ ہو قصاص کو موخر کیا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی قصاص مؤخر ہونا چاہیئے ۔
امام صاحب کی دلیل
وله انه حق لا يتجزى لثبوته بسبب لا يتجزى وهو القرابة واحتمال العفو من الصغير منقطع فيثبت لكل واحد كملا كما في ولاية الانكاح بخلاف الكبيرين لان احتمال العفو من الغائب ثابت ومسألة الموليين
ممنوعة
ترجمہ امام اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حق قصاص غیر متجری ہے اس حق کے ثابت ہونے کی وجہ سے ایسے سبب سے جو غیر متجری ہے اور وہ سبب قرابت ہے اور بچہ کی جانب سے احتمال عضو منقطع ہے تو یہ حق ہر ایک کے لئے کامل ثابت ہوگا جیسے نکاح کرنے کی ولایت میں بخلاف کبیرین کے اس لئے کہ غائب کی جانب سے احتمال عضو ثابت ہے اور دو آقاؤں کا مسئلہ غیر مسلم ہے۔
A person was killed and among his heirs there are minors and adults. The procedure for taking qisas: Statements of the jurists. Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Whoever is killed and has adult and minor heirs, the adults have the right to kill the killer according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: They do not have that right until the minors reach maturity, because qisas is shared among them and it is not possible to take part of it due to indivisibility, and if they take it all, it nullifies the right of the minors, so it is postponed until they mature, just as if the qisas is between two adults and one is absent, or between two masters. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: When a person is killed and his adult (fariq) and minor (nabil) [heirs exist], the adults have the right to kill the killer according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Sahibayn) said: They do not have this right until the minors become adults, because qisas is shared among them, and it is not possible to take part of it due to indivisibility. In the adults taking the whole, it nullifies the right of the minors, so qisas is postponed until the minors reach maturity, just as if qisas is shared between two adults with one absent, or between two masters. Explanation: A person was killed intentionally and among his heirs (awliya') there are minors and adults. What happens to qisas? The Sahibayn say: Qisas is postponed until the minors mature. Imam Abu Hanifa says: The adults will take qisas and will not wait for the minors' maturity. The proof of the Sahibayn: Qisas is a shared right among all; it is enforced only when all take it, and the minors lack capacity. It is not possible for some to take part and others later because qisas is indivisible. If the adults take the entire qisas now, the minors' right is nullified. So the only option is to wait until minors mature. Examples: 1) Zayd and Bakr are two brothers; their father is killed intentionally, both are adults but Zayd is present and Bakr absent; qisas is postponed until Bakr arrives. Similarly here. 2) A slave or [؟] Islam was killed intentionally, Zayd is adult and Bakr minor; until Bakr becomes adult, qisas is postponed. So here also qisas should be postponed. Proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: He (Abu Hanifa) said: It (qisas) is a right that is not divisible, because it is established by a cause that is not divisible, namely lineage (qarabah). The possibility of forgiveness from the minor is cut off (since a minor cannot validly forgive). Therefore it is established for each one completely, as in the guardianship of marriage. Unlike the case of two adults (one absent) because the possibility of forgiveness from the absent one exists. And the case of two masters is not conceded (i.e., the analogy is rejected).
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the execution of qisas when the victim's heirs include both adults and minors. The text first presents the ruling from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir: according to Abu Hanifa, the adult heirs may execute qisas immediately; according to the Sahibayn, they must wait until all heirs, including minors, reach maturity. The Sahibayn argue that qisas is an indivisible shared right; partial execution is impossible, and if adults take the whole, the minors' share is nullified. They analogize to a case where one adult heir is absent (qisas postponed until he returns) and to the case of two co-owners of a slave. Abu Hanifa counters that qisas is established by an indivisible cause—lineage (qarabah)—and that a minor's potential forgiveness is cut off (since a minor cannot legally forgive), so each heir holds a complete right independently, similar to marriage guardianship. The analogy to an absent adult fails because the absentee may forgive, while the minor cannot. The analogy to two masters is not accepted (it is based on a different legal principle). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as it is the position of the matn and his proof is considered stronger.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retributive justice: the right of the victim's heirs to demand like punishment for intentional killing or injury.
تجزى (tajzi'): Divisibility; the quality of being divisible into parts. Qisas is said to be non-divisible (la yatajazzā).
قرابت (qarabah): Blood relationship or lineage; the cause (sabab) that establishes the right of qisas for the heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why can adult heirs execute qisas immediately even when there are minor heirs?
A) Because qisas is divisible and adults can take their share.
B) Because the minor's inability to forgive makes the right complete for each heir.
C) Because the Sahibayn agree with this ruling.
D) Because the killer must be punished quickly to deter crime.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, because qisas is established by an indivisible cause (lineage) and a minor cannot forgive, adult heirs may execute qisas immediately without waiting for minor heirs to mature.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Qisas with Adult and Minor Heirs: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of qisas execution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas with minor heirs and apply the thamarah al-khilaf in a practical scenario.

Core Idea
When heirs include minors, Abu Hanifa permits immediate qisas; Sahibayn require delay—the right is indivisible but minors cannot pardon.

The right of qisas (retaliatory execution) belongs to the heirs of a murder victim. But what happens when some heirs are minors? Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani records a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that adult heirs may execute immediately, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad himself, insist on waiting until all heirs reach maturity. This lesson dissects the legal reasoning on both sides and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the ruling attributed to Abu Hanifa and the opposing view of Sahibayn. Abu Hanifa: adults may execute qisas immediately. Sahibayn: execution must be delayed until all heirs are adult.
Both positions are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Analyze Sahibayn's proof
Understand why Sahibayn argue for delay: qisas is a shared right that cannot be divided (ghayr mutajazzi). If adults execute, they consume the entire right, nullifying the minors' share. They analogize to the case of an absent adult heir.
The analogy with two masters of a killed slave is also cited but disputed.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa counters that qisas is indivisible because its cause (kinship) is indivisible, and minors cannot legally pardon. Hence each heir holds a complete right, analogous to guardianship in marriage (wilayat al-nikah). The possibility of pardon from an absent adult is real, but from a minor it is not, so the cases differ.
Abu Hanifa does not concede the analogy with two masters.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? If adult heirs execute the killer before minors mature, under Abu Hanifa they incur no liability; under Sahibayn, they may be liable for wrongful killing or must pay diyah.
The mufta bihi is often Abu Hanifa's view in later Hanafi practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ومن قتل وله ورثة بين كبير وصغار فللكبار أن يقتلوا عنده وعندهما ليس ذلك لهم حتى يدرك الصغار لأن القصاص مشترك بينهم ولا يمكن بعضهم استيفاءه لتجزيه واستيفاء الكبار يستوفي جميع القصاص ابطال حق الصغار فيوخر إلى ادراكهم كما اذا كان بين الكبيرين واحدهما غائب او كان بين الموليين. وله انه حق لا يتجزى لثبوته بسبب لا يتجزى وهو القرابة واحتمال العفو من الصغير منقطع فيثبت لكل واحد كملا كما في ولاية الانكاح بخلاف الكبيرين لان احتمال العفو من الغائب ثابت ومسألة الموليين ممنوعة.
He said: Whoever is killed and has heirs both adult and minor, then the adults may execute [the killer] according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) they do not have that right until the minors attain maturity, because qisas is shared among them and it is not possible for some of them to execute it due to its indivisibility, and if the adults execute it they would take all the qisas, invalidating the right of the minors, so it is delayed until they attain maturity, just as if between two adults one is absent or between two masters. And for him (Abu Hanifa) it is a right that is indivisible because it is established by a cause that is indivisible, namely kinship, and the possibility of pardon from a minor is cut off, so it is established completely for each one, as in the guardianship of marriage, unlike the case of two adults because the possibility of pardon from the absent one is established, and the case of two masters is not conceded.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the execution of qisas (retaliatory killing) when the heirs of the victim include both adults and minors. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani states the ruling: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the adult heirs have the right to immediately execute the killer, whereas according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad himself), they must wait until the minors reach majority. The Sahibayn argue that qisas is a shared right among all heirs and cannot be divided; if adults execute it, they consume the entire right, thus extinguishing the minors' share. They analogize this to the case where one of two adult heirs is absent – in such a case, execution is delayed until the absent one returns. Abu Hanifa counters that the right to qisas is indivisible because its cause (kinship) is indivisible, and the possibility of the minor pardoning the killer is non-existent before maturity (as minors cannot legally pardon). Hence, each heir holds a complete right, similar to the right of guardianship in marriage (wilayat al-nikah), where each guardian has full authority independently. The Sahibayn's analogy of an absent adult heir is distinguishable because the absent adult could have pardoned, so a doubt exists. As for the case of two masters of a killed slave, Abu Hanifa does not concede that it supports the Sahibayn's view; in his own position, the adult master may execute qisas without waiting for the minor master to mature. This dispute hinges on whether the right is considered divisible or indivisible and whether the possibility of future pardon from minors or absentees affects the immediate execution.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory killing of the murderer by the heirs of the victim, as a legal right.
ولایت نکاح (wilayat al-nikah): Guardianship over a minor or insane person for marriage; each guardian has full authority.
غير متجزي (ghayr mutajazzi): Indivisible; a right that cannot be split among multiple claimants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why can adult heirs execute qisas immediately even if some heirs are minors?
A) Because minors can be represented by the adults in qisas.
B) Because qisas is indivisible and minors cannot pardon, so the right is complete for each adult.
C) Because the Sahibayn allowed it in this case.
D) Because the victim's death was intentional.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn disagree on whether the presence of minor heirs delays qisas; the key factor is the indivisibility of the right and the capacity of minors to pardon.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for Killing with a Pickaxe: Iron Edge vs. Back – The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the ruling on qisas for fatal strikes with a pickaxe, highlighting the intra-Hanafi dispute on the back of the iron.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the three Hanafi positions on qisas when a fatal blow is struck with the back of an iron pickaxe, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Qisas for a metal strike requires a wound; the preferred Hanafi view requires جرح, not just the instrument.

The law of qisas (retaliation) for homicide distinguishes between weapons that typically cause death. When a pickaxe (بمر) is used, the ruling differs based on which part of the tool struck the victim. The basic rule is clear: if the iron edge cuts and causes a wound, qisas is due; if only the wooden handle strikes, only diyah (blood money) is owed. But what if the back of the iron (the blunt side) lands a fatal blow? This passage from Al-Hidayah unravels an important intra-Hanafi dispute that hinges on whether the instrument itself or the presence of a wound (جرح) is the operative cause for qisas.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic ruling
Identify the two clear cases: striking with the iron edge (qisas) and striking with the wooden handle (diyah). Note that this is the starting point from Imam Muhammad.
The cause for qisas here is the wound (جرح) from the sharp edge.
2
Identify the contested case
Focus on the third scenario: striking with the back (ظهر) of the iron – a blunt hit that may not cut. This is where the intra-Hanafi disagreement arises.
The back of the iron is still metal, but not sharp.
3
State the position of the Sahibayn and one narration from Abu Hanifa
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), and a narration from Abu Hanifa, qisas is wajib even if the back of the iron strikes, because the instrument (آلة) is iron, which is inherently deadly.
They consider the material itself sufficient for qisas, regardless of wound.
4
State the second narration from Abu Hanifa
Another narration from Abu Hanifa holds that qisas is only wajib if the strike causes a wound (جرح). A blunt impact without cutting does not warrant qisas, only diyah.
This view emphasizes the need for a wound as a condition.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text declares the second narration (requiring a wound) as الأصح (more correct). Thus, the relied-upon Hanafi view is that qisas for a metal strike requires a wound; without it, only diyah is due.
This tarjih is made by Sahib al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ومن ضرب رجلا بمر فقتله فان اصابه بالحديد قتل به وان اصابه بالعود فعليه الدية. قال وهذا اذا اصابه بحد الحديد لوجود الجرح فكمل السبب وان اصابه بظهر الحديد فعند هما يجب وهو رواية عن ابي حنيفة اعتبارا منه للالة وهو الحديد وعنه انما يجب اذا جرح وهو الاصح على ما نبينه ان شاء الله تعالى.
He said: Whoever strikes a man with a pickaxe and kills him, if he strikes him with the iron he is killed for it, and if he strikes him with the wood then he owes diyah. He said: This is when he strikes him with the edge of the iron because a wound occurs, so the cause is complete; but if he strikes him with the back of the iron, then according to the two (Sahibayn) it is obligatory (qisas), and that is a narration from Abu Hanifa considering the instrument, which is iron; and from him (another narration) that it is obligatory only if it wounds, and that is the more correct, as we will explain if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage deals with qisas (retaliation) when a person is killed by a blow from a pickaxe (or similar tool). It begins with the basic rule from Imam Muhammad: if the iron part (especially the sharp edge) strikes and causes death, qisas is due; if only the wooden handle strikes, only diyah (blood money) is due. The author (Sahib al-Hidayah) then clarifies a further dispute: if the blow lands on the back (non-sharp) part of the iron, does qisas apply? According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), qisas is still due because the instrument is made of iron, which is considered a deadly weapon. There are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one that also considers the instrument (iron) and thus requires qisas, and another that requires a wound (جرح) for qisas – meaning if the back of the iron strikes without cutting, it is not considered a slashing wound, so only diyah is due. The author states that the second narration (requiring a wound) is the more correct (الأصح) and will be elaborated later. This dispute centers on whether the cause of qisas is the instrument itself (iron, which can kill) or the actual wound (جرح). The preferred Hanafi view is that qisas requires a wound that cuts or pierces; mere blunt force with a metal object does not qualify.

Key Terms
بمر (bimirr): A pickaxe or similar tool with an iron head and wooden handle used for digging.
جرح (jarh): A wound that cuts or pierces the skin, causing blood flow; a necessary condition for qisas according to the preferred view.
ظهر الحديد (zahr al-hadid): The back or blunt side of an iron blade, as opposed to the sharp edge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the more correct (الأصح) Hanafi view, when is qisas due for a fatal blow with a pickaxe?
A) Whenever the iron part strikes, regardless of wound.
B) Only when the wooden handle strikes.
C) Only when the iron edge causes a wound.
D) Only when both iron and wood strike.

Key Takeaway
For qisas with a metal tool, the Hanafi mufta bihi requires a wound (جرح); the instrument alone is not sufficient.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate

Conditions for Qisas in Killing with a Spade and the Back of the Iron Dispute
Ruling on qisas for iron with wound, diya for wood; dispute on back of iron

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi conditions for qisas when striking with a spade and distinguish between the views of Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa regarding the back of the iron.

Core Idea
Qisas requires a wound from the iron; without a wound, only diya is due.

When a person is killed by a strike from a spade, the ruling depends on which part of the spade caused the blow and whether a wound occurred. Imam Muhammad's ruling establishes a clear distinction: if the iron part causes a wound, qisas applies; if the wooden handle, diya. However, when the blow is with the back of the iron (the blunt side) and no wound is visible, the Hanafi school has an internal dispute. This lesson examines the reasoning behind the views of Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa, and identifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two scenarios
The act is a fatal blow with a spade. Identify the two parts: iron (hadid) and wood (ʿūd). Note the ruling for each: iron with wound → qisas; wood → diya.
The wood scenario is straightforward: no qisas because the instrument is not inherently lethal.
2
Recognize the condition of wound (jarh)
The author clarifies that qisas for the iron part requires that the blow lands on the edge (ḥadd) causing a wound, which completes the cause (sabab). Without a wound, the cause is incomplete.
This condition is central to understanding the dispute.
3
Present the dispute on the back of the iron
When the blow is with the back of the iron (blunt side), Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that qisas is obligatory because the instrument is iron, which is inherently lethal. This is also one narration from Abu Hanifa.
Sahibayn's dalil: the instrument itself, regardless of wound.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's preferred view
Another narration from Abu Hanifa requires a wound for qisas even with iron. The author indicates this is the sounder opinion (al-asahh). The reasoning is that a wound indicates intentionality (ʿamd) and completes the cause; without it, the killing may be shibh ʿamd (quasi-intentional) which attracts diya, not qisas.
The tarjih (preference) is based on the need for certainty in applying qisas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the blow is with the back of the iron and no wound, Sahibayn would enforce qisas, while the sounder view imposes diya. The muftā bihī (operative position) is the latter, requiring a wound.
This impacts the punishment applied in a real case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن ضرب رجلا بمر فقتله فان اصابه بالحديد قتل به وان اصابه بالعود فعليه الدية. قال وهذا اذا اصابه بحدا لحديد لوجود الجرح فكمل السبب وان اصابه بظهر الحديد فعندهما يجب وهو رواية عن ابي حنيفة اعتبار منه للالة وهو الحديد وعنه انما يجب اذا جرح وهو الاصح على ما نبينه ان شاء الله تعالى. وعلى هذا الضرب بسنّة الميزان.
He said: Whoever strikes a man with a spade and kills him, if he hits him with the iron, he is killed (qisas) for it; if he hits him with the wood, then diya is due. He said: This is when he hits him with the edge of the iron because of the presence of a wound, thus the cause is complete. And if he hits him with the back of the iron, according to them (Sahibayn) qisas is obligatory, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa that he considers the instrument which is the iron, and from him (another narration) that it is only obligatory if a wound occurs, and this is the sounder opinion as we will explain insha'Allah. And similarly striking with the weight of the scale.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage begins with the ruling of Imam Muhammad on killing with a spade: if the blow lands with the iron part and causes a wound, qisas is due because the cause (the iron instrument) is complete. If it lands with the wooden handle, only diya is due. The author then clarifies that the condition for qisas is the existence of a wound (jarh) from the iron's edge. When the blow is with the back of the iron (the blunt side), the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold qisas obligatory because the instrument is iron, which is inherently lethal. However, there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: one agrees with the Sahibayn, considering the instrument; the other requires a wound for qisas. The author indicates that the latter (requiring wound) is the sounder opinion (al-asahh). This ruling is extended by analogy to striking with a scale weight—if the weight is iron and causes a wound, the same principles apply.

Key Terms
حديد (hadid): Iron part of a spade; if blow causes wound, qisas is due
عود (‘ud): Wooden handle of a spade; blow leads to diya only
جرح (jarh): Wound that completes the cause for qisas
ظهر الحديد (zahr al-hadid): Back of the iron (blunt side); dispute on qisas
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional killing
دية (diya): Blood money paid for killing not subject to qisas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school requires a wound for qisas, even when the instrument is iron, ensuring certainty in applying retaliation.

Hitting with a Large Stick or Whip: Classification and Dispute
Classification of large stick as heavy object with Hanafi ikhtilaf; whip as light object with Shafi'i ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Hanafi and Shafi'i classifications of killing with a heavy object versus a whip, and state the corresponding legal consequences (qisas vs. diya).

Core Idea
The classification of the instrument (heavy vs light) determines whether the killing is 'amd or shibh 'amd, affecting the penalty.

This passage examines two analogies for a spade's handle: it is either like a large stick (heavy object) or like a whip (light object). Each analogy leads to different rulings within the Hanafi school and between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. Understanding this classification is critical for determining whether qisas or diya applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two analogies
The text presents two views: one comparing the instrument to a large stick (heavy), the other to a whip (light). Recognize that these analogies determine further legal analysis.
The term 'muthaqqal' (heavy object) is key.
2
Recall the Hanafi internal ikhtilaf for heavy objects
For killing with a heavy object, Abu Hanifa holds it is shibh 'amd (diya + kaffarah), while the Sahibayn hold it is 'amd (qisas). This difference was explained earlier.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Identify the cross-madhhab dispute for the whip
For the whip analogy, the Hanafi school considers it shibh 'amd (diya), while Imam al-Shafi‘i considers it 'amd (qisas). Note the thamarah al-khilaf.
The text does not provide a Hanafi response; it merely notes the difference.
4
Consider the issue of muwalah
The passage ends by mentioning 'mas'ala al-muwalah', possibly referring to cumulative blows or repeated striking. This may affect the classification or penalty.
The exact meaning is unclear; it may indicate a separate technical issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قيل هو بمنزلة العصا الكبيرة فيكون قتلا بالمثقل وفيه خلاف ابي حنيفة على مانبين وقيل هو بمنزلة السوط وفيه خلاف الشافعى وهى مسألة الموالاة.
Then it is said: it is like a large stick, so it is killing with a heavy object (muthaqqal), and in it is the difference of Abu Hanifa as we have explained. And it is said: it is like a whip, and in it is the difference of al-Shafi‘i, and it is the issue of al-muwalah (?)
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage discusses the classification of the instrument used in a killing. Some scholars analogize the spade's handle (or the spade itself) to a large stick (casa kabira), which is considered a heavy object (muthaqqal). When death results from a heavy object, the Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa considers it shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional) requiring diya and kaffarah, while the Sahibayn consider it 'amd (intentional) requiring qisas. This difference was explained earlier in the text. Then another view analogizes it to a whip (sawt), which is a light object. According to Imam al-Shafi‘i, killing with a whip is considered intentional ('amd) and requires qisas, while the Hanafi school considers it shibh 'amd requiring only diya. The issue is related to 'mas'ala al-muwalah' which may refer to the principle of cumulative blows or repeated striking.

Key Terms
عصا كبيرة (‘asa kabira): Large stick; classified as heavy object (muthaqqal)
مثقل (muthaqqal): Heavy object used to kill; ruling depends on classification
سوط (sawt): Whip; classified as light object
موالات (muwalah): Possibly 'cumulative blows' or 'repeated striking'; a technical issue

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The classification of the instrument as heavy or light is decisive in determining whether the killing is intentional or quasi-intentional, leading to either qisas or diya.

Killing with a Wooden Stick: Diya Only
Ruling on killing with a wooden stick - diya wajib, no qisas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for killing with a wooden stick and explain why qisas is not applicable while diya is wajib.

Core Idea
Killing with a wooden stick is quasi-intentional, warranting diya not qisas.

This passage addresses a specific homicide scenario: striking with a wooden stick. In Hanafi law, the type of weapon crucially distinguishes between intentional ('amd) and quasi-intentional (shibh al-'amd) killing. When the instrument is blunt like a stick, qisas is not imposed; instead, diya (blood money) is obligatory to ensure the victim's blood is not wasted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Read the passage and note that the act is striking another person with a wooden stick (al-'ud) causing death. This is not a typical murder weapon like a sword.
The instrument is a blunt, heavy object, not a sharp iron weapon.
2
State the explicit ruling
The text clearly says 'diya is obligatory' (tajib al-diyah). This is the direct ruling.
No other penalty (qisas, ta'zir) is mentioned.
3
Analyze the reasoning provided
Two reasons are given: (1) the victim is a protected soul (nafs ma'sumah) whose life has been taken, so blood cannot go unpunished; (2) qisas is prevented (imtina' al-qisas) due to the nature of the act.
The prevention of qisas implies the act is not classified as intentional murder ('amd).
4
Classify the homicide type
Under Hanafi fiqh, killing with a blunt wooden instrument falls under shibh al-'amd (quasi-intentional). This category carries diya, not qisas.
Shibh al-'amd is defined by the use of an instrument not commonly used for killing (e.g., a stick, stone, or fist) combined with intent to harm but not necessarily to kill.
5
Apply the principle to ensure blood is not wasted
The phrase 'so that blood is not wasted' (hatta la yuhdar al-dam) underscores that the life taken must be compensated. Diya fulfills this even when qisas is not appropriate.
This reflects the Shari'ah's goal of protecting life (hifz al-nafs).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما اذا ضربه بالعود فائماتجب الدية لوجود قتل النفس المعصومة وامتناع القصاص حتى لا يهدر الدم
And as for when he strikes him with a wooden stick [al-'ud], then blood-money (diya) is obligatory due to the existence of killing an inviolable soul and the prevention of qisas, so that the blood is not wasted.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling: if a person is killed by striking with a wooden stick (such as a staff or phawara handle), qisas is not obligatory because this is not considered intentional murder ('amd) under Hanafi law. However, the life of the victim (nafs ma'sumah) has been taken, so to prevent the blood from being shed in vain, diya (blood money) is wajib. The ruling is based on the classification of such a weapon as a muthqal (heavy object) or something other than an iron weapon, which falls under shibh al-'amd (quasi-intentional) where diya is the penalty.

Key Terms
العود (al-'ud): A wooden stick or staff, not an iron weapon, used as a striking instrument.
النفس المعصومة (al-nafs al-ma'sumah): An inviolable soul, i.e., a person whose life is protected under Islamic law (Muslim or dhimmi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the killer intended to kill
B) Because qisas is prevented and a protected soul was killed
C) Because the wooden stick is considered a deadly weapon
D) Because the victim was not a Muslim

Key Takeaway
Killing with a wooden stick is shibh al-'amd, so the penalty is diya, not qisas, to compensate the protected life.

Drowning and Qisas: Hanafi vs Sahibayn and Shafi'i
Dispute over qisas for murder by drowning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes between murder by drowning and murder by sword, and articulate the three positions (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, al-Shafi'i) with their proofs.

Core Idea
Murder by drowning is shibh al-amd in Hanafi law because water is not a typical weapon, so only diyah is wajib, not qisas.

In this lesson, we examine a classic intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute concerning the punishment for murder by drowning. While the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that qisas (retaliatory execution) is obligatory, Imam Abu Hanifa rules that only diyah (blood money) is due. We will follow the reasoning of each side, focusing on the Hanafi argument that water is not a prepared instrument for killing, creating a shubhah that reduces the crime from 'amd to shibh al-amd.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position of Abu Hanifa
Identify Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling: drowning does not warrant qisas; only diyah is wajib. Note that the act falls under shibh al-amd (semi-intentional) due to the instrument not being prepared for killing.
The key distinction is between 'amd and shibh al-amd.
2
Identify the opposing views
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that qisas is wajib but by sword, not drowning. Imam al-Shafi'i also holds qisas is wajib but by drowning in kind.
Al-Shafi'i's method differs from Sahibayn.
3
Analyze the opponents' proof
They cite the hadith 'Whoever drowns, we drown him' (Ibn Majah) and argue that water is a killing agent, so its use indicates intentionality ('amdiyyah). Also, the victim's blood is inviolable (ma'sum).
This is a straightforward dalil naqli (textual evidence).
4
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal
Abu Hanifa responds: the hadith is not marfu' (authentically raised to the Prophet) or is a matter of siyasah (state policy). Water is ghayr mu'addah (not prepared for killing), creating doubt (shubhah) about full intent. Qisas requires exact likeness (mumathalah), which is absent between drowning and execution. Also, the purpose of deterrence (zajr) is not achieved because drowning is rare.
The Hanafi response uses both textual criticism and legal theory (shubhah, mumathalah, maqasid).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Hanafi (mufta bihi), the killer pays diyah on the 'aqilah and possibly expiation. Under Sahibayn/Al-Shafi'i, the killer is executed (by sword for Sahibayn, by drowning for al-Shafi'i).
This shows how legal theory affects real-world sentencing.

وجہ ہے کہ امام صاحب نے بڑے دبا پتھر سے مارنے کی صورت میں قصاص واجب نہیں کیا بلکہ دیت کو واجب کیا ہے بہر حال ان دونوں میں تماثل نہیں ہے حالانکہ مماثلت ہونی ضروری ہے کیونکہ قصاص کے معنی خود مماثلت کئے ہیں اسی وجہ سے مشتق کر کے اقص اثر ہ بولتے ہیں جب کہ کوئی کسی کے نقش قدم پر چلے اور اس سے مشتق کر کے قیچی کے دونوں پھلوں کے لئے مقصہ بولتے ہیں اور جرح اور دق (پتھر سے پھوڑنا) کے درمیان بھی تماثل نہیں ہے کیونکہ دق میں ظاہر کو خراب کرنا کم ہے تو جرح اور غرق کے درمیان بھی بدرجہ اولی کوئی مماثلت نہ ہوگی۔ نیز قصاص کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ زجر حاصل ہو اور یہ مقصد وہاں علی سبیل الکمال حاصل ہو گا جب کہ اس آلہ سے قتل کا عام رواج ہو اور جس سے قتل کا عام رواج نہیں ہے وہاں یہ حکمت زجر بھی حاصل نہ ہوگی اور صورت حال یہ ہے کہ تلوار اور ہتھیار سے قتل غالب اور بھاری چیز سے یا تفریق سے قتل نادر ہے تو یہاں قصاص واجب ہونے سے حکمت زجر بھی غیر متماثل ہے۔ فریق مخالف کی مستدل حدیث کا جواب و ما رواه غیر مرفوع او هو محمول على السياسة وقد او مئت اليه اضافته الى نفسه فيه واذا امتنع القصاص وجبت الدية وهى على العاقلة وقد ذكرناه واختلاف الروايتين في الكفارة
He said: Whoever drowns a child or an adult in the sea, there is no qisas according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Qisas is taken from him, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i, except that according to the two it is by severing the neck, and according to him (al-Shafi'i) he is drowned, as we explained before. Their evidence is the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Whoever drowns, we drown him.' And because the instrument (the sea water) is a killer, so its use is a sign of intentionality, and there is no doubt about the inviolability of blood. Commentary: If a person drowns a child or an adult in the sea, what is the ruling? Imam Abu Hanifa says diyah is obligatory and no qisas. The Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i say qisas is obligatory. Then there is disagreement on the manner of qisas: Sahibayn say beheading, al-Shafi'i says drowning. They (Shafi'i and Sahibayn) adduce the hadith 'Whoever drowns, we drown him' (Ibn Majah). Al-Shafi'i's argument is apparent from it. The Sahibayn say the hadith shows qisas is taken, but the method is known from the previous hadith 'No qisas except with the sword'. Also, the drowning person chose a lethal means (drowning), and the use of a killing instrument indicates intent and premeditation, and the victim is inviolable blood without doubt, so qisas is obligatory. The proof of Imam A'zam (Abu Hanifa): He has the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Beware! The victim of shibh al-amd (semi-intentional) is the victim of the whip and the stick, and for it and every accidental killing there is diyah (arsh).' And because the instrument (water) is not prepared for killing nor commonly used for it, due to difficulty of use, so doubt about lack of intentionality arises. And because qisas indicates likeness (mumathalah); from it comes 'iqtassa atharah' (he followed his footsteps), and from it 'al-miqassah' (scissors for the two blades). There is no likeness (tamathul) between wounding (jarh) and crushing (daqq) because the latter is deficient in destroying the external. Likewise, they are not alike in the wisdom of deterrence, because killing with a weapon is common, while with a heavy object is rare. Commentary: This is the proof of Abu Hanifa. The gist: Water is not an instrument of killing, so its ruling is like that of the whip and stick where diyah is obligatory, because the hadith says: 'Every shibh amd and every accidental killing has diyah.' Also, water is not a usual instrument of killing, so doubt about intent arises, and doubt drops qisas. Moreover, if qisas were applied, there would be no likeness between drowning and the punishment, because drowning does not destroy the external appearance while execution by sword does. This lack of likeness is like between wounding and crushing. Also, the purpose of deterrence is not achieved since drowning is rare. Response to the opposing hadith: That narration is not marfu' (raised to the Prophet), or it is interpreted as a discretionary policy (siyasah); and the addition 'to himself' indicates that. When qisas is prevented, diyah is obligatory, and it is upon the 'aqilah (agnatic group), as we mentioned; and there are two narrations concerning the kaffarah (expiation).
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute concerning murder by drowning. The core issue is whether qisas (retaliatory execution) applies when the killer drowns the victim. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that qisas is not applicable; rather, diyah (blood money) is obligatory. His students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) along with Imam al-Shafi'i hold that qisas is applicable. However, they differ on the method: the Sahibayn say beheading like other qisas cases, while al-Shafi'i says the killer should be drowned in kind, based on a hadith 'Whoever drowns, we drown him.' The Hanafi response is twofold: first, the hadith cited is not authentically marfu' (raised to the Prophet) or is interpreted as a matter of state policy (siyasah shar'iyyah) rather than a fixed legal ruling. Second, and more fundamentally, Abu Hanifa argues that water is not an instrument prepared for killing (ghayr mu'addah li al-qatl). Unlike a sword, which is designed for killing, water is not typically used as a weapon. Therefore, the act falls under shibh al-amd (semi-intentional homicide), which requires diyah, not qisas. The supporting hadith is: 'The victim of shibh al-amd is the victim of the whip and stick, and there is diyah in it and in every mistake.' Also, qisas requires exact likeness (mumathalah) between the crime and punishment, which is impossible between drowning (which does not physically harm the body's exterior) and execution (which does). The purpose of qisas (zajr, deterrence) is also not achieved because drowning is rare, while sword killing is common. Thus, the Hanafi position is that diyah is obligatory on the 'aqilah (the killer's agnatic group), and the killer also must observe kaffarah (expiation), with two narrations regarding its obligation.

Key Terms
شبه عمد (shibh al-amd): Homicide where the killer intended the act but used an instrument not likely to kill (like whip or stick), falling between intentional ('amd) and accidental (khata').
دية (diyah): Blood money; a fixed financial compensation paid to the heirs of the victim in cases of homicide that do not warrant qisas.
قصاص (qisas): Retributive punishment of the killer by death in the same manner as the killing, subject to strict conditions of likeness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa rule that no qisas is required for drowning, while the Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i rule that qisas is required?
A) Because the victim was not ma'sum al-dam (inviolable).
B) Because water is not a prepared instrument for killing (ghayr mu'addah), creating doubt about full intentionality (shubhah).
C) Because the killer did not intend to kill.
D) Because drowning is a form of accidental killing.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, drowning is classified as shibh al-amd, so qisas is not applicable; only diyah is wajib, due to the instrument not being mu'addah (prepared for killing).

Killing by Drowning: Qisas or Diyah?
Abu Hanifa's proof that drowning requires diyah, not qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that drowning requires diyah not qisas, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact similitude; drowning creates doubt, so only diyah is due.

This passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's argument that killing by drowning does not warrant qisas because water is not a customary weapon, creating doubt about intent. The Hanafi school distinguishes between typical and atypical killing methods, and when qisas is prevented, diyah becomes obligatory on the 'aqila. We will also examine the Shafi'i proof and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the contested ruling: does killing by drowning require qisas (retaliation) or diyah (blood money)?
The dispute is between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Analyze Abu Hanifa's dalil: qisas requires mumathala (similitude), which is absent in drowning. Also, water is not a customary weapon, so doubt about intentionality arises, and doubt drops qisas.
Qiyas: drowning is like killing with a whip or stick, for which the Prophet (peace be upon him) prescribed only diyah.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Look at the hadith they cite: the Prophet (peace be upon him) executed by drowning (qisas for drowning).
The hadith: 'Gharaqnahu' (we drowned him).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafis rebut the hadith: it is either not marfu' (not from the Prophet) or it is a matter of siyasah (policy), not a fixed legislative ruling.
The attribution of drowning to himself indicates it was a specific policy decision.
5
Apply the rule
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) and the mufta bihi position: diyah is due on the 'aqila; qisas is not applicable.
There is a secondary dispute on kaffarah: two narrations from Abu Hanifa.

و ما رواه غیر مرفوع او هو محمول على السياسة وقد او مئت اليه اضافته الى نفسه فيه واذا امتنع القصاص وجبت الدية وهى على العاقلة وقد ذكرناه واختلاف الروايتين في الكفارة

Book of Homicides. Every accidental killing has diyah, because water is not an instrument for killing and is not used for killing due to difficulty of its use, so doubt of non-intentionality arises. And because qisas requires similitude... Response to the opponent's hadith: what they narrated is not marfu' or is carried on policy, and when qisas is prevented, diyah becomes obligatory, and it is on the 'aqila, and we have mentioned it, and there are two narrations regarding kaffarah.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents Abu Hanifa's argument that killing by drowning does not warrant qisas (retaliation) but only diyah (blood money). The reasoning is that water is not a typical weapon for killing, and its use creates doubt about intent. Qisas requires exact similitude, which is absent because drowning causes death without visible external damage, while qisas would require inflicting visible harm. This is like the case of beating with a whip or stick, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) established only diyah. The opposing school (al-Shafi'i) cites a hadith, but the Hanafi response clarifies that the hadith is either not marfu' (attributed to the Prophet) or is interpreted as a matter of policy (siyasah), not as a fixed ruling. When qisas is prevented, diyah becomes due on the 'aqila (the offender's clan). Regarding kaffarah (expiation), there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: one says no kaffarah, the other (transmitted by al-Tahawi) says kaffarah is wajib.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide or injury, replacing qisas when qisas is not applicable
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional homicide or injury, requiring exact similitude
عاقلة ('aqila): The clan or group responsible for paying diyah on behalf of the killer in accidental killings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is qisas not applicable in killing by drowning?
A) Drowning is always accidental
B) There is no intent to kill
C) Qisas requires exact similitude, which is absent
D) The Prophet forbade qisas for drowning

Key Takeaway
When qisas is prevented due to lack of similitude, diyah becomes wajib on the 'aqila.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for Death After Intentional Wound
Al-Quduri's ruling on qisas when a wound causes death after a period.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for qisas when a wound leads to death after a period and apply the rule that the apparent causal link suffices.

Core Idea
Qisas is due for death caused by an intentional wound as long as no other apparent cause intervenes.

The passage from al-Quduri addresses a critical nuance: what if the victim dies after a prolonged period from the injury? Some might think the delay breaks the chain of causation. However, the Hanafi position is clear: as long as the wound remains the only apparent cause, the offender is liable for qisas. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The intentional wound that leads to death. What is the ruling? Qisas is obligatory.
2
Locate the cause (sabab)
Identify the legal cause of death: the intentional wound. The passage states 'due to the presence of the cause'.
3
Determine the condition
What condition must be satisfied? The absence of anything that invalidates the ruling in the apparent sense. No other apparent cause of death.
4
Understand the attribution
Why is death attributed to the wound? Because the wound is the apparent cause and nothing else is visibly intervening. Thus, death is attributed to the wound.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Consider a scenario where the victim also had a pre-existing disease. Would the ruling change? Yes, because the disease would be an apparent intervening cause.

قال ومن جرح رجلا عمدا فلم يزل صاحب فراش حتى مات فعليه القصاص لوجود السبب وعدم ما يبطل حكمه في الظاهر فاضيف اليه

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور عمداً کسی شخص کو زخمی کر دیا وہ برابر صاحب فراش بر ہا یہاں تک کہ وہ مر گیا تو اس پر قصاص واجب ہو گا سبب موت کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور اس چیز کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے جو ظاہر میں سبب کے حکم کو باطل کر دے پس حکم کی اضافت سبب کی جانب ہوگی۔

تشریح زید نے خالد کو زخمی کر دیا اور اس زخم کی وجہ سے خالد ایک ماہ مثلاً صاحب فراش رہ کر مر گیا تو زید سے قصاص لیا جائے گا کیونکہ زیدی کے زخم کی وجہ سے وہ مر گیا جو بھی باطل نہیں ہوا تھا لہذا موت کی اضافت زخم لگانے کی طرف ہوگی۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever intentionally wounds a man, and he (the victim) remains bedridden until he dies, then upon him is qisas due to the presence of the cause and the absence of anything that invalidates its ruling in the apparent, so it is attributed to him.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar presents a ruling: if someone intentionally wounds another, and the victim remains bedridden due to that wound and eventually dies, then qisas is obligatory on the offender. The reasoning: the wound is the legal cause (sabab) of death, and there is no intervening factor (like another wound or disease) that would break the chain of causation in the apparent sense. Therefore, death is attributed to the wound. The commentary gives an example: Zayd wounds Khalid, Khalid remains bedridden for a month, then dies. Since there is no other apparent cause, Zayd is subject to qisas.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause that leads to death, in this case the intentional wound
صاحب فراش (sahib firash): One who is confined to bed due to injury or illness

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key condition for qisas to be due on the one who wounds, according to this passage?
A) The victim must die immediately
B) The wound must be the only apparent cause of death
C) The wound must be inflicted with a weapon
D) The victim must not have any pre-existing illness

Key Takeaway
For qisas to apply, the wound must be the sole apparent cause of death; any intervening factor breaks the chain.

No Qisas for Mistaken Killing in Battle
Ruling on mistaken killing in battle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Muslim who kills another Muslim mistakenly in battle, identifying the applicable legal consequences (no qisas, wajib kaffarah and diyah) and citing the Quranic proof from Surah al-Nisa' 4:92.

Core Idea
Mistaken killing in battle: no qisas, only kaffarah and diyah.

In the chaos of battle, a Muslim warrior may tragically strike a fellow believer, thinking he is an enemy. How does Islamic law address this? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling based on the explicit Quranic verse for accidental killing, clarifying that qisas (retaliation) is not applicable, while kaffarah (expiation) and diyah (blood money) become wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a Muslim killing another Muslim in battle, mistakenly believing the victim to be a polytheist. The ruling: no qisas is due, but kaffarah and diyah are wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse (Surah al-Nisa' 4:92) is cited as proof: it prescribes kaffarah and diyah for mistaken killing, and does not mention qisas.
The verse is quoted in the Arabic text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse explicitly requires kaffarah and diyah in cases of khata', and by omission of qisas, it indicates that qisas is not a consequence for this type of killing.
Dalalah: the absence of qisas in the verse shows it is not applicable.
4
Confirm the scope of khata'
The passage explains that this is a type of error (khata' fi al-qasd – error in intention). In Hanafi fiqh, both types of khata' (in action and in intention) do not incur qisas.
Thus, the ruling is consistent with the general principle for accidental killing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا التقى الصفان من المسلمين والمشركين فقتل مسلم مسلما ظن انه مشرک فلا قود عليه وعليه الكفارة لان هذا احد نو عى الخطأ على ما بيناه والخطأ نوعيه لا يوجب القود ويوجب الكفارة وكذالدية على ما نطق به نص الكتاب

ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جب مسلمانوں اور مشرکین کی دونوں صفوں کی مٹھ بھیٹر ہوگئی پس مسلمان کسی مسلمان کو مشرک سمجھ کر قتل کر دیا تو اس پر قصاص نہیں ہے اور اس پر کفارہ ہے اس لئے کہ یہ خطا کی دونوٹس میں سے ایک ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ اور خطاء اپنی دونوں کے ساتھ قصاص کو واجب نہیں کرتا اور کفارہ اور دیت کو واجب کرتا جیسا کہ نص کتاب ناطق ہے۔ تشریح مسلمانوں اور مشرکین کی صف بندی منتشر ہو کر لڑائی ہو گئی کسی مسلمان نے کسی کو مشرک سمجھ کر قتل کر دیا حالانکہ وہ مقتول مسلمان ہے تو قاتل پر قصاص نہیں صرف کفارہ اور دیت ہے کیونکہ یہ خطاء فی القصد ہے اور جو بھی قسم ہو قتل خطاء میں قصاص نہیں ہوتا بلکہ دیت اور کفارہ واجب ہوا کرتا ہے فرمانِ باری سے یہی ثابت ہے ارشاد ہے۔ ومن قتل مؤمنا فتحرير رقبة وديه مسلمة الى اهله
He (Muhammad) said: And when the two lines of Muslims and polytheists meet, and a Muslim kills a Muslim thinking he is a polytheist, then there is no qisas upon him, and upon him is kaffarah, because this is one of the two types of error as we have explained, and error in its two types does not necessitate qisas and necessitates kaffarah, and similarly diyah as the text of the Book states. Commentary: The lines became mixed, a Muslim kills another thinking he is a polytheist, then no qisas, only kaffarah and diyah, because this is error in intention (khata' fi al-qasd). The Quranic verse: 'And whoever kills a believer... then the emancipation of a slave and diyah delivered to his family.'
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani deals with a scenario in battle: when Muslim and polytheist lines engage, and a Muslim kills another Muslim mistakenly thinking he is a polytheist, there is no qisas (retaliation). Instead, the killer must pay kaffarah (expiation) and diyah (blood money). The reasoning: this falls under 'khata' fi al-qasd' (error in intention), which is a type of accidental killing. The ruling is based on the Quranic verse (Surah al-Nisa' 4:92): 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake, then (the atonement is) the freeing of a believing slave and diyah delivered to his family.' Therefore, no qisas, but kaffarah and diyah are wajib.

Key Terms
خطأ (khata'): Error, either in action (e.g., shooting at an unintended target) or in intention (thinking the victim is someone else)
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for accidental killing, which is freeing a believing slave (or fasting two months if unable)
قود (qawd): Qisas, retaliation, specifically in the context of homicide

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a Muslim who kills another Muslim in battle, mistakenly thinking he is a polytheist?
A) Qisas is due because killing a Muslim is always intentional
B) No qisas, but kaffarah and diyah are due
C) Only diyah is due, no kaffarah
D) The killer is exempt from all liability due to battlefield conditions

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, mistaken killing of a Muslim in battle falls under khata' and incurs kaffarah and diyah, not qisas, based on Quran 4:92.

Kaffarah When Qisas is Not Established: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on a hadith and two narrations on kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa on kaffarah and identify the proof-based refutation of the opposing school's hadith.

Core Idea
Kaffarah in accidental killing is disputed within the Hanafi school; Imam Abu Hanifa has two narrations.

This passage explores a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi madhhab regarding the obligation of kaffarah when qisas cannot be applied. The commentator first addresses a hadith cited by the opposing school, arguing its weakness or political interpretation. Then, he highlights that Imam Abu Hanifa himself has two narrations on the matter, reflecting a difference in ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
Determine the exact fiqh question: is kaffarah wajib when qisas is not established?
2
Analyze the opposing school's evidence
Examine the hadith about drowning (gharraqtahu) that is often cited to show kaffarah is wajib.
3
Examine the Hanafi critique
The commentator argues the hadith is not marfu' (not from the Prophet) but from Ziyad, or it is a political action (siyasah), not a legal ruling.
This is a key methodological point: distinguishing legal rulings from political acts.
4
Trace the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa has two narrations: one says kaffarah is not wajib, another (via Tahawi) says it is wajib.
The dispute originates from the grammatical interpretation of 'fi al-kaffarah'.
5
Determine the grammatical basis
The phrase 'fi al-kaffarah' can be read as 'mubtada' and 'khabar' or as a prepositional phrase, leading to different rulings.
Advanced: this shows how usul al-nahw impacts fiqh.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدانید جلد - ۱۵ ہیں اور دو روایتوں کا اختلاف ہے کفارہ کے اندر ۔

كتاب الجنايات
تشریح رہی وہ حدیث جو فریق مخالف کا مستدل ہے تو وہ حدیث مرفوع نہیں بلکہ زیاد کا کلام ہے ”فلا يصح به استدلال“ یا یہ حدیث سیاست پر محمول ہے جس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے تفریق کی اضافت اپنی جانب فرماتے ہوئے غرقتناہ فرمایا ہے بہر حال جب قصاص نہ ہو سکا تو دیت واجب ہو گی اور دیت عاقلہ پر واجب ہوگی امام صاحب کے نزدیک دیت تو بلائنڈ واجب ہے باقی رہا کفارہ تو اس میں امام صاحب کی دوروایتیں ہیں ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ کفارہ واجب نہیں اور امام طحاوی کی روایت یہ ہے کہ کفارہ واجب ہے واختلاف مبتداء ہے اور فی الکفارہ اس کی خبر ہے۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Badanid Jild 15. There are two narrations differing in the matter of kaffarah. 57 Kitab al-Jinayat. Commentary: The hadith that the opposing party uses as evidence is not marfu' but rather the speech of Ziyad, 'so it cannot be used as evidence'. Or this hadith is interpreted as political (siyasah), the proof of which is that the Holy Prophet (peace be upon him) said, attributing separation to himself, 'We drowned him'. In any case, when qisas could not be established, diyah becomes obligatory, and diyah is wajib upon the 'aqilah. According to Imam, diyah is definitely wajib. As for kaffarah, Imam has two narrations: one narration is that kaffarah is not wajib, and the narration of Imam Tahawi is that kaffarah is wajib. The dispute is about the beginning (mubtada') and the news (khabar) in the word 'fi al-kaffarah'.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of kaffarah (expiation) in a case where qisas (retaliation) could not be carried out. The commentator first addresses a hadith cited by the opposing school (likely Shafi'i), arguing that it is not a marfu' hadith (attributed to the Prophet) but rather the statement of Ziyad, and thus not valid evidence. Alternatively, it is interpreted as a political ruling (siyasah) rather than a legal one. The conclusion is that diyah (blood money) is due, and it is paid by the 'aqilah (tribal group). Then the dispute within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Hanifa has two narrations on whether kaffarah is obligatory. One narration says no kaffarah, another (via Imam Tahawi) says it is wajib. The dispute is over the grammatical interpretation of the phrase 'fi al-kaffarah', whether 'mubtada' and 'khabar' or 'fi' as a preposition.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation required for accidental killing, including freeing a slave or fasting.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the victim's family for homicide.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the status of kaffarah in the case where qisas is not established, according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Kaffarah is definitely wajib
B) Kaffarah is not wajib
C) There are two narrations: one says wajib, the other not
D) Kaffarah is haram

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa has two narrations on kaffarah when qisas is not established, reflecting the nuanced nature of ijtihad within the Hanafi school.

Qisas — Retaliation

General Principles of Qisas for Injuries Less Than Murder
Establishes the rule that qisas applies where exact recompense is possible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of mumathalah for qisas and apply it to common injuries such as cutting a limb at a joint or loss of sight.

Core Idea
Qisas applies only where exact equivalence (mumathalah) is possible; otherwise diyah.

This lesson explores the Hanafi rulings on qisas for injuries that do not result in death. The central principle is that qisas is obligatory when the injury can be exactly replicated on the offender (mumathalah). Where exact equivalence is impossible, the offender must pay blood money (diyah). Through examples of hand/limb amputation, eye gouging, loss of sight, and tooth-breaking, the passage clarifies the scope of qisas under Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine what specific injury is being discussed and what the Hanafi ruling is (qisas or diyah).
The act may be intentional cutting, gouging, or blinding.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 'And wounds are qisas' (5:45) is the primary evidence. Identify how it supports the ruling.
The verse implies mumathalah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the phrase 'qisas' necessitates equivalence. For each case, check if exact replication is possible in nature, location, and degree.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The method for loss of sight (heated mirror) may be contested by other schools. Note the opposing view and the Hanafi response.
The Hanafis rely on Companion practice as ijma suquti.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The preferred position (mufta bihi) is that qisas is wajib wherever mumathalah is possible, based on the Quran and Companion practice.
This is the established madhhab position.

نیز گھر والے کے لئے جائز تھا کہ وہ پہلے ہی اس کو تل کر دیتا جب کہ وہ گھر میں گھسا تھا تو مال لینے کیلئے بعد میں قتل کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ اس صورت میں ہے جب دھمکی وغیرہ سے مال نہ مل سکے اور اگر مل سکے تو پھر قتل مضمون ہوگا۔
بَابُ القصاص فيما دُونَ النفس
ترجمہ یہ باب نفس سے کم میں قصاص کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح . اب تک مصنف قصاص فی النفس کو بیان کر رہے تھے اب قصاص فی الطرف کو بیان فرماتے ہیں۔ القصاص فیما دون النفس میں اصول کلی ، کن صورتوں میں قصاص ہوتا ہے اور کن میں نہیں
قال ومن قطع يد غيره عمدا من المفصل قطعت يده وان كانت يده اكبر من اليد المقطوعة لقوله تعالى والجروح قصاص وهو ينبئى عن المماثلة فكل ما امكن رعايتها فيه يجب فيه القصاص وما لا فلا وقد امكن في القطع من المفصل فاعتبر ولا معتبر بكبر اليد وصغرها لان منفعة اليد لا تختلف بذلک و کذا لک الرجل ومادون الانف والاذن لا مكان رعاية المماثلة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے عمدا اپنے غیر کا ہاتھ جوڑ سے کاٹ لیا تو اس کا ہا تھ کا ٹا جائے گا اگر چہ اس کا ہاتھ کاٹے ہوئے ہاتھ سے بڑا ہو اللہ کے فرمان والجروح قصاص کی وجہ سے ( زخموں کا بدلہ ان کے برابر ہے ) اور قصاص مماثلت کی خبر دیتا ہے۔ پس ہر وہ زخم جس میں مماثلت کی رعایت ممکن ہو تو اس میں قصاص واجب ہوگا۔ اور جہاں نہیں پس نہیں ۔ اور جوڑ سے ہاتھ کاٹنے میں مماثلت کی رعایت ممکن ہے تو قصاص معتبر ہوا اور ہاتھ کے چھوٹے اور بڑے ہونے کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ ہاتھ کی منفعت اس کی وجہ سے مختلف نہیں ہوگی اور ایسے ہی پیر اور ناک کا نرم حصہ اور کان مماثلت کی رعایت سے ممکن
ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے دوسرے کا کوئی عضو کا ٹا تو بعض صورتوں میں قصاص ہوتا ہے اور بعض میں نہیں تو اس کا اصول کلی یہ ہے کہ جس صورت میں مماثلت ہو سکتی ہے۔ وہاں قصاص ہو گا جہاں مماثلت متعد ریا ناممکن ہو وہاں قصاص نہ ہو گا بلکہ دیت واجب ہو گی تفصیل اس اجمال کی یہ ہے کہ جب ہاتھ یا پیر جوڑ کے اوپر سے کاٹا ہو و مماثلت ممکن ہوگی یعنی گئے سے کاٹا ہو یا کہنی سے یا پیر ٹخنہ سے یا گھٹنے سے تو دوسرے کا بھی اتنا ہی کاٹا جا سکتا ہے اسی طرح کان میں مماثلت کی رعایت ہو سکتی ہے اور ناک کے نرم حصہ میں بھی مماثلت ہوسکتی ہے
لہذا ان میں قصاص ہو گا۔ کیونکہ قرآن کا فیصلہ ہے و الجروح قصاص زخموں کا بدلہ برابر ہے۔ ہاتھ کا کام پکڑنا ہے لہذا اگر ہاتھ کے چھوٹا ، بڑا ہونے کی وجہ سے ہاتھ کی منفعت میں کوئی خلل نہیں ہوتا تو اس کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا تو اگر انا ہاتھ
بڑا چھوٹا اور کاٹنے والے کا بڑا ہو پھر بھی قصاص واجب ہوگا۔
اور جہاں مماثلت کی رعایت نہ ہو سکے جیسے کلائی کے نصف سے باتھ کاٹا ہو یا پنڈلی کے نصف سے کا نا ہو تو یہاں مماثلت کی رعایت
ممکن نہیں ہے لہذا قصاص نہ ہو گا۔

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۵۷
جن میں مماثلت ممکن ہو وہاں قصاص ہے اس کے برعکس میں نہیں ، آنکھ نکالنے میں قصاص نہیں
عنهم
قال ومن ضرب عين رجل فقلعها لا قصاص عليه لا متناع المماثلة فى القلع وان كانت قائمة فذهب ضوؤها فعليه القصاص لا مكان المماثلة على ما قال فى الكتاب تحمى له المرأة ويجعل على وجهه قطن رطب وتقابل عينه بالمراة فيذهب ضووها وهو ما ثور عن جماعة من الصحابة رضى الله ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی کی آنکھ پر مارا پس اس کو باہر نکال دیا تو اس پر قصاص نہ ہوگا باہر نکالنے میں مماثلت کے ممتنع ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر آنکھ موجود ہو۔ پس اس کی بینائی ختم ہوگئی تو اس پر قصاص ہو گا ۔ مماثلت کے ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو قدوری نے مختصر القدوری میں کہا ہے کہ اس کے لئے آئینہ گرم کیا جائے اور اس کے چہرے پر گیلی روٹی رکھ دی
جائے اور اس کی آنکھ کے سامنے آئینہ کیا جائے تو اس کی بینائی ختم ہو جائے گی اور یہ صحابہ کی ایک جماعت سے منقول ہے۔ تشریح ماقبل میں قاعدہ گذر چکا کہ جہاں مماثلت ممکن ہوگی وہاں قصاص ہوگا اور جہاں مما ملت ممکن نہ ہوگی تو وہاں قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ لہذا اگر زید نے بکر کی آنکھ پر مارا جس کی وجہ سے بکر کا دیدہ نکل کر باہر آ گیا تو چونکہ یہاں مماثلت ممکن نہیں اس لئے قصاص نہ ہوگا۔
اور اگر آنکھ موجود ہے فقط اس کی بینائی ختم ہوگئی ہے تو یہاں مماثلت ممکن ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ جونی آنکھ سے قصاص نہیں لینا اس کو باندھ دیا جائے اور چہرہ پر بھیگی ہوئی روٹی لپیٹ دیجائے اور گرم صاف لوہا اس کی اس آنکھ کے سامنے کیا جائے جس کی بینائی ختم کرنی ہے اس طریقہ سے بینائی ختم ہو جائے گی اور چہرہ اور دوسری آنکھ کو کوئی نقصان نہیں پہنچے گا ۔ حضرت عثمان کے زمانہ میں یہ واقعہ پیش آیا تھا تو حضرت عثمان نے صحابہ سے مشورہ کیا تو حضرت علی نے یہ مشورہ دیا تھا اور تمام صحابہ نے اس پر سکوت اختیار فرمایا تھا۔
دانت توڑنے میں قصاص واجب ہے
وفى السن القصاص لقوله تعالى والسن بالسن وان كان من يقتص عنه اكبر من سن الاخر لان منفعة السن لا تتفاوت بالصغر والكبر قال وفي كل شجة تتحقق فيها المماثلة القصاص لما تلوناه ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور دانت میں قصاص ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان " وَالسّنُ بِالسن “ کی وجہ سے اگر چہ اس شخص کا دانت جس سے قصاص لیا جا رہا ہے دوسرے کے دانت سے بڑا ہو اس لئے کہ دانت کی منفعت چھوٹائی اور بڑائی سے متفاوت نہیں ہوتی۔ قدوری نے فرمایا اور ہر ایسا زخم جس میں مماثلت متحقق ہو سکے قصاص ہے اس آیت کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم تلاوت کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے کسی کا دانت توڑ دیا تو اس میں قصاص ہو گا قرآن میں صاف حکم موجود ہے وَالسَنُ بِالسن " کہ دانت کے بدلہ میں دانت ہے اگر چہ ایک کا دانت چھوٹا اور دوسرے کا بڑا ہو ۔ کیونکہ اس اختلاف سے دانتوں کی منفعت میں کچھ تفاوت نہ ہو گا۔
اور و الجروح قصاص سے یہ بات ثابت ہو چکی ہے کہ جس زخم میں مماثلت ممکن ہو اس میں قصاص لیا جائے گا۔
Book of Injuries. Also, it was permissible for the homeowner to kill him earlier when he entered the house; so killing later to take the wealth is also permissible. But this is when wealth cannot be obtained through threats etc.; if it can be obtained, then killing is condemned. Chapter of Qisas for Less Than Life. Translation: This chapter is about qisas for less than life. Commentary: The author has been discussing qisas for life; now he discusses qisas for limbs. In qisas for less than life, a general principle: in which cases qisas is due and in which not. He said: Whoever cuts off another's hand at the joint intentionally, his hand shall be cut off, even if his own hand is larger than the cut hand, due to the saying of Allah 'And wounds are qisas,' and it indicates similarity. So whenever it is possible to observe similarity, qisas is obligatory; where not, no. And it is possible in cutting at the joint, so it is considered; and size of the hand is not considered because the benefit of the hand does not differ by that. Likewise for the foot, the soft part of the nose, and the ear, due to possibility of observing similarity. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Whoever cuts another's hand at the joint intentionally, his hand shall be cut off even if his hand is larger than the cut hand, because of Allah's command 'and wounds are qisas' (and recompense of wounds is equal), and qisas indicates similarity. So every wound in which similarity can be observed, qisas is obligatory; where not, then not. And in cutting at the joint, similarity is possible, so qisas is considered, and the hand being large or small is not considered because the benefit of the hand does not differ by that. Similarly for the foot, the soft part of the nose, and the ear due to possibility of similarity. Commentary: If someone cuts another's limb, in some cases qisas is due, in others not. The general principle is: where similarity is possible, qisas applies; where similarity is impossible or not possible, qisas does not apply but diyah is due. Details: when hand or foot is cut above the joint, similarity is possible—i.e., if cut at the wrist, elbow, ankle, or knee, then the other's can be cut similarly. Similarly for the ear, similarity can be observed, and for the soft part of the nose, so qisas applies. Because the Quran's decree is 'and wounds are qisas' (recompense equal). The function of the hand is grasping, so if size does not affect the benefit, it is not considered; so even if one hand is larger and the other's is smaller, qisas is still obligatory. And where similarity cannot be observed—e.g., cutting half the forearm or half the shin—then qisas does not apply. In cases where similarity is possible, qisas; otherwise not. No qisas for gouging out an eye. He said: Whoever strikes a man's eye and gouges it out, there is no qisas because similarity is impossible in gouging. But if the eye remains and its sight is lost, then there is qisas because similarity is possible. As the book says: A mirror is heated for him, moist cotton is placed on his face, and the mirror is placed before his eye, so its sight goes. This is transmitted from a group of Companions. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Whoever strikes someone's eye and knocks it out, there is no qisas because similarity in knocking out is impossible. But if the eye remains and its light goes, then qisas applies because similarity is possible, according to the detail mentioned in al-Mukhtasar: A mirror is heated for him, moist cotton is placed on his face, and the mirror is placed before his eye, so its light goes. This is narrated from a group of Companions. Commentary: The rule has passed that where similarity is possible, qisas applies; where impossible, qisas is not obligatory. So if Zaid hits Bakr's eye and his eyeball comes out, since similarity is impossible, no qisas. But if the eye remains and only its sight is lost, similarity is possible: the culprit is bound, wet bread/cloth is wrapped on his face, and a hot clean iron is placed before his eye to destroy its sight, without harming the face or other eye. This incident occurred in the time of Uthman; he consulted the Companions, and Ali gave this advice, and all Companions remained silent (in approval). Qisas is obligatory for breaking teeth. And for teeth, qisas is due because of Allah's saying 'and the tooth for the tooth,' even if the tooth of the one from whom qisas is taken is larger than the other's tooth, because the benefit of a tooth does not differ by smallness or largeness. He said: In every wound in which similarity is realized, there is qisas, due to the verse we recited. Translation: Al-Quduri said: For teeth, qisas is due because of Allah's command 'and the tooth for the tooth,' even if the tooth of the person from whom qisas is taken is larger, because the benefit of the tooth does not vary by smallness or largeness. He said: In every wound where similarity is realized, there is qisas because of the verse we recited. Commentary: If someone breaks another's tooth, qisas applies. The Quran clearly commands 'the tooth for the tooth,' even if one's tooth is smaller and the other's larger, because this difference does not affect the benefit of teeth. And from 'and wounds are qisas' it is established that in every wound where similarity is possible, qisas is taken.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on Al-Hidayah, expounding the chapter on qisas for injuries less than murder. The author explains the general principle: qisas (retributive justice) is obligatory wherever exact equivalence (mumathalah) between the injury inflicted and the retaliatory injury can be achieved; where equivalence is impossible, only diyah (blood money) is due. The principle is derived from the Qur'anic verse 'And wounds are qisas' (Al-Ma'idah 5:45), which mandates equivalence. The commentary then applies this principle to specific body parts.

For cutting of a limb at a joint (e.g., hand at wrist, foot at ankle), qisas is obligatory because a similar cut can be made at the corresponding joint of the offender. The size of the hand (large or small) does not matter, as the function (manfa'ah) of the hand—grasping—remains unaffected by size. This is a Hanafi position; size is irrelevant to the prescribed qisas.

For gouging out an eye, qisas is not applicable because it is impossible to exactly replicate the act of removal without risking greater harm or death. However, if the eye remains but its sight is lost, qisas is possible through a specific method: the offender's eyes are bound, a wet cloth is placed over the face, and a heated mirror or iron is held before the targeted eye to destroy its vision without injuring the face or other eye. This method is attributed to a practice of the Companions, notably used in the time of Caliph 'Uthman with consultation of 'Ali and silence of others, indicating consensus.

For teeth, qisas is obligatory based on the explicit Qur'anic ruling 'the tooth for the tooth' (Al-Ma'idah 5:45). Even if one tooth is larger than the other, the benefit of teeth (biting, chewing) does not differ, so equivalence is possible.

The passage thus systematically presents the Hanafi ruling on qisas for wounds, emphasizing the condition of exact equivalence and providing practical examples where it applies or does not.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retributive punishment by inflicting equivalent injury on the offender.
مماثلة (mumathalah): Exact similarity or equivalence between the original injury and the retaliatory injury.
دية (diyah): Blood money compensation paid when qisas is not possible.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit or function of a body part; if the function remains same despite size difference, qisas applies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is the ruling for qisas when a person intentionally cuts off another's hand at the wrist joint?
A) Qisas is not valid because the hands may differ in size.
B) Qisas is obligatory because exact equivalence is possible at the joint and size does not affect function.
C) Only diyah is obligatory because cutting at the joint is not specified in the Quran.
D) Qisas is valid only if the offender's hand is smaller.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school makes qisas obligatory only when exact equivalence (mumathalah) is possible, emphasizing function over form.
