Qisas for Eye Injuries: The Principle of Mumasala
Ruling with proof on qisas for eye injuries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for eye injuries and apply the condition of mumasala to determine whether qisas or diyah applies.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact equivalence; for enucleation it's impossible, for vision loss it's possible.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar draws a sharp distinction between two types of eye injury: enucleation (removal of the eyeball) and loss of vision while the eye remains intact. The ruling hinges on the principle of mumasala (exact equivalence), which is a fundamental condition for qisas in the Hanafi school. We will explore why the former cannot be retaliated exactly, while the latter can, and examine the method endorsed by the Companions for exact retaliation of vision loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage presents two scenarios: enucleation (qal') and loss of vision (dhahab al-daw') with the eye intact. Note the different outcomes.
Focus on the condition that triggers the difference: possibility of exact equivalence.
2
Understand the condition of mumasala
Qisas is only wajib when exact equivalence is possible. Enucleation cannot be replicated exactly because the manner of extraction varies; vision loss can be replicated by a controlled method that destroys vision without harming the eye structure.
This condition is derived from the Quranic command of 'eye for eye' but interpreted through practicality.
3
Examine the Companions' method
The text describes heating an iron, placing moist cotton or bread on the face, and facing the iron toward the eye to destroy vision. This was the practice of the Companions in the time of Uthman, with Ali's advice and silent approval of others.
This ijma sukuti (silent consensus) provides the evidentiary basis for the ruling.
4
Apply the ruling to hypothetical cases
Given a scenario, decide whether qisas or diyah applies based on whether exact equivalence is possible. For enucleation, no qisas; for vision loss, qisas is wajib.
Remember: the method for vision loss is only for retaliation, not for initial punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی کی آنکھ پر مارا پس اس کو باہر نکال دیا تو اس پر قصاص نہ ہوگا باہر نکالنے میں مماثلت کے ممتنع ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر آنکھ موجود ہو۔ پس اس کی بینائی ختم ہوگئی تو اس پر قصاص ہو گا ۔ مماثلت کے ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو قدوری نے مختصر القدوری میں کہا ہے کہ اس کے لئے آئینہ گرم کیا جائے اور اس کے چہرے پر گیلی روٹی رکھ دی جائے اور اس کی آنکھ کے سامنے آئینہ کیا جائے تو اس کی بینائی ختم ہو جائے گی اور یہ صحابہ کی ایک جماعت سے منقول ہے۔ تشریح ماقبل میں قاعدہ گذر چکا کہ جہاں مماثلت ممکن ہوگی وہاں قصاص ہوگا اور جہاں مماثلت ممکن نہ ہوگی تو وہاں قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ لہذا اگر زید نے بکر کی آنکھ پر مارا جس کی وجہ سے بکر کا دیدہ نکل کر باہر آ گیا تو چونکہ یہاں مماثلت ممکن نہیں اس لئے قصاص نہ ہوگا۔
اور اگر آنکھ موجود ہے فقط اس کی بینائی ختم ہوگئی ہے تو یہاں مماثلت ممکن ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ جس آنکھ سے قصاص نہیں لینا اس کو باندھ دیا جائے اور چہرہ پر بھیگی ہوئی روٹی لپیٹ دیجائے اور گرم صاف لوہا اس کی اس آنکھ کے سامنے کیا جائے جس کی بینائی ختم کرنی ہے اس طریقہ سے بینائی ختم ہو جائے گی اور چہرہ اور دوسری آنکھ کو کوئی نقصان نہیں پہنچے گا ۔ حضرت عثمان کے زمانہ میں یہ واقعہ پیش آیا تھا تو حضرت عثمان نے صحابہ سے مشورہ کیا تو حضرت علی نے یہ مشورہ دیا تھا اور تمام صحابہ نے اس پر سکوت اختیار فرمایا تھا۔
He said: Whoever strikes a man's eye and knocks it out, there is no qisas upon him due to the impossibility of equivalence in extraction. If it remains but its light (vision) goes, then qisas is required due to the possibility of equivalence, as stated in the book: an iron is heated for him, moist cotton is placed on his face, and his eye is faced with the iron, so its light goes. This is reported from a group of Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And whoever strikes someone's eye and it is knocked out, there is no qisas on him because of the impossibility of equivalence in extraction. If the eye remains but its vision is lost, then qisas is required because of the possibility of equivalence, according to the detail mentioned by Quduri in Mukhtasar al-Quduri: an iron is heated for him, moist bread is placed on his face, and the iron is faced before his eye, so his vision is lost. This is transmitted from a group of Companions. Explanation: The rule has passed previously that wherever equivalence is possible, qisas is required; wherever equivalence is not possible, qisas is not obligatory. So if Zaid struck Bakr's eye causing it to be knocked out, since equivalence is not possible, qisas is not due. And if the eye remains but only its vision is lost, then equivalence is possible, and that is: the eye from which qisas is not taken is tied, moist bread is wrapped on the face, and a clean hot iron is placed before the eye whose vision is to be destroyed; by this method the vision is destroyed and the face and other eye suffer no harm. This incident occurred in the time of Uthman; Uthman consulted the Companions, and Ali gave this advice, and all the Companions remained silent (in approval).
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on qisas for eye injuries. It begins by stating the general rule: qisas requires exact equivalence. In the case of eye removal, qisas is not possible because you cannot replicate the extraction identically— you cannot take out the offender's eye in exactly the same manner without risk. However, if the eye remains but vision is lost, qisas can be carried out by a method reported from the Companions: the offender is made to face a heated iron or mirror that destroys vision without damaging the eye itself. This method ensures equivalence. The text also mentions that this procedure was approved by the Companions in the time of Uthman, with Ali's advice. Thus, this ruling is based on the principle of mumasala (equivalence) and is supported by the silent consensus (ijma sukuti) of the Companions.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for bodily injury, requiring exact equivalence in kind.
مماثلة (mumasala): Exact equivalence in the nature and extent of injury, required for qisas.
قلع (qal'): Extraction or removal of the eye from its socket.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the passage, why is qisas not wajib for knocking out someone's eye?
A) Because the eye is not a limb for which qisas is prescribed
B) Because exact equivalence in extraction is impossible
C) Because the victim must request diyah instead
D) Because the offender can claim self-defense

Key Takeaway
Qisas for eye injuries hinges on the possibility of exact equivalence: enucleation precludes qisas, but loss of vision can be exactly retaliated using a method established by the Companions.

Tooth: Qisas Wajib Even if Sizes Differ
Ruling on qisas for teeth based on Quranic verse and principle of mumasala

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for teeth and explain why size differences do not affect the obligation, citing the Quranic dalil and the principle of manfa'ah.

Core Idea
Qisas for teeth is wajib regardless of size because the essential benefit (manfa'ah) is identical.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical objection to qisas for teeth: what if the offender's tooth is larger than the victim's? The Hanafi school affirms that qisas remains wajib, using the Quranic verse 'And the tooth for the tooth' as the primary proof, and clarifying that equality is based on function, not physical dimensions. The discussion also restates the broader principle that any wound where mumasala (equivalence) is possible qualifies for qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is breaking another's tooth; the ruling is that qisas (retaliatory extraction) is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the Quranic verse 5:45 'And the tooth for the tooth' (wa al-sinna bi al-sinn).
This is a qat'i thubut and qat'i dalala text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit command 'tooth for tooth' indicates qisas is legislated. The Hanafi school holds that the imperative implies obligation (wujub).
4
Note the objection and its resolution
The objection: if the offender's tooth is larger, qisas may seem disproportionate. Resolution: the benefit (manfa'ah) of a tooth does not differ by size; therefore functional equality is achieved.
Manfa'ah includes chewing, speech, etc.
5
Extract the general principle
The text extends the ruling: any wound where mumasala (equivalence in benefit and location) is realized, qisas is wajib.
This is derived from the same verse and the principle applied to teeth.

Source Text

وفى السن القصاص لقوله تعالى والسن بالسن وان كان من يقتص عنه اكبر من سن الاخر لان منفعة السن لا تتفاوت بالصغر والكبر قال وفي كل شجة تتحقق فيها المماثلة القصاص لما تلوناه

In the tooth, there is qisas due to the saying of Allah: 'And the tooth for the tooth' — even if the one from whom qisas is taken has a larger tooth than the other, because the benefit of the tooth does not differ by smallness or bigness. He said: And in every wound in which mumasala is realized, qisas is wajib due to what we have recited. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And in the tooth, qisas is wajib due to the command of Allah 'And the tooth for the tooth', even if the tooth of the person from whom qisas is taken is larger than the other's tooth, because the benefit of the tooth does not differ by smallness or bigness. Al-Quduri said: And every wound in which mumasala can be realized, qisas is wajib due to this verse that we have recited. Explanation: If someone breaks another's tooth, qisas is wajib. The Quran clearly commands 'and the tooth for the tooth', even if one tooth is smaller and the other larger, because the benefit of teeth does not differ by this variation. And from the verse 'and wounds for qisas', it is established that any wound in which mumasala is possible, qisas will be taken.

Commentary
This passage establishes qisas for tooth injuries. The primary dalil is the Quranic verse quoting the Law of Moses: 'And the tooth for the tooth' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:45), which is part of the law of equality in retribution. The text addresses an objection: if the offender's tooth is larger, can qisas still be exacted? The Hanafi ruling says yes, because the benefit (manfa'ah) of a tooth does not differ by size. Both small and large teeth serve the same function. Therefore, equivalence is achieved even if sizes differ. The passage also restates the general principle: any wound where mumasala is possible triggers qisas, as derived from the same verse.

Key Terms
سن (sinn): Tooth; the object of qisas in this ruling.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory justice; exacting a similar injury upon the offender.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit or utility; the functional purpose of a body part.
مماثلة (mumasala): Equivalence; the condition for qisas that the injury can be exactly reciprocated in benefit and location.

Bone: No Qisas Except for Tooth
Ruling that qisas is not applicable to bones other than teeth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for bones and explain the reasoning based on the impossibility of exact equivalence (mumasala).

Core Idea
Qisas is only for teeth; for other bones, exact equivalence is impossible, so diyah applies.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling in Islamic criminal law: the applicability of qisas (retaliatory punishment) for injuries to bones. While qisas is generally prescribed for intentional injuries, the Hanafi school holds that it applies only to teeth, not to other bones. This is based on a prophetic hadith and the practical difficulty of achieving exact equivalence (mumasala) in bone injuries. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the law of retribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is inflicting intentional injury on a bone (excluding tooth). The ruling: qisas is not applicable; instead, diyah (blood money) is due.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of the Prophet: 'La qisas fi al-'azm' (No qisas in bone), supported by statements from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit negation indicates that qisas is not legislated for bones. The rationale is that exact equivalence is impossible due to variations in bone healing and growth.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage does not mention any intra-Hanafi disagreement; this is the established Hanafi position and appears to be agreed upon across schools.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The ruling is mufta bihi and relied upon; the proof is strong and the reasoning sound.

اور ہڈی سے مراد دانت کا غیر ہے اور اصول وہی ہے جو مذکور ہو چکا ہے کہ جہاں مماثلت ممکن ہو وہاں قصاص ہو گا ورنہ نہیں ہوگا، اور ہڈی میں مماثلت نہیں ہو سکتی، البتہ دانت میں مماثلت ہو سکتی ہے کیونکہ ہڈی میں کمی بیشی ، زیادتی اور نقصان کا احتمال ہے اور یہ احتمال دانت میں نہیں اس لئے کہ دانت کو سوہان سے رگڑ کر اول کے برابر کیا جاسکتا ہے اور اگر اول کا پورا دانت اکھاڑا ہو تو دوسرے کا بھی پورا دانت اکھاڑا جا سکتا ہے۔
He said: And there is no qisas in bone except in the tooth. This wording is narrated from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with them. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'No qisas in bone.' And by bone is meant other than the tooth. Because considering mumasala in other than the tooth is impossible due to the possibility of increase and decrease, unlike the tooth because it can be filed with a file. And if it is pulled out from its root, the second (tooth) is pulled out similarly so that both become equivalent. Translation: And there is no qisas in bone except in the tooth. This wording is narrated from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. And the Prophet said: No qisas in bone. By bone is meant other than the tooth. And because the consideration of mumasala in other than the tooth is difficult due to the possibility of increase and decrease, unlike the tooth because it can be filed with a file. And if he pulls out the tooth from its root, the second tooth is also pulled out from its root, so both become equivalent. Explanation: In any bone except tooth, qisas will not be taken. The author says that the text 'No qisas in bone except in the tooth' is transmitted from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. Also in hadith: 'No qisas in bone.' And by bone is meant other than tooth. The rule is as mentioned: wherever mumasala is possible, qisas is due; otherwise not. And in bone, mumasala is not possible, but in tooth it is possible because bone is susceptible to variation - excess and deficit - while tooth is not because it can be filed to match. And if the first tooth was completely pulled out, the second can also be completely pulled out.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage clarifies that qisas is not applicable to bones (except teeth). The proof includes a hadith and statements of the sahaba (Umar and Ibn Mas'ud). The reasoning is based on the principle of mumasala: bones are irregular in shape and healing; if you break a bone, it cannot be replicated exactly because of possible differences in healing, thicker/thinner, etc. In contrast, a tooth can be filed or extracted identically, ensuring exact equivalence. Thus, for bone injuries, diyah (blood money) applies instead of qisas. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and is grounded in textual evidence and rational analogy.

Key Terms
عظم ('azm): Bone, excluding teeth.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not apply qisas to bones (except teeth) because exact physical equivalence is practically impossible; diyah is the alternative.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
No Qisas in Bones Except Teeth
Ruling with proof from hadith and analogy for teeth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for bones, identify the hadith evidence, and explain the rationale based on similitude.

Core Idea
Qisas is not applied to bones except teeth because exact similitude is impossible for other bones.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from the chapter of qisas. The Hanafi school restricts retaliation to only teeth among bones, citing a prophetic tradition and a rational argument about equality. Understanding this ruling clarifies the boundaries of physical retribution in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: inflicting injury on a bone. The ruling is that qisas (retaliation) is not permissible for bones except the tooth.
Focus on the exception 'except the tooth'.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The author cites a hadith: 'La qisas fi al-azm' (no qisas in a bone), transmitted from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud, and attributed to the Prophet.
This is a textual proof (dalil naqli).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication of meaning)
The negation 'la' indicates absence of ruling; 'al-azm' includes all bones. The exception 'except the tooth' is derived from the rational argument that follows.
The exception is not explicit in the hadith but is justified by the reason of possible equality.
4
Understand the rational argument (talil)
For bones other than teeth, exact similitude is impossible because healing may cause irregular increase or decrease. Teeth, however, can be filed down or extracted entirely, allowing exact matching.
This is an application of the principle that qisas requires precise equivalence (mumathala).
5
Note the consequence
The practical effect: for injuries to teeth, qisas may be applied tooth-for-tooth; for all other bones, only diya (blood money) or arsh (fixed compensation) is due.
This distinguishes Hanafi position from schools that apply qisas more broadly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا قصاص فى عظم الا فى السن وهذا اللفظ مروى عن عمر رضی الله عنه وابن مسعود رضى الله عنه وقال عليه السلام لا قصاص فى العظم والمراد غير السن ولان اعتبار المماثلة فى غير السن متعذر لاحتمال الزيادة والنقصان بخلاف السن لا نه يبرد بالمبرد و لو قلع من اصله يقلع الثاني فيما ثلان

And because considering similitude in other than the tooth is difficult due to possibility of increase and decrease, unlike the tooth because it is filed with a file, and if pulled from its root, the second is also pulled, so they become similar.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school establishing that qisas (retaliation) is not applied for breaking any bone except the tooth. The author cites the hadith 'La qisas fi al-'azm' transmitted from 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. The reasoning: for bones other than teeth, exact similitude is impossible because healing may cause irregularity, making equal retaliation uncertain. Teeth, however, can be filed down to match or fully extracted tooth for tooth, ensuring equality. Thus qisas is specific to teeth among bones.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for injury or killing
عظم (azm): Bone

Qisas — Retaliation

No Qisas Between Different Categories for Injury
Inter-madhhab dispute on qisas for wounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qisas for wounds below the soul between parties of different gender or status and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the property analogy.

Core Idea
Limbs are property, not souls – value equality is required for qisas, not just physical similarity.

This passage addresses a key ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding qisas (retaliation) for injuries below the level of death. The Hanafi school denies qisas between parties of different gender or status (man/woman, free/slave), while the Shafi'i school generally permits it, analogizing limbs to souls. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi school's treatment of limbs as property-like, requiring exact monetary equivalence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the three cases where the Hanafi school denies qisas for wounds below the soul: between man and woman, between free and slave, and between two slaves. Note the exception: a free person cutting a slave's limb (no qisas) – but the passage says 'except in the case of a free person cutting the limb of a slave' (that is also against qisas). Actually the text says contrary to Shafi'i in all that except... meaning the exception is that Shafi'i agrees with Hanafi in that case? Let's read carefully: 'contrary to al-Shafi'i in all that except in the case of a free person cutting the limb of a slave.' So Shafi'i also denies qisas in that one case. So the Hanafi position is: no qisas in all three categories, and Shafi'i agrees on the free-cutting-slave case.
The passage lists three denials: man/woman, free/slave, slave/slave. The exception is a free person cutting a slave's limb – Shafi'i also denies qisas here.
2
Identify the opposing school and their argument
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that limbs are subsidiary to souls. Since qisas applies equally in homicide regardless of gender or status (a man killing a woman, a free person killing a slave), it should also apply to limbs. This is an analogy (qiyas) from souls to limbs.
Shafi'i's dalil is based on the subsidiary nature of limbs.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school rejects this analogy. Their proof: limbs are treated like property (amwal) in the Shari'ah. For qisas on property, exact value equality is required. The Shari'ah has fixed different values for limbs: e.g., a man's finger is valued at 500 dinars, a woman's at 250. Thus, a man and woman are not equal in limb value, so qisas is impossible.
The Hanafi argument is based on the valuation fixed by revelation (takhmin al-shar').
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i analogy
The Hanafi school provides two distinctions: (1) Limbs are treated as property, so value matters; souls have no monetary value – all lives are equal. (2) Differences in physical strength (which might exist between a man and a woman) have no fixed measure, so they are ignored; but value differences are precisely known, so they are considered. This refutes the Shafi'i analogy.
The Hanafi response uses the property analogy to distinguish limbs from souls.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, in Hanafi law, if a man cuts off a woman's finger, he must pay full diyah (500 dinars) but no qisas. In Shafi'i law, qisas would apply unless the victim is a slave and the offender free. So the difference affects the actual punishment: retaliation vs. blood money.
The practical consequence is whether the offender's limb is cut (qisas) or he pays compensation (diyah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا قصاص بين الرجل والمراة فيما دون النفس ولا بين الحر والعبد ولا بين العبدين خلافا للشافعي في جميع ذلك الا في الحر يقطع طرف العبد و يعتبرا لاطراف بالانفس لكونها تابعة لهما ولنا ان الاطراف يسلك بها مسلک الاموال فينعدم التماثل بالتفاوت فى القيمة و هو معلوم قطعا بتقويم الشرع فامكن اعتباره بخلاف التفاوت في البطش لانه لا ضابط له فاعتبر اصله و بخلاف الا نفس لان المتلف ازهاق الروح ولا تفاوت فيه
And there is no qisas between man and woman for what is below the soul, nor between free and slave, nor between two slaves, contrary to al-Shafi'i in all that except in the case of a free person cutting the limb of a slave. And they (al-Shafi'i) analogize limbs to souls because limbs are subsidiary to them. Our (Hanafi) evidence is that limbs are treated like property, so equality is negated by difference in value, and that is definitively known by the valuation of the Shari'ah, so it can be considered, unlike difference in physical strength because there is no measure for it, so its origin is considered, and unlike souls because the destroyer extinguishes life and there is no difference in it.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding qisas (retaliation) for injuries below the level of death (ma dun al-nafs). The Hanafi position denies qisas between a man and woman, between a free person and a slave, and between two slaves. Al-Shafi'i generally allows qisas in all these cases, except when a free person cuts the limb of a slave (where he too denies qisas). The Shafi'i reasoning is that limbs are subsidiary to the soul, and since qisas applies equally in homicide regardless of gender or status, it should also apply to limbs. The Hanafi response: limbs are treated like property (amwal) in terms of compensation, and thus exact equivalence (tamathul) requires equal monetary value. Since a man's finger is valued at 500 dinars and a woman's at 250, they are not equal, so qisas is not possible. Differences in physical strength have no fixed measure, so they are disregarded (the origin of strength is present in both). Souls, by contrast, have no variation in value—all lives are equal—so qisas in homicide applies across categories. This ruling underscores the Hanafi principle that qisas for limbs requires identical value, not just identical body parts.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for injury or killing
تماثل (tamathul): Equality between parties required for qisas; here referring to equal value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because slaves are not worthy of qisas.
B) Because the value of a free person's limb is higher than a slave's, preventing equality.
C) Because qisas is only for intentional injuries.
D) Because the Shari'ah does not allow retaliation between free and slave.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, qisas for limbs requires equal monetary value, not just physical similarity, so it is denied between parties of different gender or status.

Equality of Diyat Required for Qisas in Limbs
Ruling on qisas in limbs based on diyat equality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on qisas in limbs between a man and a woman and between a Muslim and a dhimmi, and explain why diyat equality determines the applicability of qisas.

Core Idea
For qisas in limbs, only equal diyat values permit retaliation; differing values shift the remedy to monetary compensation.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, two critical distinctions are drawn regarding qisas (retaliatory justice) for bodily limbs. The Hanafi school applies the principle of mumathala (exact equivalence) strictly: when Shariah has fixed the same diyat (compensation) for a particular limb for two classes of people, qisas is wajib; when the diyat values differ, qisas is replaced by diyat. This lesson explores the rulings for man-woman and Muslim-dhimmi cases, grounding the legal reasoning in the fixed values set by revelation.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The Hanafi rule: qisas in limbs requires equality of diyat values (mumathala).
This is the foundational principle from the text.
2
Identify the two cases
The passage addresses: (1) man vs. woman, (2) Muslim vs. dhimmi.
Each case is treated differently based on diyat values.
3
Recall the diyat values fixed by Shariah
Man's hand diyat is higher than woman's; Muslim's hand diyat equals dhimmi's.
These values are not assumed but explicitly set by Shariah.
4
Apply the rule
Since man-woman values differ, qisas is not applied (only diyat). Since Muslim-dhimmi values are equal, qisas is wajib.
The application follows directly from the equality condition.

فرمایا تو اس تفاوت کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا اور مرد اور عورت کے ہاتھ میں تفاوت کا شریعت نے اعتبار کر کے اس کی الگ الگ قیمت متعین فرمادی ہے اس لئے وہ تفاوت معتبر ہو گیا ہے۔ اور جان کو ضائع کرنے میں یہ تفاوت بھی معتبر نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بہر صورت روح کو تلف کرنے والا ہے اور روح میں کوئی تفاوت نہیں ہے لہذا قصاص واجب ہوگا۔ مسلم اور ذمی کے درمیان قصاص واجب ہے القصاص فى الاطراف بين المسلم والكافر للتساوى بينهما في الارش ترجمہ اور مسلمان اور کافر کے درمیان اطراف میں قصاص واجب ہے ان دونوں کے درمیان ارش میں برابری کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح یہاں کافر سے مراد ذمی ہے مسلمان اور ذمی کے ہاتھ کی قیمت شریعت نے ایک رکھی ہے، لہذا مساوات کی وجہ سے قصاص واجب ہوگا کیونکہ قصاص مماثلت کو چاہتا ہے اور مماثلت موجود ہے۔
He said: this difference will not be considered. And the difference between the hand of a man and a woman, the Shariah has considered it and fixed separate prices for them, so that difference has become valid. And in destroying a life, this difference is also not considered. Because in any case, it destroys the soul, and there is no difference in souls, therefore qisas is obligatory. Qisas in limbs is obligatory between a Muslim and a dhimmi due to equality between them in arsh. Translation: Qisas in limbs is obligatory between a Muslim and a disbeliever because of equality in arsh. Explanation: Here disbeliever means dhimmi. The value of the hand of a Muslim and a dhimmi is fixed as one by the Shariah, therefore due to equality qisas is obligatory, because qisas requires similarity and similarity exists.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses two rulings on qisas in limbs. First, it clarifies that the difference in diyat values between a man's and a woman's hand is considered by Shariah (man's hand diyat is higher), so qisas is not applicable between them for limbs because equality (mumathala) is lacking. However, for life, there is no such disparity, so qisas is wajib. Second, it establishes that qisas in limbs is wajib between a Muslim and a dhimmi because Shariah has set the same diyat for both for limbs (e.g., hand), ensuring equality. The underlying principle is that qisas requires exact reciprocity; when equality of value is present, qisas applies; when it is absent, only diyat applies.

Key Terms
ارش (arsh): Compensatory payment for loss of a limb, as opposed to diya (full blood money).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment involving exact reciprocity for bodily harm.
مماثلت (mumathala): Exact similarity or equality between the injury and the retaliation.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen living under the protection of the Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the dhimmi is considered equal to a Muslim in all respects.
B) Because the diyat value of a limb is the same for a Muslim and a dhimmi, but differs between a man and a woman.
C) Because qisas is only for life, not for limbs.
D) Because the woman's guardian must agree.

Key Takeaway
Qisas in limbs is wajib only when the diyat values of the limb are exactly equal; when they differ, only monetary compensation (arsh) is required.

Qisas — Retaliation

No Qisas for Cutting Half Forearm or Jaifah Wound if Victim Recovers
Ruling on impossibility of mumathala leading to no qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios where qisas is not applied due to impossibility of mumathala and explain the reasoning for each.

Core Idea
If exact reciprocity (mumathala) is impossible, qisas is waived and diyat applies.

The Hanafi school holds that qisas for bodily injuries requires precise equality between the injury and the retaliation. This lesson examines two specific scenarios from Quduri's matn where such equality cannot be ensured: cutting half the forearm (involving bone) and a penetrating wound (jaifah) that heals despite being usually fatal. Even if the victim recovers fully, qisas is not applied because the condition of mumathala cannot be met.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text mentions two distinct cases where qisas is not due: (1) cutting the hand from half the forearm, (2) inflicting a jaifah wound that later heals. Identify them from the matn.
Both involve recovery, but the reasoning differs.
2
Understand the condition of mumathala
Qisas requires exact similarity (mumathala) between the injury and the retaliation. This is a Shari'ah condition derived from the principle of equality in retaliation.
If mumathala is impossible, qisas cannot be applied.
3
Analyze the impossibility in each case
For the forearm: it involves breaking bone, which has no fixed measure to ensure precise reciprocation. For the jaifah wound: recovery is rare, so one cannot guarantee the same outcome for the perpetrator; thus mumathala is impossible.
The reason differs: the first is due to the nature of bone, the second due to rarity of recovery.
4
Conclude the ruling
Since mumathala is impossible in both cases, qisas is not applied. Instead, the perpetrator is liable for diyat (blood money). The tanbih also notes an exception: if the victim does not recover and the wound is fatal (sari'), qisas applies.
Always check if the wound is sari' before ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس نے کسی کا نصف کلائی سے ہاتھ کاٹا اور جا ئفہ زخم لگایا پھر زخمی درست ہو گیا اس میں قصاص نہ ہوگا قال ومن قطع يد رجل من نصف الساعدا وجرحه جائفة فبراً منها فلا قصاص عليه لا نه لا يمكن اعتبار المماثلة فيه اذ الأول كسر العظم ولا ضابط فيه وكذا البرء نادر فيفضى الثانى الى الهلاك ظاهرا ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی مرد کا ہاتھ نصف کلائی سے کاٹا یا اس کو جا ئفہ زخم لگا دیا ، پس وہ اس سے اچھا ہو گیا تو اس پر قصاص نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ اس میں مماثلت کا اعتبار ممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اول ( کلائی کا شنا) ہڈی تو ڑنا ہے اور ہڈی میں کوئی ضابطہ مقرر نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی اچھا ہونا نا در ہے تو ثانی ظاہر اہلاکت کی جانب مفضی ہوگا۔ تشریح جائفہ ایسے زخم کو کہتے ہیں جو جوف تک سرایت کر جائے یعنی سر پر مارا اس کا اثر دماغ تک پہو نچاوغیرہ۔ تو یہاں مصنف نے دو مسئلے ذکر کئے ہیں، - اگر کسی نے کسی کی نصف کلائی کاٹ دی تو یہاں قصاص نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں مماثلت کی رعایت ممکن نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ ہڈی کاٹنا ہے جس کا حکم یہی ہے۔ - ایسا زخم لگایا جو اندر تک سرایت کر گیا یعنی جائفہ جس سے عموماً آدمی اچھا نہیں ہوتا مگر وہ ٹھیک ہو گیا تو قصاص نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ تو اچھا ہو گیا اور دوسرے کے بارے میں اغلب گمان یہ ہے کہ وہ اچھا نہ ہو سکے گا تو مماثلت کی رعایت ممکن نہیں ہے۔ تنبیہ اور اگر اؤل اچھا نہ ہوا ہوتو دیکھا جائے کہ زخم ساری ہے یا نہیں اگر ساری ہے تو قصاص ہوگا، ورنہ انتظار کیا جائے گا جب تک حالت منکشف نہ ہو جائے پھر اس کے مطابق عمل کیا جائے گا۔
He said: And whoever cuts the hand of a man from half the forearm or wounds him with a jaifah wound, and he recovers from it, then there is no qisas upon him because it is not possible to consider similarity in it. As for the first, it is breaking bone, and there is no fixed measure for it. And similarly, recovery is rare, so the second leads to destruction apparently. Translation by Quduri: The one whose hand was cut from half the forearm or who was given a jaifah wound and then recovered, there is no qisas for it because similarity cannot be considered. Because the first is breaking bone and there is no fixed rule, and similarly recovery is rare, so the second tends to lead to destruction. Explanation: Jaifah is a wound that penetrates to the body cavity. The author mentioned two issues: if someone cuts half the forearm, no qisas because bone cutting has no fixed measure; if a wound penetrates (jaifah) from which people usually do not recover, but he recovered, then no qisas because the perpetrator's recovery is uncertain. Note: If the first (victim) did not recover, then see whether the wound is fatal (sari'); if fatal, qisas applies; otherwise wait until the outcome is known.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This ruling from Quduri explains two scenarios where qisas is not incumbent. The first is cutting the hand from half the forearm (nisf al-sa'id)—this involves breaking bone, where exact reciprocity cannot be ensured because there is no fixed measure for bone. The second is a jaifah wound (penetrating to the body cavity) that ultimately heals—since such wounds are usually fatal, recovery is rare; thus mumathala is impossible as the perpetrator could not guarantee the same outcome. Therefore, no qisas is applied. The tanbih (note) adds: if the victim does not recover, then if the wound is fatal (sari'), qisas applies; otherwise, one must wait until the outcome is known.

Key Terms
جائفہ (jaifah): A wound that penetrates to the body cavity (jauf), such as a head wound that reaches the brain.
مماثلت (mumathala): Exact similarity between the injury and the retaliation, which is a condition for qisas.
ساعد (sa'id): Forearm; 'nisf al-sa'id' means half the forearm, i.e., cutting from the middle of the forearm towards the wrist.
ساری (sari): A fatal wound that usually leads to death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the injury healed, so the harm is undone.
B) Because cutting half the forearm involves bone, and exact reciprocity cannot be ensured.
C) Because the perpetrator intended only a minor injury.
D) Because the victim forgave.

Key Takeaway
Qisas is waived when exact similarity (mumathala) is impossible, as in bone fractures and generally fatal wounds that happen to heal.

Options for the Victim When the Offender's Hand Is Defective
Ruling on choice between qisas of defective hand and full diyat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the victim's options when the offender's hand is defective and explain the qiyas on fungible items that supports it.

Core Idea
When exact qisas is impossible, the victim may choose: defective qisas or full diyat.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling when a victim's sound hand is cut off by someone whose own hand is defective (paralyzed or missing fingers). The classical text, as explained by Imam Quduri, gives the victim a choice: either take the defective hand in qisas (accepting it as satisfaction) or claim the full diyat. This ruling is derived through qiyas (analogy) on fungible items when the exact replacement is unavailable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the victim's response after his sound hand is cut off by an offender with a defective hand. The ruling: the victim has a choice (khiyar) between qisas on the defective hand or full diyat.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on the impossibility of exact qisas.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas on the case of a fungible item (mithli) that is destroyed and unavailable. In that case, the creditor may accept a defective substitute or claim the price.
The analogy is explicit in the text: 'like a fungible item when it vanishes from people's hands'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The common illa is the inability to obtain an exact equivalent. In qisas, exact reciprocity is impossible because the offender's hand is defective; similarly, when a mithli is unavailable, exact replacement is impossible.
Thus, the victim may either accept the defective hand (like accepting defective item) or claim diyat (like claiming price).
4
Note the subsidiary ruling
If the defective hand falls off or is cut unjustly before the victim chooses, his right to qisas is lost and he does not automatically get diyat because transfer to diyat requires his explicit choice.
Exception: if the hand was cut rightfully (e.g., as qisas for another crime), then diyat is due.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
Some schools may require qisas on the offender's similar limb even if defective. The Hanafi school distinguishes by giving the victim the option to claim diyat, based on the impossibility of exact qisas.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences in judicial rulings.

Source Text

قطع اليد المعيبة ولا شى له غيرها وان شاء اخذ الا رش كاملا لان استيفاء الحق كملا متعذر فله ان يتجوز بدون حقه وله ان يعدل الى العوض كا لمثلى اذا انصرم عن ايدى الناس بعد الاتلاف ثم اذا استوفاها ناقصا فقد ساقط ہو جائے گا، جیسے جب وہ عمدہ کی جگہ ردی سے راضی ہو جائے۔ تشریح زید کا ہاتھ صحیح سالم ہے اور بکر کا ہاتھ شل ہے خشک ہے یا اس کی انگلیاں کم ہیں اور صورت یہ ہوئی کہ بکر نے زید کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا تو اب زید کیا کرے تو اس کو دو اختیار ہیں ۔ 1- اگر زید چاہے تو بکر کا ہاتھ جیسا بھی ہے ویسے ہی سے قصاص لے لے اور اس کو کاٹ دے کیونکہ جب کامل ہا تھ بکر کا ہے ہی نہیں تو اس کے علاوہ چارہ کار نہیں ہے اور اپنے مذکورہ ہاتھ خود بخود گر گیا یا ظلماً کسی نے کاٹ دیا اب کیا ہوگا ولو سقطت المئوفة قبل اختيار المجنى عليه او قطعت ظلماً فلاشيء له عندنا لان حقه متعين في القصاص وانما ينتقل الى المال باختياره فيسقط بفواته بخلاف ما اذا قطعت بحق عليه من قصاص اوسرقه حيث يجب عليه الارش لانه اوفی به حقا مستحقا فصارت سالمة له معنى ترجمہ اور اگر ناقص ہاتھ مجنی علیہ کے اختیار کرنے سے پہلے ساقط ہو گیا یا ظلما کاٹ دیا گیا تو مجنی علیہ کے لئے ہمارے نزدیک کچھ
One's hand is sound and the other's is paralyzed (dry) or missing fingers, so there is a choice between taking qisas and taking diyat. He said: If the hand of the victim is sound and the hand of the cutter is paralyzed or missing fingers, then the victim has a choice: if he wishes, he may cut the defective hand and nothing else is for him; if he wishes, he may take the full arsh. Because obtaining the full right is impossible, so he has the option to compromise with less than his right or to resort to compensation, like a fungible item when it vanishes from people's hands after destruction. Then, if he takes it defective, he has accepted it, so his right falls, just as when he accepts low-quality instead of high-quality. Translation by Quduri: When the cut hand is sound and the cutter's hand is dry or missing fingers, the one whose hand was cut has a choice: he may cut the defective hand and nothing else is for him, or he may take the full diyat. Because complete recovery of the right is impossible. Explanation: Zayd's hand is sound and Bakr's hand is paralyzed. If Bakr cuts Zayd's hand, Zayd has two options: (1) cut Bakr's defective hand, (2) take diyat. The example is like a fungible item that is destroyed and the substitute is not available; the creditor may accept the defective or claim price. If the defective hand falls off before the victim's choice, or is cut unjustly, then there is nothing for him in our school, because his right is fixed to qisas, and it transfers to money only by his choice, so it falls by its loss. Unlike if it is cut rightfully due to qisas or theft, then arsh is due.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rule on qisas when the offender's hand is defective. The victim has two options: either take qisas by cutting the defective hand (and accept it as satisfaction) or claim full diyat. This is analogous to the case where a fungible item (mithli) is destroyed and the substitute is unavailable or defective; the creditor may accept the defective item or claim its price. The text also addresses a subsidiary: if the defective hand falls off before the victim chooses, the victim loses the right to qisas (since the object of qisas is gone) and does not get diyat either, because his right was specifically fixed to qisas, and transfer to diyat occurs only by his choice. However, if the hand was cut as a matter of right (e.g., as qisas for another crime), then arsh is due because it was taken rightfully.

Key Terms
شلاء (shalla'): A hand that is paralyzed, withered, or dried up.
ناقصة الأصابع (naqisat al-asabi'): Missing fingers; a hand with fewer than the normal number of fingers.
مقطوع (maqtu'): The victim whose limb has been cut off.
مثلی (mithli): A fungible item that can be replaced with an exact counterpart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When exact qisas is impossible due to defect, the Hanafi school gives the victim the option to either accept the defective limb or claim full diyat.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Effect of Offender's Limb Loss on Qisas and Diyah
Explains ruling when offender's hand is lost before victim chooses diyah or qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas and diyah when the offender's limb is lost before the victim chooses, and distinguish the exception when the limb was cut as a legal punishment.

Core Idea
Qisas requires a present limb; if lost before choice, neither qisas nor diyah is due unless diyah was already chosen or the loss was by legal punishment.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in criminal law: after a hand is cut in retaliation, the offender's hand is lost (falls off or is cut unjustly) before the victim chooses between qisas and diyah. The Hanafi ruling is that the victim's right to qisas is extinguished because the limb no longer exists, and diyah is not automatically substituted unless the victim had already chosen it. However, if the hand was cut off as a legally mandated punishment (e.g., qisas for another crime or hadd for theft), diyah remains due even without choice. This nuanced ruling illustrates how Hanafi jurists balance the nature of the right (qisas is a personal right, diyah a property right) and the reality of the limb's existence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the original obligation
The act is qisas (retributive cutting of the offender's hand). The original obligation (wajib asli) is qisas, not diyah; diyah only becomes obligatory when the victim chooses it.
This is the default Hanafi position: qisas is the primary right, diyah is a substitute upon choice.
2
Analyze the scenario of limb loss without victim's choice
If the offender's hand is lost (falls off or is unjustly cut) before the victim has chosen diyah, both qisas and diyah lapse. Qisas lapses because the limb (mahall) is absent; diyah does not arise because it was not chosen.
The victim ends up with no remedy in this scenario.
3
Contrast with scenario where diyah was already chosen
If the victim had already chosen diyah before the limb was lost, the obligation of diyah remains valid and must be paid.
The right has already transferred from personal to property right.
4
Examine the exception: limb cut as legal punishment
If the offender's hand was cut off as a legal punishment (e.g., qisas for another crime, or hadd for theft), then diyah is wajib even if the victim had not chosen it. The hand is considered metaphorically present because the offender fulfilled a duty.
Rationale: The punishment was a fulfillment of obligation, not a loss of the limb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كتاب الجنايات
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس کا حق قصاص میں متعین ہے اور مال کی جانب حق منتقل ہوتا ہے مجنی علیہ کے اختیار کرنے کی وجہ سے تو اس کا حق ساقط ہو جائے گا ہاتھ کے فوات کی وجہ سے بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ کسی ایسے حق کی وجہ سے ہاتھ کاٹا گیا جو اس پر واجب ہے یعنی قصاص یا چوری تو اس پر دیت واجب ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے اس سے اپنے حق واجبی کو ادا کیا ہے تو معنوی اعتبار سے ہاتھ اس کے لئے
سالم رہا۔
تشریح بکر کا وہ ہاتھ جس کا ذکر چل رہا تھا خود بخود گر گیا یا ظلما کسی نے کاٹ دیا تو اب کیا ہوگا؟ مجنی علیہ سے زید مراد ہے جس کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا ہے۔
تو بہر حال اگر زید نے ابھی دیت لینا اختیار نہ کیا ہو بلکہ ابھی اس کا ذکر ہی نہیں آیا تھا یا زید نے قصاص کو منتخب کر لیا تھا کہ یہ صورت پیش آگئی کہ بکر کے ہاتھ کو کسی نے ظلماً کاٹ دیا یاوہ خود ہی گر گیا تو اب نہ قصاص رہا اور نہ دیت کیونکہ واجب اصلی تو یہاں قصاص ہے اور مال جب واجب ہوتا ہے کہ مجنی علیہ دیت کو اختیار کرے۔ حالانکہ اس صورت میں مجنی علیہ نے دیت کو اختیار نہیں کیا لہذا نہ قصاص ہوگا اور نہ دیت، قصاص اس لئے نہ ہوگا کہ محل قصاص ندارد ہے اور دیت اس لئے نہیں کہ اس کو اختیار نہیں کیا گیا تھا۔ البتہ اگر مجنی علیہ دیت لینا اختیار کر چکا تھا اور یہ واقعہ پیش آیا ہو تو دیت کا وجوب برقرار ہے۔ اور یہی تمام صورتیں ہیں لیکن اس کا ہا تھ ظلما نہیں کاٹا گیا بلکہ کسی حق کے بدلہ میں کاٹا گیا ہے جو اس پر واجب ہے مثلاً قصاص میں کاٹا گیا ہے یا چوری میں کاٹا گیا ہے تو اب کسی بھی صورت میں مجنی علیہ کا حق ساقط نہ ہو گا بلکہ بہر صورت دیت واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں معنوی حیثیت سے گو یا ہاتھ موجود ہے، مگر حقیقہ نہیں، حقیقت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے قصاص معدوم ہو گیا اور معنی کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے دیت باقی رہے گی۔
It is not because his right is fixed in qisas, and the right transfers to the side of property due to the victim's choice, so his right will be dropped due to the loss of the hand. Contrary to the case when the hand was cut due to a right that is obligatory upon him, i.e., qisas or theft, then diyah is wajib because he has fulfilled his obligatory right, so in a metaphorical sense the hand remained intact for him. Explanation: Bkr's hand, which was being mentioned, fell off by itself or someone unjustly cut it, then what will happen? The victim refers to Zayd whose hand was cut. So in any case, if Zayd had not yet chosen to take diyah, rather it had not even been mentioned, or Zayd had chosen qisas, and this situation occurred that Bkr's hand was unjustly cut by someone or it fell off, then neither qisas remains nor diyah because the original obligation here is qisas, and property becomes obligatory when the victim chooses diyah. However, in this situation the victim did not choose diyah, so neither qisas nor diyah will occur. Qisas will not occur because the locus of qisas is absent, and diyah because it was not chosen. But if the victim had already chosen to take diyah and this incident occurred, then the obligation of diyah remains. And these are all scenarios. But if his hand was not cut unjustly, but was cut in exchange for a right that is obligatory on him, e.g., it was cut in qisas or for theft, then in any case the victim's right will not be dropped; rather in any case diyah will be wajib. Because in this case, in a metaphorical sense the hand is present, but not in reality. Considering reality, qisas is extinguished, and considering meaning, diyah remains.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where the offender's hand, which was injured, is later lost (falls off or is cut unjustly) before the victim has chosen between qisas and diyah. The ruling is that the victim's right to qisas is extinguished because the subject of qisas no longer exists. If the victim had already chosen diyah, then diyah remains obligatory. However, if the hand was cut off as a legally mandated punishment (qisas for another crime or hadd for theft), then even if the hand is lost, diyah is still due because the hand is considered metaphorically present since the offender fulfilled his obligation. This is a Hanafi ruling based on the principle that qisas requires a physical limb to be exacted, while diyah is a property right that transfers upon choice.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retributive justice: exacting a similar injury on the offender as he inflicted
دیت (diyah): Monetary compensation paid to the victim or heirs for bodily harm
مجنی علیہ (majni alayh): The victim of the crime
محل قصاص (mahall qisas): The physical site of qisas, i.e., the offender's limb that must be present for retribution
حق واجبی (haqq wajibi): An obligatory right that must be fulfilled

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the victim's right to qisas if the offender's hand is lost (e.g., falls off) after the injury but before the victim chooses diyah?
A) Qisas remains valid and must be exacted on another limb.
B) Qisas is extinguished and diyah is also not due.
C) The victim automatically gets diyah.
D) The offender must pay both qisas and diyah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, qisas is the default right; diyah only arises upon the victim's explicit choice, except when the limb was lost as a legal punishment — then diyah is always due.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for Head Wound When Victim's Head Smaller Than Assailant's
States the victim's choice between qisas and diyah for a head wound that covers his entire head but not the assailant's.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to a victim of a head wound when the wound covers the entire width of the victim's head but not the assailant's, and explain the Hanafi reasoning based on the principle of avoiding excessive disfigurement.

Core Idea
Exact proportional qisas or take arsh—the victim chooses to prevent greater harm.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in qisas for head wounds (shajjah). When the victim's head is smaller than the assailant's, the wound may cover the entire victim's head but only part of the assailant's. The Hanafi school grants the victim a choice between exacting qisas proportional to his own wound and taking compensatory payment (arsh). This ruling is based on the principle that exacting full qisas would cause greater disfigurement than the victim suffered, which is unjust. The reasoning parallels the case of a paralyzed hand versus a healthy one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine the anatomical dimensions: the wound on the victim's head spans the entire width (qarnan) of his head but does not span the entire width of the assailant's head.
Victim's head is smaller.
2
State the ruling
The victim may choose either to exact qisas to the same measure as his wound (starting from any side) or to take arsh (compensation).
This is a right, not a duty.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The wound is disfiguring; exacting full qisas on the assailant's head would cause more disfigurement than the victim suffered, so giving a choice avoids injustice.
Principle: do not exceed the harm.
4
Apply the analogy with paralyzed hand
Just as in the case of a healthy vs. paralyzed hand where qisas is impossible without excess, here exacting full qisas is impossible without causing more harm.
Qiyas: similar reasoning.
5
Extend to opposite and lengthwise scenarios
The same ruling applies when the victim's head is larger and when the wound is in the length of the head, because the reasoning does not change.
The principle is consistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن شج رجلا فاستوعبت الشجة ما بين قرنيه وهى لا تستوعب ما بين قرنى الشاج فالمشجوج بالخيار ان شاء اقتص بمقدار شجته يبتدى من اى الجانبين شاء وان شاء اخذ الارش لان الشجة موجبة لكونها مشينة فيزداد الشين بزيادتها وفى استيفائه ما بين قرنى الشاج زيادة على ما فعل ولا يلحقه من الشين باستيفائه قدر حقه ما يلحق المشجوج فينتقص فيخير كما في الشلاء والصحيحة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی شخص کا سر پھوڑ دیا پس زخم نے سر کی دونوں جانب کو گھیر لیا اور یہ زخم پھوڑنے والے کی دونوں جانب کو نہیں گھیرتا تو مشحوج کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے تو اپنے زخم کی مقدار کے مطابق قصاص لے لے جونی جانب سے شروع کر دے اور اگر چاہے دیت لے لے اس لئے کی زخم قصاص کو واجب کرنے والا ہے کیونکہ یہ عیب دار کرنے کا باعث ہے پس زخم کی زیادتی کی وجہ سے عیب میں اضافہ ہوگا اور مشحوج کے وصول کرنے میں شاج کی دونوں جانب کے درمیان شاج کے فعل پر زیادتی ہے اور مشحوج کے اپنے حق کے بقدر وصول کرنے میں شاج کو وہ عیب لاحق نہیں ہوگا جو مشحوج کو لاحق ہوا ہے تو مسجوج کا حق ناقص ہو جائے گا تو مشجوج کو اختیار ہو گا جیسے شل اور صحیح ہاتھ میں ۔
تشریح زید کا سر چھوٹا سا ہے مثلاً چوڑائی میں داہنی جانب سے بائیں جانب تک کل چار انگل کا عرض ہے، اور بکر کا مثلاً ایک بالشت ہے اب صورت یہ ہوئی کہ بکر نے زید کا سر پھوڑا اور اتنا زخم لگا ہے کہ پورے عرض کو محیط ہو گیا یعنی چار انگل ، اب اگر زید سے کہا جائے کہ چار انگل قصاص لے لے تو بکر کے سر میں چار انگل تھوڑی سی دور تک ہو جائیں گے اور اس کا پورا سر خراب نہ ہوگا تو حق زید ناقص رہا اور اگر پورا سر پھوڑنے کا یعنی پوری ایک بالشت زخمی کرنے کا اختیار دیا جائے تو یہ مقدار جنایت سے زیادہ ہے جو ظلم ہے۔ لہذازید کو دو اختیار ہیں .
-1
صرف چار انگل کی مقدار جس جانب سے چاہے پھوڑ دے۔ - اور اگر چاہے تو دیت لے لے جیسے پہلے مسئلہ میں ہوا تھا جب کہ قاطع کا ہاتھ شل یا خشک تھا ایسے ہی یہاں بھی ہو گا۔ تنبیه شاج سر کو زخمی کرنے والا یعنی بکر محجوج جس کا سر زخمی کیا گیا ہے یعنی زید۔
مشجوج کا سر بڑا اور شاج کا سر چھوٹا ہے، اب قصاص اور دیت دونوں کا اختیار ہے
وفي عكسه يخير ايضا لانه يتعذر الاستيفاء كملا للتعدى الى غير حقه وكذا اذا كانت الشجة في طول الرأس وهى تاخذ من جبهته الى قفاه ولا تبلغ الى قفا الشاج فهو بالخيار لان المعنى لا يختلف
ترجمہ اور اس کے عکس میں بھی اختیار دیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ کامل استیفاء حعذر ہے، مشجوج کے حق کے غیر تک تعدی کی وجہ سے اور ایسے ہی جب کہ زخم سر کی لمبائی میں ہو اور زخم شروع ہوا ہو اس کی پیشانی سے اس کی گدی تک اور یہ زخم شاج کی گدی تک نہ پہو نچتا ہو تو مشجوج مختار ہے اس لئے کہ وجہ مختلف نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اور اگر ادل کے برعکس ہو یعنی مجوج کا سر بڑا ہے اور شاج کا چھوٹا ہے اب بھی یہی حکم ہوگا کہ چاہے قصاص لے لے اپنے حق کے بقدر اور چاہے دیت لے نے مثلاً محجوج کا سر چار انگل زخمی ہوا ہے جو ذرا سی دور میں آ گیا اور شاج کے اندر یہ مقدار دونوں جانب کو گھیر لے گی تو مشحوج کو اختیار ہے کہ چار انگل اس کے سرکو زخمی کرے اور اگر چاہے تو دنیت لے لے۔
اور یہی گفتگو اگر بجائے عرض کے طول میں ہو اس میں بھی یہی حکم ہے اور یہی اس کی بھی وجہ ہے۔
He said: And whoever wounds a man's head such that the wound encompasses the area between his two temples (horns), and it does not encompass the area between the two temples of the wounder, then the wounded person has the choice: if he wishes, he may exact qisas to the measure of his wound, starting from whichever side he wishes; and if he wishes, he may take compensatory payment (arsh). Because the wound obligates qisas due to it being disfiguring, and the disfigurement increases with its extent. And in exacting it between the temples of the wounder, there is an increase over what he did, and the wounder does not suffer the same disfigurement from exacting his due amount as the wounded suffered, so he becomes deficient, thus he is given a choice, just as in the case of a paralyzed and a healthy hand. Explanation: Al-Quduri said: And whoever wounds a person's head, so the wound encompassed both sides of the head and does not encompass both sides of the wounder, then the wounded has the choice: if he wishes, he may exact qisas to the measure of his wound, starting from whichever side he chooses; and if he wishes, he may take diyah, because the wound obligates qisas as it is disfiguring, so the disfigurement increases with its increase. And in exacting it between the temples of the wounder, there is an increase over his act, and the wounder does not suffer the same disfigurement from exacting his due as the wounded suffered, so the wounded's right becomes deficient, thus he is given a choice, like in the case of a paralyzed and a healthy hand. Explanation: Zayd's head is small, e.g., width from right to left is four fingers, and Bkr's is e.g., one span. Now the situation is that Bkr wounded Zayd's head and the wound encompassed the entire width, i.e., four fingers. Now if Zayd is told to take qisas of four fingers, on Bkr's head four fingers will be a small distance and his entire head will not be damaged, so Zayd's right is deficient. And if he is given the option to wound the entire head, i.e., one span, that is more than the injury, which is injustice. So Zayd has two options: (1) Only four fingers from whichever side he wishes; (2) If he wishes, take diyah, like in the previous issue when the cutter's hand was paralyzed or dry. Similarly here. Note: The wounder is Bkr, the wounded is Zayd. The wounded's head is large and the wounder's head is small, now both qisas and diyah are options. And in the opposite case, he is also given a choice because complete exacting is impossible due to transgressing beyond his right. Similarly, if the wound is in the length of the head, taking from his forehead to his nape and does not reach the nape of the wounder, then he has a choice because the reasoning does not differ. Translation: And in its opposite, he is also given a choice because complete exacting is impossible due to transgressing beyond his right. And similarly, when the wound is in the length of the head and it takes from his forehead to his nape and does not reach the nape of the wounder, then the wounded has a choice because the meaning does not differ. Explanation: And if the opposite occurs, i.e., the wounded's head is large and the wounder's is small, then the same ruling applies: he may take qisas to the measure of his right or take diyah. For example, the wounded's head was wounded four fingers, which covered a small distance, and within the wounder this amount would encompass both sides, so the wounded has the choice to wound four fingers on his head or take diyah. And this same discussion applies if it is in length instead of width: the same ruling and the same reason.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri, explained in Urdu, addresses a specific scenario in head wounds (shajjah). When the victim's head is smaller than the assailant's, the wound covers the entire width of the victim's head but not the assailant's. The victim has two options: (1) exact qisas proportional to his own wound's size, choosing which side to start from, or (2) take diyah (arsh). The reason is that the wound is disfiguring, and exacting full qisas (the entire width of the assailant's head) would exceed the original injury and cause more disfigurement than suffered. This parallels the case of a healthy hand vs. a paralyzed hand. The same ruling applies in the reverse situation (victim's head larger) or when the wound is in the length of the head. In all cases, the victim is given a choice because exacting complete qisas is impossible without exceeding the right.

Key Terms
شجة (shajjah): A head wound that breaks the bone or cuts the skin, specifically a wound that exposes the bone.
قرنان (qarnan): The two sides of the head from the temples to the back of the head.
شاج (shājj): The person who inflicts the head wound.
مشجوج (mashjūj): The person who receives the head wound.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for wounds less than full diyah, calculated based on the extent of the wound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when a head wound covers the entire width of the victim's head but not the assailant's, what options does the victim have?
A) Only qisas on the entire assailant's head.
B) Only diyah.
C) To exact qisas proportional to the wound's size or take arsh.
D) No qisas is possible; only diyah.

Key Takeaway
The victim of a head wound that covers his entire head but not the assailant's may choose between proportional qisas and arsh to avoid excessive harm.

Qisas — Retaliation

No Qisas for Tongue or Penis: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for tongue and penis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qisas for tongue and penis and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the root-cut scenario.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact equality; tongue and penis contract and expand, so equality is impossible.

The Hanafi school holds that qisas is not applicable for the tongue or the penis due to their variable size. This lesson examines the rationale and an internal disagreement: Abu Yusuf argued that if cut from the root, equality can be achieved. We will analyze the proof and the relied position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the ruling from Al-Quduri: 'No qisas in the tongue and not in the penis.' This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's opposing view
Abu Yusuf holds that if the organ is cut from the root, qisas is wajib because the entire organ is removed and equality can be ensured.
The root-cut eliminates the variability issue according to him.
3
Compare the proofs
The majority proof: the organ contracts and expands, so exact equality (musawah) cannot be achieved. Abu Yusuf's proof: cutting from the root removes the entire organ, making the measure of retaliation possible via the incision.
Focus on the 'illa (effective cause): variability vs. root-cut.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response and determine the mufta bihi
The majority responds that even from the root, the organ's variable length before cutting makes it impossible to ensure that the retaliation matches the injury exactly. Therefore, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is no qisas; only diyah is due.
Al-Quduri's text implies the majority view is the operative one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا قصاص في اللسان ولا في الذكر وعن ابى يوسف انه اذا قطع من اصله يجب لانه يمكن اعتبار المساواة ولنا انه ينقبض وينبسط فلا يمكن اعتبار المساواة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور زبان اور ذکر میں قصاص نہیں ہے اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ جب ان کو جڑ سے کاٹ دیا جائے تو قصاص واجب ہے اس لئے کہ مساوات ممکن ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ کہ یہ سکڑ جاتے ہیں اور کشادہ ہو جاتے ہیں تو مساوات کا اعتبار ممکن نہیں ہے۔
He said: And no qisas in the tongue and not in the penis. And from Abu Yusuf that if it is cut from its root, it is obligatory because equality can be considered. And our proof is that it contracts and expands, so equality cannot be considered. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And there is no qisas in the tongue and in the penis. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that when they are cut from the root, qisas is obligatory because equality is possible. And our proof is that they contract and expand, so equality cannot be considered.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri presents the Hanafi ruling that qisas is not established for the tongue or the penis. The reason given in the commentary is that these organs are not fixed in size; they contract and expand, so exact equality in qisas is impossible. Abu Yusuf, however, held that if these organs are cut from the root, qisas is possible because then the entire organ is removed, and equality can be measured by the motion of cutting from the root. The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) reject this due to the variability of the organ's length. The relied-upon position is that there is no qisas, and only diyah is due.

Key Terms
لسان (lisān): The tongue, as a body part for which qisas is sought.
ذكر (dhakar): The male genital organ, as a body part for which qisas is sought.
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retributive justice: exacting a similar injury on the offender.
انقباض (inqibāḍ): Contraction (of the organ), making it shorter.
انبساط (inbisāṭ): Expansion (of the organ), making it longer.
مساوات (musāwāt): Equality between the injury inflicted and the retaliation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Yusuf differ from the Hanafi majority regarding qisas for the tongue?
A) He believed the tongue does not contract or expand.
B) He argued that cutting from the root ensures equality.
C) He considered the tongue a vital organ requiring qisas.
D) He relied on a different hadith.

Key Takeaway
Qisas requires exact equivalence; for variable organs like tongue and penis, only diyah is due.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Victim's Option When Qisas Cannot Be Exact Due to Head Size Differences
Explains victim's options when head injury cannot be exactly matched

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when exact qisas for a head wound is impossible due to size mismatch, and distinguish the scenarios that trigger the victim's choice between limited qisas and diyat.

Core Idea
When exact retaliation is impossible, the victim may choose partial qisas or full diyat.

In this lesson, we examine a practical scenario from Al-Hidayah: a head wound (shajj) where the victim's head is smaller than the perpetrator's. Since exact equivalence in qisas is impossible without either undercompensating the victim or exceeding the injury, Hanafi law gives the victim a choice: take the equivalent partial wound on the perpetrator, or accept blood money (diyah). This rule applies symmetrically to width and length mismatches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Name the perpetrator (shājj) and victim (mashjūj). Note their head sizes relative to each other.
2
Understand the problem of exact qisas
Why cannot the victim take an identical wound? Because the perpetrator's head is larger, a wound of the same width would be less severe; a wound of full width would exceed the victim's injury. Both are unjust.
The Hanafi principle insists on exact equivalence in qisas (mumāthalah).
3
State the Hanafi solution
The victim is given two options: (a) inflict a wound of the same size as his own injury (partial qisas) on the perpetrator, or (b) take diyah (blood money).
This preserves justice by allowing the victim to obtain his due without oppression.
4
Extend to other scenarios
The same ruling applies when the victim's head is larger (the perpetrator's is smaller) and when the wound is in the longitudinal direction instead of width.
The underlying ʿilla (reason) is the impossibility of complete exact retaliation without transgression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح زید کا سر چھوٹا سا ہے مثلاً چوڑائی میں داہنی جانب سے بائیں جانب تک کل چار انگل کا عرض ہے، اور بکر کا مثلاً ایک بالشت ہے اب صورت یہ ہوئی کہ بکر نے زید کا سر پھوڑا اور اتنا زخم لگا ہے کہ پورے عرض کو محیط ہو گیا یعنی چار انگل، اب اگر زید سے کہا جائے کہ چار انگل قصاص لے لے تو بکر کے سر میں چار انگل تھوڑی سی دور تک ہو جائیں گے اور اس کا پورا سر خراب نہ ہوگا تو حق زید ناقص رہا اور اگر پورا سر پھوڑنے کا یعنی پوری ایک بالشت زخمی کرنے کا اختیار دیا جائے تو یہ مقدار جنایت سے زیادہ ہے جو ظلم ہے۔ لہذا زید کو دو اختیار ہیں۔
1. صرف چار انگل کی مقدار جس جانب سے چاہے پھوڑ دے۔
2. اور اگر چاہے تو دیت لے لے جیسے پہلے مسئلہ میں ہوا تھا جب کہ قاطع کا ہاتھ شل یا خشک تھا ایسے ہی یہاں بھی ہو گا۔ تنبیه: شاج سر کو زخمی کرنے والا یعنی بکر، مشجوج جس کا سر زخمی کیا گیا ہے یعنی زید۔
مشجوج کا سر بڑا اور شاج کا سر چھوٹا ہے، اب قصاص اور دیت دونوں کا اختیار ہے۔
وفي عكسه يخير ايضا لانه يتعذر الاستيفاء كملا للتعدى الى غير حقه وكذا اذا كانت الشجة في طول الرأس وهى تاخذ من جبهته الى قفاه ولا تبلغ الى قفا الشاج فهو بالخيار لان المعنى لا يختلف۔ ترجمہ: اور اس کے عکس میں بھی اختیار دیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ کامل استیفاء متعذر ہے، مشجوج کے حق کے غیر تک تعدی کی وجہ سے اور ایسے ہی جب کہ زخم سر کی لمبائی میں ہو اور زخم شروع ہوا ہو اس کی پیشانی سے اس کی گدی تک اور یہ زخم شاج کی گدی تک نہ پہنچتا ہو تو مشجوج مختار ہے اس لئے کہ وجہ مختلف نہیں ہے۔ تشریح: اور اگر اس کے برعکس ہو یعنی مشجوج کا سر بڑا ہے اور شاج کا چھوٹا ہے اب بھی یہی حکم ہوگا کہ چاہے قصاص لے لے اپنے حق کے بقدر اور چاہے دیت لے لے۔ مثلاً مشجوج کا سر چار انگل زخمی ہوا ہے جو ذرا سی دور میں آ گیا اور شاج کے اندر یہ مقدار دونوں جانب کو گھیر لے گی تو مشجوج کو اختیار ہے کہ چار انگل اس کے سر کو زخمی کرے اور اگر چاہے تو دیت لے لے۔
اور یہی گفتگو اگر بجائے عرض کے طول میں ہو اس میں بھی یہی حکم ہے اور یہی اس کی بھی وجہ ہے۔
Explanation: Zaid's head is small, for example, in width from right side to left side total four fingers breadth, and Bakr's head is, for example, one span. Now the situation is that Bakr broke Zaid's head and inflicted a wound that encompassed the entire width, i.e., four fingers. Now if Zaid is told to take four fingers as retaliation, then in Bakr's head four fingers will go a short distance and his whole head will not be damaged, so Zaid's right remains deficient. And if he is given the option to break the whole head, i.e., full one span wound, then this amount exceeds the injury, which is oppression. Therefore Zaid has two options: 1. Break only the amount of four fingers from whichever side he wishes. 2. Or if he wishes, he may take the diyah, just as in the previous issue when the cutter's hand was paralyzed or dry, similarly here it will be. Note: Shajj is the one who wounds the head, i.e., Bakr; Mashjuj is the one whose head was wounded, i.e., Zaid. Mashjuj's head is big and Shajj's head is small, now both retaliation and diyah are options. And in its opposite he is also given choice, because complete execution is impossible due to transgression beyond his right. Similarly, when the wound is in the length of the head, it takes from his forehead to his nape and does not reach the nape of the Shajj, then the Mashjuj has the choice, because the reason does not differ. Translation: And in its opposite he is also given choice, because complete execution is impossible, due to transgression beyond the right of the Mashjuj. And similarly, when the wound is in the length of the head, the wound begins from his forehead to his nape and this wound does not reach the nape of the Shajj, then the Mashjuj has the choice, because the reason does not differ. Explanation: And if the opposite occurs, i.e., Mashjuj's head is big and Shajj's is small, then also the same ruling applies: he may take retaliation to the extent of his right, or he may take diyah. For example, Mashjuj's head was wounded four fingers, which went a short distance, and inside Shajj this amount will encompass both sides, so Mashjuj has the choice to wound four fingers on his head, or if he wishes, take diyah. And the same discussion if it is in length instead of width, the same ruling applies, and the same is its reason.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Al-Hidayah, explaining the victim's options when retaliation (qisas) cannot be exactly equal due to different head sizes between the victim and the perpetrator. The key principle is that qisas must be equivalent, and if perfect equivalence is impossible, the victim may either exact whatever equivalent retaliation is possible or take diyat (blood money). The text considers three scenarios: (1) victim's head smaller in width, (2) victim's head larger in width, (3) wound in longitudinal direction. In all cases, the victim has the choice between limited retaliation or diyat. This is based on the general Hanafi rule that when complete qisas is impossible without transgression, the option shifts to partial qisas or compensation.

Key Terms
شاج (shājj): The person who inflicts a wound on the head (the perpetrator in head injury cases).
مشجوج (mashjūj): The person who receives a head wound (the victim).
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliation in kind, exacting the same injury on the perpetrator as was inflicted on the victim.
دیت (diyah): Blood money, monetary compensation paid to the victim or heirs in lieu of qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only diyat
C) Either exact the same width on the perpetrator's head or take diyat
D) No recourse

Key Takeaway
When exact qisas for a head wound is impossible due to head size differences, the Hanafi school gives the victim the choice between partial retaliation and blood money.

No Qisas for Tongue and Penis Due to Variable Size
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for tongue and penis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qisas for the tongue and penis, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for fatwa.

Core Idea
No qisas for tongue or penis because they contract and expand — exact equality is impossible.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific area of jinayat (injuries): whether retaliation (qisas) applies when the tongue or male organ is cut. The Hanafi school has a well-known position that qisas is not required for these organs due to their variable nature. However, Imam Abu Yusuf partially differs. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurisprudence applies the principle of exact equivalence (musawah) in qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act is being discussed (cutting the tongue or penis) and what is the default ruling in the matn?
Al-Quduri states: no qisas for the tongue and no qisas for the penis.
2
State the majority Hanafi ruling
What is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani? They deny qisas entirely.
The reason given is that these organs contract and expand, making equality impossible.
3
Identify the opposing view
What does Abu Yusuf hold? He distinguishes based on the location of the cut.
Abu Yusuf: if cut from the root, qisas is obligatory because equality is possible.
4
Analyze the key evidence
What is the proof (dalil) for each side? Majority uses rational proof (contractile nature); Abu Yusuf uses the defined junction at the root.
Text: ينقبض وينبسط فلا يمكن اعتبار المساواة.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon for fatwa? The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is preferred.
Thus, no qisas in any case; only diyat is wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زبان اور ذکر (عضو تناسل) میں قصاص ہے یا نہیں
قال ولا قصاص في اللسان ولا في الذكر وعن ابي يوسف انه اذا قطع من اصله يجب لانه يمكن اعتبار المساواة ولنا انه ينقبض وينبسط فلا يمكن اعتبار المساواة
ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا اور زبان اور ذکر میں قصاص نہیں ہے اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ جب ان کو جڑ سے کاٹ دیا جائے تو قصاص واجب ہے اس لئے کہ مساوات ممکن ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ کہ یہ سکڑ جاتے ہیں اور کشادہ ہو جاتے ہیں تو مساوات کا اعتبار ممکن نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: اگر زید نے بکر کی زبان کاٹ دی یا ذکر کاٹ دیا تو قصاص نہ ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اگر زبان اور ذکر کو جڑ سے کاٹ دیا تو قصاص واجب ہوگا ورنہ نہیں کیونکہ اب مماثلت اور مساوات ہو سکتی ہے، کہ دوسرے کا بھی جڑ سے کاٹ دیا جائے مگر ہم نے کہا کہ زبان اور ذکر کبھی تو سکڑ جاتے ہیں اور کبھی کشادہ ہو جاتے ہیں تو مساوات کا اعتبار غیر ممکن ہے۔
Is there qisas for the tongue and the penis (private part)? He (Imam al-Quduri) said: There is no qisas for the tongue and no qisas for the penis. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that if they are cut from the root, qisas is obligatory because equality can be considered. And our (Hanafi) proof is that they contract and expand, so equality cannot be considered. Translation: Al-Quduri said: There is no qisas for the tongue and the penis. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that when they are cut from the root, qisas is obligatory because equality is possible. And our proof is that they contract and expand, so consideration of equality is not possible. Explanation: If Zaid cut Bakr's tongue or penis, qisas will not be applied. Imam Abu Yusuf said that if the tongue and penis are cut from the root, qisas will be obligatory, otherwise not, because then similarity and equality can occur, as the other's can also be cut from the root. But we said that the tongue and penis sometimes contract and sometimes expand, so consideration of equality is impossible.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qisas for cutting the tongue or penis. The relied-upon position (from the matn of Al-Quduri) is that no qisas applies because these organs are not fixed in size; they contract and expand, making precise equivalence impossible. Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if cut entirely from the root, the cut is at a defined junction, so equality can be achieved, thus qisas applies. The Hanafi response (of the majority) is that even from the root, the organ's variable nature prevents exact matching. The practical effect: under the mufta bihi position, the victim receives diyat.

Key Terms
اللسان (al-lisān): The tongue, mentioned as an organ where qisas is generally not applied due to its contractile nature.
الذكر (al-dhakar): The male penis; similar ruling as tongue due to variable size.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the tongue is internal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school denies qisas for the tongue and penis due to their variable size, making exact equality impossible; diyat is the alternative.

Qisas — Retaliation
