Qisas for Glans, Ear, and Lip: The Measurability Condition
Specifies when qisas applies for glans, ear, and lip based on measurability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on qisas for cutting the glans, ear, and lip, and explain the condition of measurability that determines whether qisas applies.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact equivalence; only known, measurable cuts qualify.

This passage from a classical Hanafi text clarifies when qisas is obligatory for injuries to three specific body parts: the glans, ear, and lip. The key principle is that qisas demands precise matching (musawah); if the exact amount of the cut cannot be determined, diyat replaces qisas. By working through these rulings, you will understand how the Hanafi school applies the condition of measurability in bodily injury cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three body parts and the ruling for each when cut completely
For each body part—glans, ear, lip—state whether qisas applies when the entire part is cut. According to the text, qisas is obligatory for full cuts of all three: glans (الحشفة), ear (الأذن), and lip (الشفة).
2
Note the exception for partial cuts
The text distinguishes partial cuts: for the glans and lip, partial cuts do not trigger qisas; for the ear, even a partial cut requires qisas. This is a crucial difference.
Ear is unique because it has a fixed boundary that does not change shape.
3
Extract the underlying reasoning (illah) for each ruling
For the glans: the cut location is known like a joint (معلوم كالمفصل). For the ear: it does not contract or expand, and has a known limit (حد يعرف). For the lip: when completely cut, equality can be considered; when partial, equality is impossible.
The illah for the ear applies to both full and partial cuts because the boundary is fixed.
4
Formulate the general principle
From these cases, derive that qisas requires the ability to achieve exact equality in the injury. If the exact amount cannot be known or replicated (as in partial glans or lip cuts), qisas is not applied and diyat substitutes.
This principle also applies to other body parts in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الا ان تقطع الحشفة لان موضع القطع معلوم كالمفصل ولو قطع بعض الحشفة او بعض الذكر فلا قصاص فيه لان البعض لا يعلم مقداره بخلاف الاذن اذا قطع كله او بعضه لانه لا ينقبض ولا ينبسط وله حد يعرف فيمكن اعتبار المساواة والشفة اذا استقصاها بالقطع يجب القصاص لا مكان اعتبار المساواة بخلاف ما اذا قطع بعضها لانه يتعذر اعتبارها
ترجمہ: مگر یہ کہ حشفہ کاٹ دیا جائے اس لئے کہ کاٹنے کی جگہ معلوم ہے مثل جوڑ کے، اور اگر حشفہ کا کچھ حصہ یا ذکر کا کچھ حصہ کاٹا گیا تو اس میں قصاص نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ بعض کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے بخلاف کان کے جب کہ وہ کل یا اس کا بعض حصہ کاٹا جائے اس لئے کہ کان نہ سکڑتا اور نہ کشادہ ہوتا اور کان کی جانی پہچانی مقدار ہے تو مساوات کا اعتبار ممکن ہے، اور ہونٹ جب کہ اس کو پورا کاٹا ہو تو قصاص واجب ہوگا، مساوات کے اعتبار کی وجہ سے، بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ اس کا بعض کاٹا ہو اس لئے کہ مساوات کا اعتبار متعذر ہے۔
تشریح: اگر کسی نے کسی کا حشفہ کاٹ دیا تو یہ جگہ جانی پہچانی ہے لہذا قصاص لیا جائے گا جیسے ہاتھ کی صورت میں جوڑ سے کاٹنے کا حکم تھا۔ اور اگر حشفہ یا ذکر کا کچھ حصہ کاٹا ہو تو اس میں قصاص نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ بعض معلوم نہیں یعنی متعین جگہ نہیں ہے، اس لئے مماثلت و مساوات کی رعایت نہ ہو سکے گی۔ ہاں اگر کان کاٹ دیا سارا یا کچھ تو قصاص واجب ہوگا کیونکہ سکڑتا نہیں اور نہ کشادہ ہوتا ہے اور کان کی ایک حد مقرر ہے تو یہاں مساوات ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور ہونٹ اگر پورا کاٹ دیا ہو تو قصاص ہے اور بعض میں قصاص نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ اول میں مساوات ہو سکتی ہے اور ثانی میں مساوات نہیں ہو سکتی۔
Except if the glans is cut, because the place of cutting is known like a joint. And if part of the glans or part of the penis is cut, then there is no qisas in it, because the amount of the part is not known. Contrary to the ear, if the whole or part of it is cut, because it does not contract nor expand, and it has a known limit, so equality can be considered. And the lip, if it is completely cut, qisas is obligatory due to the possibility of considering equality, contrary to if part of it is cut, because considering equality is impossible. Translation: Except if the glans is cut, because the place of cutting is known like a joint. And if some part of the glans or some part of the penis is cut, then there is no qisas in it, because the quantity of the part is not known. Contrary to the ear, when the whole or some part of it is cut, because the ear neither contracts nor expands, and the ear has a known, recognized amount, so equality can be considered. And the lip, when it is completely cut, qisas is obligatory due to the possibility of considering equality, contrary to the case when some of it is cut, because considering equality is not possible. Explanation: If someone cut someone else's glans, this place is known, so qisas will be taken, just as in the case of the hand, the ruling was cutting at the joint. And if some part of the glans or some part of the penis is cut, then there is no qisas in it, because the part is not known, i.e., it is not a defined place, so similarity and equality cannot be observed. Yes, if the ear is cut, completely or partially, qisas is obligatory because it does not contract nor expand, and the ear has a fixed limit, so equality can be achieved. And the lip, if the whole lip is cut, qisas is due; and if part is cut, there is no qisas, because in the first equality can be achieved, and in the second equality cannot be achieved.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage states rulings on qisas for specific body parts based on whether exact equivalence can be measured. The glans (حشفہ) is like a joint, so cutting the whole glans requires qisas; partial cut does not because the exact part is not measurable. The ear, whether whole or part, requires qisas because it has fixed boundaries and does not vary in size. The lip only requires qisas if cut completely; partial lip cuts do not qualify because the missing part cannot be exactly matched. These distinctions derive from the principle that qisas must be precisely equivalent; if the injury's amount cannot be determined, diyat is substituted.

Key Terms
الحشفة (al-ḥashafah): The glans of the penis; its cut is treated like a joint cut, so full cut requires qisas.
الشفة (al-shafah): The lip; if completely cut, qisas applies due to measurability; partial does not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When any part of the lip is cut
B) Only when the entire lip is cut
C) Never
D) Only if the lip is cut from the corner

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qisas for bodily injuries is only permissible when the exact amount of the cut is knowable and replicable, as seen in the distinct rulings for the glans, ear, and lip.

Settlement (Sulh) Between Killer and Heirs Abolishes Qisas
Ruling that sulh for property cancels qisas and imposes payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sulh for property cancels qisas and justify it using the Quranic verse and hadith.

Core Idea
Sulh with the heirs, even for a pittance, extinguishes qisas and binds the killer to pay the agreed sum.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from Al-Quduri's matn on sulh (settlement) in qisas cases. The passage establishes that when the killer and the heirs reach a compromise involving property, the right to qisas is replaced by a financial obligation, regardless of the amount. We will explore the textual proofs and the legal reasoning behind this leniency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Note that when the killer and the heirs agree on a property settlement (sulh), qisas is dropped and the property becomes wajib (obligatory) upon the killer.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the property is small or large.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: the Quranic verse 'فمن عفي له من أخيه شيء' (which is said to be revealed about sulh) and the hadith 'من قتل له قتيل...'.
These are naqli (textual) evidences supporting the permissibility of sulh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse indicates that a concession from the victim's family (through sulh) is acceptable in lieu of qisas; the hadith generalizes the acceptance of compensation.
The Hanafi interpretation sees the verse as directly endorsing sulh.
4
Understand the rationale
Qisas is a right of the heirs, and they may drop it by pardon ('afw) or by accepting compensation. Sulh is a form of mutual consent that serves the interests of both parties: the heirs receive something, and the killer's life is spared.
This reasoning shows why sulh is valid even for a small amount.
5
Confirm the conditions
The only conditions mentioned are: (1) mutual consent between the killer and the heirs, and (2) specification of some property (mal) as compensation.
No requirement for the property to equal diyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل قال واذا اصطلح القاتل واولياء القتيل على مال سقط القصاص ووجب المال قليلا كان أو كثيرا لقوله تعالى فمن عفى له من اخيه شئ الآية على ما قيل نزلت الآية فى الصلح وقوله عليه السلام من قتل له قتيل الحديث والمراد والله اعلم الاخذ بالرضا على ما بيناه وهو الصلح بعينه ولانه حق ثابت للورثة يجرى فيه الاسقاط عفوا فكذا تعويضا لاشتماله على احسان الاولياء واحياء القاتل فيجوز بالتراضى
ترجمہ: یہ فصل ہے مصالحت وغیرہ کے بیان میں۔ قدوری نے فرمایا: اور جب قاتل اور مقتول کے اولیاء نے مصالحت کر لی کسی مال پر تو قصاص ساقط ہو گیا اور مال واجب ہوگیا، قلیل ہو یا زیادہ، اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان فمن عفی لہ من اخيه شئ الآیہ کی وجہ سے، اس قول کے مطابق کہ آیت صلح کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی، اور آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے فرمان: من قتل له قتيل الحديث، اور مراد واللہ اعلم رضامندی سے لینا ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے بیان کیا، اور یہی بعینہ صلح ہے، اور اس لئے کہ یہ حق ورثہ کے لئے ثابت ہے، جس میں معاف کر کے ساقط کرنا جاری ہے، اسی طرح معاوضے کے طور پر بھی، اس لئے کہ اس میں اولیاء کا احسان اور قاتل کا زندہ رہنا شامل ہے، تو باہمی رضامندی سے جائز ہے۔
Section: He (Al-Quduri) said: And when the killer and the heirs of the killed person make a settlement (sulh) on some property, then the qisas is dropped and the property becomes obligatory, whether it be little or much, due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'But whoever remits something from his brother...' the verse, according to what has been said that the verse was revealed about sulh, and his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever has a relative killed...' the hadith. And the meaning, and Allah knows best, is taking with consent as we have explained, and it is exactly sulh. And because it is an established right of the heirs, in which dropping by way of pardon is applicable, so likewise by way of compensation, because it includes kindness to the heirs and giving life to the killer, so it is permissible by mutual consent.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil naqli) from the section on sulh (settlement). The matn states that if the killer and the heirs reach a settlement for any property (money or goods), qisas falls and the agreed amount becomes payable, regardless of whether it is small or large. The proofs are the Qur'anic verse 'فمن عفي له من أخيه شيء' which is said to have been revealed about sulh, and the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ. The rationale is that qisas is a right of the heirs, and they may drop it by pardon (afw) or by accepting compensation. Sulh is a form of mutual consent that extinguishes qisas and imposes the agreed property. The hanafi position emphasizes the validity of sulh even for a small amount, as it benefits both parties: the heirs receive compensation and the killer's life is spared.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A settlement or compromise between the killer and the heirs, usually for a property consideration.
عفو (ʿafw): Pardon; when heirs forgive the killer without compensation, qisas drops and no payment is due.
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retributive justice; the right of the heirs to demand the killer's life or equivalent punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The heirs can still demand qisas after accepting the money

Key Takeaway
A sulh settlement for any property, once mutually agreed, extinguishes the right to qisas and imposes the agreed compensation.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for Body Parts: Fixed vs Variable
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for variable body parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for tongue, penis, glans, ear, and lip, and distinguish the position of Abu Yusuf from the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact equivalence; parts that contract or expand cannot have qisas.

The principle of qisas is retaliation in kind, but only when exact equivalence (masawat) is possible. This passage explores which body parts qualify for qisas according to the Hanafi school, particularly the intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the tongue and penis. Understanding the condition of fixed limit versus variable size will clarify why the glans, ear, and whole lip have qisas, while partial cuts and the tongue/penis do not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Body Parts and the General Hanafi Rule
The passage lists five body parts: tongue, penis (dhakar), glans (hashafah), ear, and lip. For each, state whether the Hanafi school imposes qisas or not. Note the general principle: qisas is only when the cut part has a known, fixed limit and does not change size.
2
Locate the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf (Abu Yusuf's Exception)
Imam Abu Yusuf argues that if the tongue or penis is cut from the root, qisas is due because cutting the other's from the root ensures equivalence. Identify this opposing view within the Hanafi school and note that it contrasts with the majority position.
3
Analyze the Basis of Each Position: The Masawat Condition
Abu Hanifa's position rests on the physical nature of the tongue and penis: they contract and expand, so cutting at the root cannot guarantee equal length. Abu Yusuf focuses on the action (root cut) rather than the part's variability. Understand how the same condition (masawat) leads to different conclusions.
4
Apply the Principle to Glans, Ear, and Lip
For the glans, the place of cutting is precisely known like a joint, so full cut permits qisas but partial cut does not. The ear has a fixed boundary and does not contract/expand, so both full and partial cuts permit qisas. The lip: full cut permits qisas because equivalence can be observed; partial cut does not. Work through each example to see how the fixed-limit test applies.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Relyed-Upon Position)
The commentary explicitly sides with Abu Hanifa ('hum ne kaha'). Confirm that the operative ruling for fatwa today is: no qisas for tongue or penis even if cut from root; qisas for entire glans, entire ear or part of it, and entire lip; no qisas for partial cuts of glans or lip.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنايات
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ تشریح اگر زید نے بکر کی زبان کاٹ دی یا ذکر کاٹ دیا تو قصاص نہ ہوگا امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اگر زبان اور ذکر کو جڑ سے کاٹ دیا تو قصاص واجب ہوگا ورنہ نہیں کیونکہ اب مماثلت اور مساوات ہو سکتی ہے، کہ دوسرے کا بھی جڑ سے کاٹ دیا جائے مگر ہم نے کہا کہ زبان اور ذکر کبھی تو سکٹڑ جاتے ہیں اور کبھی کشادہ ہو جاتے ہیں تو مساوات کا اعتبار غیر ممکن ہے۔
حشفہ میں قصاص ہے
الا ان تقطع الحشفة لان موضع القطع معلوم كا لمفصل ولو قطع بعض الحشفة او بعض الذكر فلا قصاص فيه لان البعض لا يعلم مقداره بخلاف الاذن اذا قطع كله او بعضه لانه لا ينقبض ولا ينبسط وله حد يعرف فيمكن اعتبار المساواة والشفة اذا استقصا ها بالقطع يجب القصاص لا مكان اعتبارا لمساواة بخلاف ما اذا قطع بعضها لا نه يتعذر اعتبارها

اور اگر حشفہ یا ذکر کا کچھ حصہ کا نا ہو تو اس میں قصاص نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ بعض معلوم نہیں یعنی متعین جگہ نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے مماثلت و مساوات کی رعایت نہ ہو سکے گی۔
ہاں اگر کان کاٹ دیا سارا یا کچھ تو قصاص واجب ہو گا کیونکہ سکڑتا نہیں اور نہ کشادہ ہوتا ہے اور کان کی ایک حد مقرر ہے تو یہاں مساوات ہوسکتی ہے۔ اور ہونٹ اگر پورا کاٹ دیا ہو تو قصاص ہے اور بعض میں قصاص نہ ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اول میں مساوات ہو سکتی ہے اور ثانی میں مساوات نہیں ہو سکتی۔
Chapter of Jinayat. Commentary: If Zaid cut Bakr's tongue or cut his private part, there is no qisas. Imam Abu Yusuf said: If the tongue and private part are cut from the root, qisas is obligatory, otherwise not, because now equivalence becomes possible, that the other's may also be cut from the root. But we said that the tongue and private part sometimes contract and sometimes become extended, so observing equivalence is impossible. Qisas exists for the glans: unless the glans is cut, because the place of cutting is known like a joint. If part of the glans or part of the penis is cut, there is no qisas therein because the amount of the part is not known, unlike the ear when all or part of it is cut, because it does not contract or extend and it has a known limit, so equivalence can be observed. And the lip, if it is completely cut, qisas becomes due due to the possibility of observing equivalence, unlike if part of it is cut, because observing equivalence is impossible. Commentary: If someone cut someone's glans, this place is known, so qisas will be taken, like the ruling of cutting at the joint in the case of the hand. And if part of the glans or part of the penis is cut, there is no qisas because the part is not known, i.e., it is not a specific place, so equivalence cannot be observed. Yes, if the ear is cut entirely or partially, qisas becomes due because it does not contract or extend and the ear has a fixed limit, so equivalence is possible. And for the lip, if it is completely cut, there is qisas, and if partially, no qisas, because in the first equivalence is possible and in the second it is not possible.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the rulings of qisas for specific body parts, containing an intra-Hanafi dispute. The text begins with a general ruling: cutting the tongue or penis does not require qisas. Imam Abu Yusuf (Abu Yusuf) differs: if cut from the root, qisas is due because equivalence is possible by cutting the other's from the root. The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) is that these parts vary in size (contract and expand), so precise equivalence is impossible. Qisas is established for the glans because the cutting point is precisely known like a joint; similarly for the ear (whether whole or part) as it has a fixed boundary and does not change size. The lip, when cut entirely, allows equivalence; when only part is cut, the amount is uncertain so no qisas. The commentary emphasizes the principle of 'masawat' (equality) as the basis for qisas: where exact measurement is possible, qisas is due; where parts are indeterminate, only diya (blood money) applies. The position of Abu Yusuf is mentioned but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as stated by the commentator ('ham ne kaha').

Key Terms
حشفہ (hashafah): The glans (head) of the male organ.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment, exacting like injury for injury.
مساوات (masawat): Equality or equivalence between the original injury and the retaliation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Qisas only if the entire ear is cut.
D) Diya wajib, no qisas.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires exact equivalence for qisas; body parts that contract/expand (tongue, penis) or have unknown partial amounts (partial glans, partial lip) do not qualify, while fixed-limit parts (glans, ear, whole lip) do.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate

Compromise in Qisas – Sulh Drops Qisas and Imposes Wealth
Ruling with proof on sulh dropping qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compromise in qisas and explain the evidence from Quran and hadith, distinguishing the Hanafi requirement of mutual consent from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Compromise on any wealth between killer and heirs drops qisas and makes that wealth wajib, by Quran and Sunnah.

When a person is killed, the heirs have the right to demand qisas (retribution) or to forgive. But what if they strike a deal with the killer for money? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on such a compromise (sulh), which is considered a valid and commendable act that spares a life. We will look at the Quranic and hadith proofs, and also address a key disagreement with the Shafi'i school regarding whose consent is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a compromise (sulh) between the killer and the heirs upon some wealth. The ruling: qisas drops and that wealth becomes wajib (due), whether little or much.
The wealth can be any amount; it does not have to be the full diya.
2
Locate the primary dalil from Quran
The author cites Surah al-Baqarah 2:178: 'فمن عفى له من اخيه شئ' (then whoever is forgiven by his brother something). The Hanafi interpretation is that this verse allows compromise for a portion of the blood money or any wealth.
The verse is said to have been revealed concerning compromise (sulh).
3
Locate the secondary dalil from Hadith
The hadith: 'من قتل له قتيل فهو بالخيار: إما أن يعفو، وإما أن يقتل' (whoever has a slain relative has the choice: either pardon or kill). The Hanafi school interprets pardoning as including pardoning with compensation, i.e., compromise.
The key is that 'pardoning' can be for free or for wealth.
4
Analyze the basis for sulh's validity
The passage explains that qisas is a right of the servant (haqq al-'abd) where the servant's right predominates. Therefore, it can be dropped by the heirs through pardon (afw) or through compensation (sulh), similar to how one may forgive a debt or accept a settlement.
This categorization of rights justifies why qisas can be subject to compromise.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the heirs alone have the choice to take blood money even without the killer's consent. The Hanafi school requires mutual consent between killer and heirs for a valid sulh. The commentary defends the Hanafi view by interpreting the hadith's 'taking' as requiring the killer's consent.
The Shafi'i position is based on the same hadith but with a different emphasis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل قال واذا اصطلح القاتل واولياء القتيل على مال سقط القصاص ووجب المال قليلا كان أو كثيرا لقوله تعالى فمن عفى له من اخيه شئ الآية على ما قيل نزلت الآية فى الصلح وقوله عليه السلام من قتل له قتيل الحديث والمراد والله اعلم الاخذ بالرضا على ما بيناه وهو الصلح بعينه ولانه حق ثابت للورثة يجرى فيه الاسقاط عفو ا فكذا تعويضا لاشتماله على احسان الا ولياء واحياء القاتل فيجوز بالتراضى ترجمہ ی فصل ہے مصالحت وغیرہ کے بیان میں قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب قاتل اور مقتول کے اولیاء نے مصالحت کر لی کسی مال پر تو قصاص ساقط ہو گیا اور مال واجب ہوگیا قلیل ہو یا زیادہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان فمن عفی لہ من اخيه شئ الایہ کی وجہ سے اس قول کے مطابق جو کہا گیا ہے کہ آیت صلح کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے۔ اور نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان من قتل له قتيل (الحدیث) کی وجہ سے۔ اور حدیث کی مراد واللہ اعلم قاتل کی رضامندی سے لینا ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور (یہی بعینہ رضامندی سے لینا ) صلح ہے اور اس لئے کہ قصاص ورثہ کا ایسا حق ثابت ہے جس میں معافی کے طریقہ پر اسقاط جاری ہوتا ہے تو ایسے ہی عوض لینے کے طریقہ پر اسقاط جاری ہوگا ) تعویض کے مشتمل ہونے کی وجہ سے اولیاء کے احسان پر اور قاتل کے احیاء پر تو تعویض رضا مندی سے جائز ہے۔ تشریح حقوق چار قسم کے ہوتے ہیں :-
- خالص اللہ کا حق ہے۔
-۲- خالص بندہ کا حق
- دونوں کا حق لیکن حق اللہ اس میں غالب ہو
-۴ دونوں کا حق لیکن اس میں بندہ کا حق غالب ہو جیسے نماز ، اموال مملوک، حد قذف قصاص تو قصاص میں بندہ کا حق غالب ہے اسی وجہ سے بندہ کے معاف کر دینے سے معاف ہو جائیگا حدقذف معاف نہ ہوگی۔
بہر حال جب قاتل اور مقتول کے ورثہ نے یہ مصالحت کر لی کہ اتنے مال کے بدلہ میں صلح ہے اور قصاص معاف ہے تو اب قصاص ختم ہو گیا صرف دو مال واجب ہوگا جس پر مصالحت ہوئی ہے خواہ وہ مال قلبل ہو یا کثیر صلح کا ثبوت قرآن سے ہے، فمن غـفـى لـه من اخيه شئى فاتباع بالمعروف واداء اليه باحسان (وہ قاتل) جس کو اس کے بھائی ( مقتول) کی طرس سے کچھ معافی دی جائے۔ ( بواسطہ اولیاء ) تو تابعداری کرنی چاہیئے دستور کے موافق اور خوبی کے ساتھ اس کو ادا کرنا چاہیئے ۔ یعنی مقتول کے وارثوں میں سے اگر بعض بھی خون کو معاف کر دیں تو اب قاتل کو قصاص میں قتل تو نہیں کر سکتے بلکہ دیکھیں گے کہ ان وارثوں نے معاف کس طرح کیا ہے محض ثواب کی غرض سے بلا معاوضہ مالی معاف کیا ہے یا دیت شرعی اور بطور مصالحت کسی مقدار مال پر راضی ہو کر صرف قصاص سے دست برداری دی ہے۔ اول صورت میں قاتل ان وارثوں کے مطالبہ سے بالکل سبکدوش ہو جائیگا اور دوسری صورت میں قاتل کو چاہیئے کہ وہ معاوضہ اچھی طرح نیت اور خوشدلی کے ساتھ ادا کرے۔ مسلح کا ثبوت حدیث سے من قتل له قتيل اما ان يعفو واما ان يقتل یعنی جس شخص کا کوئی ولی قتل کر دیا گیا تو اس کو اختیار ہے چاہے معاف کر دے اور چاہے قصاص لے لے اور مال کے بدلہ معاف کرنا بھی عفو ہے۔ سوال ماقبل میں یہ مسئلہ گذر چکا ہے کہ اگر اولیا ء دیت لینے پر راضی ہو جائیں اور قاتل راضی نہ ہو بلکہ وہ قصاص پر راضی ہو تو اولیاء بغیر اس کی رضامندی کے دیت نہیں لے سکتے۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک اختیار صرف اولیاء کو ہے قاتل کو نہیں ہے اس حدیث سے امام شافعی کی تائید ہوتی ہے؟
جواب حدیث میں بھی لینے سے وہی لینا مراد ہے جو قاتل کی رضامندی سے ہو۔ اور جو لینا رضا مندی سے ہوگا اسی کو تو صلح
Chapter on compromise. He said: And when the killer and the heirs of the slain compromise upon wealth, qisas drops and the wealth becomes due, whether little or much, due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'then whoever is forgiven by his brother something...' the verse is said to have been revealed concerning compromise, and due to his saying peace be upon him: 'whoever has a slain relative...' the hadith. And the intention, Allah knows best, is taking with consent, as we have explained, and that is compromise itself. And because it is a right established for the heirs in which dropping by way of pardon operates, similarly dropping by way of compensation operates because it contains kindness to the heirs and revival of the killer, so it is permissible by mutual consent. Commentary: This is a chapter on compromise etc. Al-Quduri said: When the killer and the heirs of the slain compromise upon some wealth, qisas drops and the wealth becomes due, little or much, due to Allah's command 'then whoever is forgiven by his brother something...' the verse, according to the saying that the verse was revealed regarding compromise, and due to the Prophet's (peace be upon him) saying 'whoever has a slain relative' the hadith. And the intention of the hadith, Allah knows best, is taking with the consent of the killer as we have explained, and that is compromise itself. And because qisas is a right established for the heirs in which dropping by way of pardon operates, similarly dropping by way of compensation operates because it contains kindness to the heirs and revival of the killer, so compensation by mutual consent is permissible. Commentary: Rights are of four types: 1) Pure right of Allah, 2) Pure right of the servant, 3) Right of both but the right of Allah predominates, 4) Right of both but the right of the servant predominates, like prayer, owned property, hadd of qadhf, qisas. So in qisas, the right of the servant predominates, therefore it is waived by the servant's pardon, whereas hadd of qadhf is not waived. In any case, when the killer and the heirs of the slain compromise that there is compromise for such wealth and qisas is pardoned, then qisas ends and only the wealth agreed upon becomes due, whether that wealth is little or much. The proof of compromise is from the Quran: 'Then whoever is forgiven by his brother something, then follow in kindness and pay to him with goodness.' That is, if some of the heirs forgive the blood, then the killer cannot be killed in qisas; rather they will see how the heirs forgave: whether purely for reward without financial compensation, or they agreed on legal blood money or compromise on some amount, thereby relinquishing qisas. In the first case, the killer is completely discharged from their claim; in the second case, the killer must pay the compensation with good intention and cheerfully. Proof from hadith: 'Whoever has a slain relative, either he pardons or he kills.' Meaning, the person whose relative is killed has the choice: to pardon or to take qisas. And pardoning in exchange for wealth is also forgiveness. A previous issue: if the heirs agree to take blood money but the killer does not consent and wants qisas, the heirs cannot take blood money without his consent. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the choice is only for the heirs, not the killer. Does this hadith support Imam al-Shafi'i? Answer: In the hadith, 'taking' also refers to taking with the consent of the killer. And what is taken with consent is compromise.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a chapter (fasl) from the matn of al-Quduri with commentary, establishing the ruling and evidence for compromise (sulh) between the killer and the heirs of the victim. The ruling: When they compromise on a specific wealth, qisas drops and that wealth becomes due, regardless of amount. The evidence is both Quranic and Prophetic. The Quranic verse 'فمن عفى له من اخيه شئ' is interpreted to refer to compromise. The hadith gives the heirs the option to pardon or to kill, but the Hanafi school interprets 'pardon' as including pardon with compensation, and requires the killer's consent for any financial taking. The commentary then categorizes rights: qisas is a right where the servant's right predominates, hence heirs can waive it. The text also responds to a potential objection from Imam al-Shafi'i's view that only heirs have choice; the Hanafi answer is that the hadith implies consent from the killer as well. The passage notes four types of rights to contextualize why qisas can be waived.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A compromise agreement between the killer and the heirs, usually involving payment of wealth in exchange for dropping qisas.
عفو (afw): Pardon or forgiveness by the heirs, which can be for free or in exchange for compensation (sulh).
اسقاط (isqat): The dropping or abrogation of a right, here qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is required for a valid compromise (sulh) between the killer and the heirs?
A) The heirs must agree to accept blood money of at least the full diya.
B) The killer must confess to the murder.
C) Both the killer and the heirs must consent to the agreement.
D) The judge must approve the amount of blood money.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates compromise (sulh) in qisas only when both the killer and the heirs willingly agree, and once done, qisas is dropped and the agreed wealth becomes wajib.

Permissibility of Sulh in Qisas and Classification of Rights
Explaining the nature of rights and permissibility of compromise in qisas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits compromise (sulh) in qisas and distinguish the rights classification that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Compromise in qisas is valid because the servant's right predominates.

In this passage, the author establishes that qisas is primarily a right of the victim's heirs, which they may waive or accept compensation for. By classifying rights into four categories, he shows that where the servant's right dominates, the servant can pardon or compromise. The Quranic verse and hadith provide the scriptural basis for sulh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm is. Here, the act is compromise (sulh) in qisas – accepting compensation instead of retaliation. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) and becomes binding once agreed.
The passage explicitly states 'so compensation with consent is permissible.'
2
Locate the classification of rights
The author divides rights into four categories. Identify which category qisas belongs to. The passage states: 'qisas is a right of both Allah and the servant, but the servant's right predominates.'
This classification is key to understanding why the servant (heir) can drop qisas.
3
Understand the implications of the classification
Because the servant's right predominates, the servant can waive it – either completely (pardon) or in exchange for something (sulh). Contrast this with rights where Allah's right predominates, which cannot be waived by humans (e.g., hadd of qadhf).
The passage explicitly compares qisas with hadd qadhf.
4
Cite the Quranic proof and explain its legal implication
The verse 'فمن عفی له من أخيه شيء' indicates that when some forgiveness is given, the killer must pay with good conduct. This shows that taking compensation is permissible and even encouraged.
The Hanafi usul principle: the imperative 'اتباع' implies obligation to pay after forgiveness.
5
Note the hadith proof and the requirement of mutual consent
The hadith gives the heir a choice to forgive or kill. The Hanafi school interprets 'forgive' to include forgiving in exchange for property (sulh), but requires the killer's consent because it is a contract. This distinguishes the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i.
The passage emphasizes 'taking with consent' as the meaning of the hadith.

مطابق جو کہا گیا ہے کہ آیت صلح کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے۔ اور نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان من قتل له قتيل (الحدیث) کی وجہ سے۔ اور حدیث کی مراد واللہ اعلم قاتل کی رضامندی سے لینا ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور (یہی بعینہ رضامندی سے لینا ) صلح ہے اور اس لئے کہ قصاص ورثہ کا ایسا حق ثابت ہے جس میں معافی کے طریقہ پر اسقاط جاری ہوتا ہے تو ایسے ہی عوض لینے کے طریقہ پر اسقاط جاری ہوگا ) تعویض کے مشتمل ہونے کی وجہ سے اولیاء کے احسان پر اور قاتل کے احیاء پر تو تعویض رضا مندی سے جائز ہے۔ تشریح حقوق چار قسم کے ہوتے ہیں :-
- خالص اللہ کا حق ہے۔
-۲- خالص بندہ کا حق
- دونوں کا حق لیکن حق اللہ اس میں غالب ہو

According to what has been said: the verse of peace was revealed concerning this, and due to the Prophet's command 'Whoever has a relative killed' (hadith). And the meaning of the hadith, and Allah knows best, is taking with the killer's consent, according to the detail we have explained. And taking with consent is exactly peace. And because qisas is a right established for the heirs in which dropping applies through forgiveness, similarly dropping applies through taking compensation, due to the inclusion of compensation for the favor of the heirs and the preservation of the killer's life. So compensation with consent is permissible. Explanation: Rights are of four types: 1) Pure right of Allah. 2) Pure right of the servant. 3) Right of both but Allah's right predominates. 4) Right of both but the servant's right predominates, like salah, owned property, hadd of qadhf, qisas. So in qisas, the servant's right predominates; therefore, if the servant pardons, it is pardoned, whereas hadd of qadhf is not pardoned. In any case, when the killer and the heirs of the victim compromise that there is peace for such and such property and qisas is forgiven, then qisas ends and only that property becomes obligatory for which the compromise was made, whether little or much. The proof of peace is from the Quran: 'Then whoever is granted remission from his brother, let the pursuit be with good conduct and payment with goodness.' That is, if some of the heirs forgive the blood, then the killer cannot be killed as retribution; rather, it will be seen how the heirs forgave: whether purely for reward without monetary compensation, or for legal diyah, or by way of compromise agreeing to some amount of property and merely relinquishing qisas. In the first case, the killer is completely absolved from the claim of the heirs; in the second case, the killer must pay the compensation with good intention and cheerfulness. Proof of peace from hadith: 'Whoever has a relative killed has the choice either to forgive or to kill.' That is, the person whose relative was killed has the option either to forgive or to take qisas. And forgiving for property is also forgiveness.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the permissibility of compromise (sulh) in qisas. The author begins by stating the basis: the Quranic verse on peace and the hadith. He then classifies rights into four categories to show that qisas is predominantly a right of the servant, hence can be waived. The main ruling: if heirs and killer agree on a sum, qisas drops and the sum becomes wajib. The proof from Quran (2:178) and Hadith is cited. The commentary clarifies the options: either free pardon or compromise. The passage follows the author's order: first the general principle, then the classification, then the specific ruling, then the proofs.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): Compromise or settlement between the killer and heirs to forgo qisas for a sum of money.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional killing or injury.
عفو (afw): Pardon without compensation or for a consideration.
دیت (diyah): Blood money prescribed by law for homicide or injury, not fixed by contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Qisas is a right where the servant's right predominates, making compromise (sulh) valid with mutual consent, supported by Quran and Hadith.

Division of Compromise Amount: Free Man and Slave Jointly Kill
Ruling on division of compromise amount in joint murder by free man and slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the division of a compromise amount when a free man and a slave jointly commit murder, and explain the legal basis for equal liability.

Core Idea
In sulh for qisas, liability splits equally between free and master because the contract is attributed to both.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Imam Muhammad regarding a joint murder by a free man and a slave. The heirs accept a compromise amount in lieu of qisas. The key legal question is how the payment is apportioned. The answer reveals an important principle of contractual liability in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the contract
Who commissioned the compromise? The free man and the slave's master. The slave himself is not a party because he lacks legal capacity.
The agent is acting for both.
2
Recognize the attribution of the contract
The contract of sulh is attributed to both the free man and the master, as they both gave authorization.
Attribution does not distinguish between free and slave status.
3
Derive the equal division
Since the contract is equally attributed, the liability for the compromise amount is divided equally between the free man and the master.
Each pays 500 out of 1000.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آزاد اور غلام نے ملکر قتل کیا اور دونوں نے ایک ہزار پر مصالحت کے لئے ورثاء کے پاس بھیجا ورثاء مقتول نے ہزار پر مصالحت کر لی کتنی رقم کس پر آئے گی
وان كان القاتل حراو عبد أفامر الحر ومولى العبد رجلا بان يصالح عن دمهما على الف درهم ففعل فالالف على الحر والمولى نصفان لان عقد الصلح اضيف اليهما
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور اگر قاتل آزاد اور ایک غلام ہو پس آزاد نے اور غلام کے مولیٰ نے کسی شخص کو حکم دیا کہ وہ ان دونوں کے خون کی جانب سے ہزار درہم پر مصالحت کرے پس اس نے کر لی تو ہزار درہم آزاد اور آقا پر آدھے آدھے ہوں گے اس لئے کہ عقد صلح کی اضافت ان دونوں کی جانب ہے۔
A free man and a slave jointly committed murder, and both sent (someone) to the heirs to compromise for one thousand. The heirs of the victim agreed on one thousand. How much will be paid by whom? And if the killer is a free man and a slave, and the free man and the master of the slave commissioned a man to compromise on behalf of their blood for one thousand dirhams, and he did so, then the one thousand is divided equally between the free man and the master, because the contract of sulh was attributed to both of them. Translation: Muhammad said: If the killer is a free man and a slave, then the free man and the master of the slave ordered a man to compromise on behalf of their blood for one thousand dirhams, and he did so, then the one thousand dirhams will be half and half on the free man and the master, because the contract of sulh is attributed to both.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This is a specific legal case (mas'ala) from Imam Muhammad. Two persons jointly commit a murder: one free man and one slave (owned by a master). They both send an agent to the victim's heirs to offer a compromise of 1000 dirhams in exchange for forgiveness of qisas. The heirs accept. The question is: how is the 1000 divided between the free man and the slave's master? The ruling: equally, 500 each. The reason is that the contract of sulh is attributed to both the free man and the master (who represents the slave's liability since the slave cannot own property). The free man pays his half, and the master pays the other half on behalf of the slave. This shows that the liability is shared equally regardless of whether one is free and the other is a slave.

Key Terms
غلام (ghulam): A male slave owned by a master, not a legal person capable of owning property.
مولیٰ (mawla): Master or owner of the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the given case, if the free man and the slave's master compromise for 1000 dirhams, how much does the free man pay?
A) Nothing
B) 250 dirhams
C) 500 dirhams
D) 1000 dirhams

Key Takeaway
When a free man and a slave jointly commit murder and a compromise is reached, the liability for the payment is split equally between the free man and the slave's master because the contract of sulh is attributed to both.

Qisas — Retaliation

Ruling on the Amount and Immediate Payment of Sulh Compensation in Qisas
States ruling on sulh compensation amount and its immediate obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that any agreed amount of sulh compensation is valid and determine that payment is immediate if not specified.

Core Idea
Any sulh compensation amount is valid; if not specified, it is due immediately by default.

When heirs compromise qisas for compensation (sulh), the amount is not fixed by text. Both parties may agree on any sum, however small or large. If they do not mention payment timing, the compensation is due immediately because it arises from a contract. This lesson explains the proof and the default rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that in sulh for qisas, the amount of compensation (mal al-sulh) can be small or large, and if not specified, payment is immediate.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is that there is no fixed textual limit (nass muqaddar) for the amount, so it is delegated to the parties' agreement, analogized to khul' and other contracts.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The absence of a textual specification means the matter is left to mutual consent; the analogy to khul' strengthens this because khul' also has no fixed compensation.
4
Apply the default rule for contractual obligations
When a contract obligates payment, the default is immediate (hal), like dower and sale price, unlike diyah which is imposed by law and may be deferred.
This distinction between contractual and non-contractual obligations is key.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may impose minimum amounts or require specific payment terms; Hanafis rely on the absence of text and analogy.

نیز قصاص اولیاء کا حق ہے جس کی وجہ سے اولیاء کو حق ہے کہ اپنا حق مفت میں معاف کردیں یا کچھ عوض لے کر معاف کر دیں پھر اس عوض لینے میں فریقین کا فائدہ ہے اولیاء کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ ان کی طرف سے قاتل پر احسان رکھا گیا اور قاتل کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ اس کی جان بچ گئی لہذا دونوں کی رضا مندی درکار ہے۔

تشریح ما صلح کی مقدار کتنی ہو تو چونکہ نص میں اس کی مقدار وارد نہیں ہوتی اس لئے یہ ولی اور قاتل کے اتفاق پر موقوف ہے خواہ قلیل ہو یا کثیر جیسے ضلع میں اور مال کے بدلہ اعتاق میں یہی صورت ہے۔ اور اگر انہوں نے نقد اور ادھار کا کوئی ذکر نہیں کیا تو مال نقد واجب ہوگا کیونکہ قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جو مال کسی عقد سے برضامندی طرفین واجب ہو تو وہ فی الحال واجب الادا ہو گا۔ اور جو عقد سے واجب نہ ہو وہ فی الحال واجب نہ ہوگا اور یہ مال عقد سے واجب ہوا ہے لہذا فی الحال واجب الادا ہے اور دیت قسط وار واجب ہے کیونکہ اس کا وجوب عقد سے نہیں بلکہ شریعت کے واجب کرنے سے ہے۔
Also, qisas is the right of the heirs, therefore the heirs have the right to forgive their right for free or to forgive for some compensation. Then, in taking this compensation, there is benefit for both parties: the benefit for the heirs is that favor is shown to the killer from their side, and the benefit for the killer is that his life is spared. Hence, mutual consent is required. The compensation in sulh, whether small or large, is equal (in validity). And the small and large in it are equal because there is no fixed text (nass muqaddar) for it, so it is delegated to their agreement, like khul' and others. And if they did not mention immediate or deferred, then it is immediate because it is wealth obligated by contract, and the principle in such cases is immedacy, like dower and price, unlike diyah because it is not obligated by contract. Commentary: The amount of compensation in sulh: since its quantity is not mentioned in the text, it depends on the agreement of the guardian and the killer, whether small or large, as in khul' and the compensation for manumission. And if they did not mention cash or credit, then the wealth is obligated as cash because the principle is that wealth that becomes obligatory by a contract with mutual consent is immediately due. And that which is not obligatory by contract is not immediately due. This wealth is obligated by contract, so it is immediately due. Diyah is obligated in installments because its obligation is not by contract but by the law's imposition.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the amount and payment terms of compensation (mal al-sulh) in a compromise for qisas. The author first establishes that the heirs have the right to pardon the killer either for free or for compensation, and that both parties' consent is necessary. Then he addresses the quantity of compensation: the Arabic matn states that small and large amounts are equal, meaning there is no prescribed minimum or maximum. The proof for this is the absence of a fixed textual limit (nass muqaddar), so the matter is left to mutual agreement, analogous to khul' (divorce by redemption) and other contracts. Further, if the parties do not specify payment as immediate or deferred, the payment is considered immediate. The reasoning is that this wealth becomes obligatory by a contract (the sulh contract), and the default rule for obligations arising from contracts is immedacy, like the dower in marriage or the price in a sale. This is contrasted with diyah (blood money), which is not contractual but imposed by Islamic law, and thus may be paid in installments. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the guardian (wali) and killer can agree on any amount, and if no time is set, it is due immediately.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A compromise agreement between the heirs and the killer to forgo qisas in exchange for compensation.
مال صلح (mal al-sulh): The compensation paid by the killer to the heirs in a sulh agreement.
نص مقدر (nass muqaddar): A fixed textual limit or prescribed amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the heirs and the killer agree on a sulh for qisas but do not specify whether the compensation is to be paid immediately or later, when is it due according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is due immediately because it is a contractual obligation.
B) It is due after one year, like diyah.
C) It is due only when the killer is released.
D) It is due in three installments.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, sulh compensation in qisas has no fixed amount and is immediately payable if not specified.

Division of Sulh Payment in Joint Killing by Free Man and Slave
Presents case of joint killing and how sulh amount is split

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on division of sulh payment when a free man and a slave jointly kill, and explain the qiyas that supports equal division between the free man and the slave's master.

Core Idea
In joint killing, sulh is split equally between free man and slave's master because the contract is attributed to both.

This passage from Imam Muhammad's work presents a case where a free man and a slave, through an agent, settle with the victim's heirs for a lump sum. The question is who bears the payment. The Hanafi ruling is that the free man and the slave's master share equally. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, which is based on the principle of attribution (idafah) and analogy to joint purchase.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and legal act
Identify the free man (Zaid), the slave (Bakr), the master (Khalid), and the agent (Zahid). The legal act is sulh (compromise) through an agent to avoid qisas.
2
Locate the ruling and the dalil
The matn states: 'the thousand is half on the free man and half on the master.' The dalil is 'because the contract of sulh is attributed to both of them.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The attribution (idafah) of the agent's act to both principals means the liability is joint. The analogy (qiyas) to two persons buying a slave shows equal division of the price.
4
Apply the principle to the case
Since the agent acted for both principals, the obligation falls on both equally, regardless of the slave's personal incapacity.
5
Note the broader principle
The rule illustrates that in Hanafi law, the action of an agent is attributed to the principal, and joint principals share liability equally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح زید آزاد ہے اور بکر خالد کا غلام ہے زید اور بکر نے ساجد کو عد قتل کر دیا جس کی وجہ سے ان دونوں پر قصاص واجب ہوا لیکن ان دونوں نے زاہد کو وکیل بنایا کہ وہ ساجد کے ورثہ سے گفتگو کرے اور ہزار درہم کے بدلہ مصالحت کرے تا کہ دونوں قاتل ( زید اور بکر ) کی جان بچ جائے ۔ بہر حال زاہد نے گفتگو کر لی اور ہزار درہم پر مصالحت ہوگئی
سوال تو اب سوال یہ ہے کہ وہ ہزار درہم کون دے گا ؟ جواب تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ زید اور خالد دونوں آدھا آدھا ادا کریں گے کیونکہ زاہد وکیل کا فعل ان دونوں کا فعل شمار ہوگا کیونکہ زاہد تو غیر معبر محض ہے جس کو اضافت الی الاصیل کی حاجت پیش آتی ہے اور اصیل یہ دونوں ہیں۔ اور اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے دو شخصوں نے ایک غلام خریدا تو وہ ان دونوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا اور شمن بھی آدھا آدھا واجب ہوگا کیونکہ ثمن غلام کا بدل ہے۔
And if the killer is a free man and a slave, then the free man and the master of the slave command a man to compromise on their behalf for their blood for a thousand dirhams, and he does so, then the thousand is half on the free man and half on the master, because the contract of sulh is attributed to both of them. Translation: Muhammad said: And if the killer is a free man and a slave, then the free man and the master of the slave command a person to compromise on behalf of their blood for a thousand dirhams, and he does so, then the thousand dirhams will be half on the free man and half on the master, because the contract of sulh is attributed to both of them. Commentary: Zaid is free and Bakr is Khalid's slave. Zaid and Bakr intentionally killed Sajid, so qisas became obligatory on both. But they appointed Zahid as their agent to negotiate with Sajid's heirs and compromise for a thousand dirhams to save their lives. Zahid negotiated and the compromise was made for a thousand dirhams. The question is: who will pay the thousand dirhams? The answer: Zaid and Khalid will each pay half, because the action of the agent Zahid is considered their action, since Zahid is merely a conduit who needs attribution to the principals, and these two are the principals. An example: if two persons buy a slave, then the slave is half and half between them, and the price is also half and half, because the price is the exchange for the slave.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a case ruling from Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) regarding a joint killing by a free man and a slave, and the resulting sulh (compromise) with the heirs. The matn states that if the free man and the slave's master authorize a person to compromise on their behalf for a fixed sum (here 1000 dirhams), the agent does so, and the sum is divided equally between the free man and the master. The reasoning is that the contract of sulh is attributed to both of them as principals; the agent is merely a representative, so the obligation falls on the principals. The Urdu commentary elaborates with an example: Zaid (free) and Bakr (slave of Khalid) kill Sajid intentionally, making qisas obligatory. They appoint Zahid as agent to settle with the heirs for 1000 dirhams. The question is who pays. The answer: Zaid and Khalid each pay 500 dirhams. This is because the agent's action is attributed to the principals. An analogy is given of two persons buying a slave: both are equally liable for the price.

Key Terms
مولیٰ (mawla): Master of a slave.
اضافت (idafah): Attribution of the contract to the principals; the agent's action is referred back to them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The free man pays the full amount because the slave is not liable.
B) The free man and the slave himself each pay half.
C) The free man and the slave's master each pay half.
D) The heirs can choose to collect from either party.

Key Takeaway
In joint killings settled by sulh, the payment is split equally between the free man and the master, not the slave, because the contract is attributed to the principals.

Qisas — Retaliation

Effect of One Heir Pardoning Qisas: Hanafi View and Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on qisas and spouses' rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on one heir's pardon of qisas, identify the Maliki/Shafi'i objection, and explain the practical difference between the schools.

Core Idea
Qisas is a joint right; one heir's pardon extinguishes it for all — spouses included.

This passage addresses a critical question in qisas law: what happens when one joint heir pardons the right to qisas? The Hanafi ruling is that the right to qisas falls entirely, and the remaining heirs receive their share of diyah. The passage then delves into a dispute with Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the inclusion of spouses. Understanding this ruling requires appreciating the Hanafi doctrine that qisas is a joint right of all heirs, and that inheritance includes both lineage and cause-based rights.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two components: (1) One heir's pardon drops qisas for all heirs, (2) Spouses have a right in qisas and diyah.
The core ruling is that qisas is a joint right.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Malik and Shafi'i hold that spouses have no right in qisas or diyah, so their pardon is irrelevant.
The disagreement is specifically about spouses.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
They argue that inheritance (khilafah) is based on lineage (nasab), not on a cause (sabab) like marriage, because the cause ends with death.
Their proof is a dalil naqli from the nature of inheritance.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is implicit: inheritance and the right to qisas/diyah follow all heirs, whether by lineage or cause. The joint right encompasses all heirs.
The Hanafis do not limit the right to lineage alone.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi law, if a spouse pardons, qisas drops for all and diyah is distributed. Under Maliki/Shafi'i, the spouse's pardon has no effect on qisas, and the blood relatives can still demand qisas.
This has real consequences for the killer and heirs.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ اور جب کہ شرکاء میں سے ایک نے خون معاف کر دیا یا اپنے حصہ کی جانب سے کسی عوض پر مصالحت کر لی تو باقی لوگوں کا حق قصاص ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور ان کے لئے دیت میں سے ان کا حصہ ہوگا۔ اور اس کی اصل یہ ہے کہ قصاص تمام در شا کا حق ہے اور ایسے ہی دیت بخلاف مالک شافعی کے زوجین کے حق میں۔ ان دونوں کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وراثت تو خلافت ہے اور خلافت نسب کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے نہ کہ سب کی سبب کے منقطع ہو جانے کی وجہ سے موت کے ذریعہ ۔

And when one of the partners pardons the blood or compromises his share for compensation, the right of the rest to qisas falls, and they have their share of the diyah. The basis of this is that qisas is the right of all the heirs, and similarly diyah. Contrary to Malik and Shafi'i regarding spouses: their proof is that inheritance is a replacement (khilafah), and replacement is by lineage (nasab) not by cause (sabab), because it is severed by death. Translation: And when one of the partners pardons the blood or compromises on his share for some compensation, then the rest's right to qisas is dropped, and they have their share of the diyah. The basis of this is that qisas is the right of all the heirs, and similarly diyah. Contrary to Malik and Shafi'i regarding spouses: their proof is that inheritance is a replacement, and replacement is by lineage not by cause, because it is severed by death. Commentary: When one of those for whom the right of qisas was established pardons his right, then the remaining guardians (awliya') cannot take qisas, but they can take their share of diyah. For example, Zaid has five sons and no other heir. Zaid is intentionally killed, so qisas is obligatory. But one son forgives his right, then qisas falls and only diyah is obligatory. The form is that one-fifth of the full diyah is subtracted, and four-fifths are divided equally among the four sons. It is stated as a principle that since qisas is the right of all heirs, and when it is the right of all, each has the right to take qisas or forgive. So when one forgives his right, qisas falls. In our view, all heirs have a right in qisas and diyah, whether their inheritance is by lineage or by cause. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i differ, saying that spouses have no right in qisas and diyah, because inheritance is a replacement, and replacement is based on lineage, not cause, because cause ceases with death.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the effect of one heir pardoning qisas and the inclusion of spouses in the right to qisas and diyah. The Hanafi ruling is that if one of the joint heirs (shuraka') pardons his share of the blood or compromises it for compensation, the right of all other heirs to exact qisas is dropped. However, they are not left without remedy; they receive their proportionate share of the diyah (blood money). The proof is that qisas is a joint right of all heirs, and the exercise of the right by one party affects the whole. The example given: a deceased has five sons; one son pardons; the remaining four cannot demand qisas but each gets his share of the diyah (four-fifths divided among them). Then the passage addresses a disagreement with Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether spouses (husband or wife) have any right in qisas and diyah. The Hanafis hold that spouses do have such rights because they inherit by cause (sabab, i.e., marriage) and inheritance is a form of succession that applies to all heirs, whether by lineage or cause. The opposing view (Malik and Shafi'i) argues that inheritance is a replacement (khilafah) based on lineage (nasab), and since the marital tie is a cause that ends with death, spouses do not enter into the right of qisas. The Hanafi response, implicit in the text, is that the right to qisas and diyah follows inheritance generally, not limited to lineage.

Key Terms
شرکاء (shuraka'): Joint heirs sharing the right to qisas or diyah.
خلفت (khilafah): Replacement or succession; inheritance is a form of replacement of the deceased by the heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a married woman is killed intentionally, and her husband pardons his share of qisas, what happens to the right of qisas for the deceased's blood relatives?
A) The blood relatives can still demand qisas because the husband is not a blood relative.
B) The blood relatives' right to qisas also falls, and they receive their share of diyah.
C) The husband has no right in qisas, so his pardon is irrelevant.
D) The blood relatives can demand qisas but the husband forfeits his share of diyah.

Key Takeaway
One heir's pardon of qisas extinguishes the right for all heirs under Hanafi law; spouses are included as joint holders of the right.

Joint Liability of Multiple Murderers in Settlement Through Agent
Ruling on joint murderers' liability when settling through agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that joint murderers are equally liable for a settlement amount negotiated through a common agent, and explain the qiyas that supports it.

Core Idea
Joint murderers share settlement equally when acting through one agent, just as joint buyers share the price.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario from the Hanafi fiqh: two murderers jointly appoint an agent to negotiate a settlement with the victim's heirs to avoid qisas. The key question is how the settlement amount is divided. The Hanafi ruling is that it is split equally between the murderers, based on the principle that the agent's act is attributed to all principals equally. This ruling is supported by an analogy to joint purchase, where the price is shared equally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Read the passage carefully: Zayd (free) and Bakr (slave) kill Sajid, making qisas wajib. They appoint Zahid as agent to settle with heirs for 1000 dirhams. Settlement is reached. The question is who pays the 1000 dirhams.
Note that both murderers are jointly liable for qisas, but here they seek to avoid it via settlement.
2
Extract the ruling
The answer given: Zayd and Bakr each pay half (500 dirhams each). The text states this is because the agent's act counts as the act of both principals.
3
Identify the qiyas (analogy)
The author uses the example of two persons jointly buying a slave: the slave and the price are shared equally. This is the original case (asl). The new case (far') is the joint murderers settling through an agent. The illa (effective cause) is that in both cases, the obligation arises from a joint action and the compensation is for a joint liability.
In joint purchase, the price is compensation for the slave; in joint murder, the settlement amount is compensation for the lives (blood).
4
Understand the agency principle
The agent (Zahid) is a mere intermediary (غير معبر); his actions are attributed to the principals (Zayd and Bakr). Therefore, the settlement is considered as if both murderers made it themselves, leading to equal liability.
This is a key Hanafi principle regarding agency.
5
Apply to variations
Consider if the murderers had acted separately or appointed separate agents. The ruling might differ. This lesson focuses on the joint appointment scenario.
The passage does not cover other scenarios, but you can test understanding by asking what would happen if one murderer was wealthy and the other poor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زید آزاد ہے اور بکر خالد کا غلام ہے زید اور بکر نے ساجد کو عد قتل کر دیا جس کی وجہ سے ان دونوں پر قصاص واجب ہوا لیکن ان دونوں نے زاہد کو وکیل بنایا کہ وہ ساجد کے ورثہ سے گفتگو کرے اور ہزار درہم کے بدلہ مصالحت کرے تا کہ دونوں قاتل ( زید اور بکر ) کی جان بچ جائے ۔ بہر حال زاہد نے گفتگو کر لی اور ہزار درہم پر مصالحت ہوگئی سوال تو اب سوال یہ ہے کہ وہ ہزار درہم کون دے گا ؟ جواب تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ زید اور خالد دونوں آدھا آدھا ادا کریں گے کیونکہ زاہد وکیل کا فعل ان دونوں کا فعل شمار ہوگا کیونکہ زاہد تو غیر معبر محض ہے جس کو اضافت الی الاصیل کی حاجت پیش آتی ہے اور اصیل یہ دونوں ہیں۔ اور اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے دو شخصوں نے ایک غلام خریدا تو وہ ان دونوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا اور شمن بھی آدھا آدھا واجب ہوگا کیونکہ ثمن غلام کا بدل ہے۔
Zayd is free and Bakr is Khalid's slave. Zayd and Bakr intentionally killed Sajid, so qisas became wajib upon both. But they appointed Zahid as their agent to speak with Sajid's heirs and make a settlement for one thousand dirhams to save the lives of both killers. So Zahid spoke and a settlement was made for one thousand dirhams. The question is: who will pay the thousand dirhams? The answer given is that Zayd and Khalid will each pay half, because the act of the agent Zahid counts as the act of both, since Zahid is merely a mediator who needs attribution to the principal, and the principals are these two. An example is like when two persons buy a slave, the slave is half-half between them, and the price is also wajib half-half, because the price is compensation for the slave.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This is a commentary (تشریح) on a specific scenario. It presents a ruling on the liability of joint murderers when they authorize a single agent to negotiate a settlement with the victim's heirs. The scenario: Zayd (free) and Bakr (a slave belonging to Khalid) intentionally kill Sajid, making both liable for qisas. They appoint Zahid as agent to settle with the heirs for 1000 dirhams. The question: who pays the 1000 dirhams? The answer: Zayd and Bakr each pay half. The reasoning: the agent's act is attributed to both principals equally, because the agent is a mere intermediary (غير معبر) who requires attribution to the principal. The text provides an analogy: when two persons jointly purchase a slave, they share ownership and the price equally, because the price is compensation for the slave. Similarly, here the settlement amount is compensation for the lives (blood), and both murderers are equally liable since they jointly caused the death. The ruling does not discuss whether the slave Bakr's master (Khalid) is liable; it assumes Bakr has means or that his master may pay on his behalf. The key principle is that joint murderers are equally liable for settlements made through a common agent.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakil): An agent appointed to negotiate settlement with the victim's heirs.
مصالحت (musalahah): Settlement between murderers and heirs for monetary compensation in lieu of qisas.
ثمن (thaman): Price or compensation paid; here, the settlement amount.
غیر معبر (ghayr mu'abbar): Literally 'not a barrier'; here, it means the agent is a mere intermediary whose actions are attributed to the principal.

B) The settlement amount is compensation for a joint act, just as the price in a joint purchase is compensation for the jointly purchased item
C) The murderers are both free
D) The victim's heirs agreed to the settlement

Key Takeaway
Joint murderers who jointly appoint an agent to settle with the victim's heirs are equally liable for the settlement amount, by analogy to joint purchase of a slave.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Forgiveness by One Heir and Spouses' Right in Qisas and Diyah
Ruling on forgiveness and Hanafi dispute with Malik/Shafi'i on spouses' inclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that one heir's forgiveness drops qisas for all heirs and state the Hanafi position that spouses inherit qisas and diyah, distinguishing it from the Maliki/Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
One heir's forgiveness drops qisas for all; spouses inherit qisas and diyah in Hanafi law.

The right to qisas belongs to all heirs collectively. When one heir forgives his share, the retaliation right extinguishes for everyone, but the killer must still pay diyah proportionate to the remaining heirs' shares. A key dispute arises: Do spouses (husband/wife) have any right in qisas and diyah? The Hanafi school affirms, while Malik and Shafi'i deny, based on different conceptions of inheritance. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the inter-madhhab debate.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on forgiveness
The text begins: if one co-heir forgives his share of qisas or settles for compensation, the right to qisas drops for all, and each remaining heir gets his share of diyah. Example: Zayd's five sons, one forgives; qisas drops, four-fifths of diyah is distributed among the other four.
This is the first ruling anchored in the principle that qisas is a right of all heirs.
2
Identify the dispute on spouses
The Hanafi school holds that spouses are included among heirs with right to qisas and diyah. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i exclude them, arguing inheritance is by lineage, not cause (marriage).
The dispute is on the scope of 'heirs' for these specific rights.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi dalil: (a) The Prophet ordered the wife of Ushaym al-Dhababi to inherit from the diyah of her husband. (b) Qisas and diyah are inheritable – e.g., if a victim's son dies before qisas, his son (grandson) inherits the right to qisas. (c) Marital relationship continues legally for inheritance.
The hadith is the primary textual evidence.
4
Analyze the opposing proof
Malik and Shafi'i argue: inheritance is succession (khilafah) based on lineage (nasab), not cause (sabab). Marriage ends at death, so spouses cannot claim rights that arise after death like qisas/diyah.
Their position is based on the nature of inheritance as a relationship of lineage.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In Hanafi law, spouses can claim qisas or diyah. In Maliki/Shafi'i law, spouses only inherit from the general estate, not from the specific right to qisas/diyah. This affects actual distribution of blood money and the ability to demand retaliation.
The practical difference is in who receives compensation.

If one of the co-heirs forgives the blood or settles for compensation from his share, the right to qisas drops for the rest, and they get their share of diyah. The principle is that qisas is the right of all heirs, and similarly diyah, contrary to Malik and Shafi'i regarding spouses. Their argument is that inheritance is succession, and succession is by lineage, not by cause, because the cause is cut off by death. Commentary: The right of qisas is for all heirs. If one forgives, others cannot take qisas but can take diyah. Example: Zayd has five sons. He is intentionally killed. One son forgives; qisas drops; only diyah is wajib; one-fifth is excluded, and four-fifths are divided equally among the four remaining. The principle: since all heirs have right in qisas, each has the right to take or forgive. So if one forgives, qisas falls. According to us, all heirs have right in qisas and diyah, whether their inheritance is by lineage or cause. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i disagree, saying spouses have no right because inheritance is succession based on lineage, and the cause (marriage) ends at death. Our evidence: The Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered that the wife of Ushaym al-Dhababi inherit from the 'aql of her husband Ushaym. Also, qisas and diyah are rights that are inherited. For example, if a man has two sons, and one son dies leaving a son, then qisas is between the surviving son and the grandson. So it is established for all heirs. Marital relationship remains after death as a legal matter for inheritance, or it is established after death based on its cause (the wound). Commentary: We hold spouses have rights. The Prophet ordered the wife of Ushaym to inherit from the diyah. This shows the wife had a right in diyah, so similarly in qisas. Also, inheritance runs in qisas and diyah, so all heirs are entitled. Evidence of inheritance running: if a man has two sons and one dies before qisas, his son steps in. So inheritance applies. And the claim that marriage ends at death is not absolute; for inheritance, it remains to establish the right of spouses to inherit. Or the right to qisas/diyah is not established after death but is based on the wound which occurred before death, when marriage existed.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage covers two interrelated rulings: (1) When one co-heir forgives his share of qisas, the right to qisas falls for all heirs, but they may claim their proportionate share of diyah (blood money) from the killer. An example is given: if a man with five sons is killed, and one son forgives, qisas drops and the remaining four sons get four-fifths of the diyah, with the one-fifth corresponding to the forgiving son's share forfeited. (2) The text then addresses an inter-madhhab dispute: Do spouses (husband or wife) have a right in qisas and diyah as heirs? The Hanafi position (our school) affirms they do. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who ordered that the wife of Ushaym al-Dhababi inherit from the diyah ('aql) of her husband. This shows that a widow has a right in diyah, and by analogy (qiyas) also in qisas (since qisas is also a right that can be inherited). Furthermore, the Hanafis argue that qisas and diyah are rights in which inheritance runs (yajri fihi al-irth). Evidence: if a murder victim has two sons, and one son dies before execution of qisas, his son (grandson of victim) inherits his father's right to qisas, so qisas becomes between the surviving son and the grandson. This proves that qisas is inheritable, so all heirs (including spouses, who are heirs) have a right. The Malikis and Shafi'is argue that spouses do not have right in qisas/diyah because inheritance is a form of succession (khilafah) that is based on lineage (nasab) and not on cause (sabab) like marriage, since marriage ends with death. The Hanafis respond: marital relationship continues after death legally (hukman) for the purpose of inheritance. Alternatively, the right to qisas/diyah is not established after death; rather, it is established based on the cause (the wound) which occurred before death when the marriage was still valid. Therefore, spouses are included.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment (capital punishment) for intentional killing, right of heirs.
دية (diyah): Blood money (financial compensation) paid in lieu of qisas, inheritable among heirs.
زوجین (zawjayn): Spouses (husband and wife) of the deceased.
وراثة (wirathah): Inheritance; the right of heirs to succeed to the estate and rights of the deceased.
خلافت (khilafah): Succession; the transfer of rights to heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of one co-heir forgiving his right to qisas?
A) The remaining heirs can still execute qisas on the killer
B) The remaining heirs get their share of diyah but qisas is dropped
C) The killer must be executed only if the forgiving heir was a spouse
D) The remaining heirs get nothing

Key Takeaway
One heir's forgiveness drops qisas for all heirs, but diyah shares remain; spouses inherit qisas and diyah in Hanafi law, contrary to the Maliki/Shafi'i position.

Qisas — Retaliation
advanced
12 min
Spouses’ Right in Qisas and Diyah and the Effect of One Heir’s Forgiveness
Inter-madhhab dispute on spouses inheriting qisas/diyah and ruling on partial forgiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on spouses inheriting qisas and diyah, and apply the rule of indivisibility of qisas to scenarios involving partial forgiveness.

Core Idea
Qisas is indivisible: one heir's forgiveness extinguishes it entirely, but spouses still inherit their share.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two interconnected issues: whether spouses have a right in qisas and diyah, and what happens when one heir forgives the right to qisas. The Hanafi school takes a distinctive stance that all heirs, including spouses, hold a joint right, and because qisas is indivisible, any partial forgiveness nullifies the entire qisas right, converting the remaining heirs' shares into monetary compensation. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proofs and contrasts them with the positions of Malik and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
State the specific ruling being contested: whether spouses inherit the right to qisas and diyah.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafis claim all heirs, including spouses, have a right. Cite the hadith of Ushaym al-Dhababi and the analogy of inheritance flowing in qisas.
3
State the opposing view and its basis
Malik and al-Shafi'i exclude spouses. Their argument: 'inheritance' in the relevant texts refers only to post-death inheritance, and the pre-death right of spouses in the estate does not extend to qisas/diyah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis counter: marriage remains legally effective for inheritance purposes after death, or the cause of qisas (the injury) occurred during the marriage.
5
Apply the indivisibility rule
Explain why one heir's forgiveness ends the qisas right for all, and identify the exception when two victims are involved.
