اولیاء نے اس کو معاف کر دیا تو اس معافی کی وجہ سے خالد کے اولیاء کا حق ساقط نہ ہو گا بلکہ ان کو قصاص لینے کا حق باقی ہے۔
It will not be in diyah. And those people intend by inheritance the inheritance that occurs after death, otherwise before death in the estate, the right that is attached to the heirs, in that spouses also receive inheritance. Nevertheless, according to those people, spouses have no right in qisas and diyah. And according to us, all heirs have the right. Evidence of the Hanafis: And we have that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the inheritance of the wife of Ushaym al-Dhababi from the blood money of her husband Ushaym. And because it is a right in which inheritance flows, such that if a person is killed and he has two sons, then one of them dies leaving a son, the qisas is between the direct son and the grandson, so it is established for all the heirs. And the marital relationship remains after death in a legal sense regarding inheritance, or it is established after death based on its cause which is the injury. Translation and our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered that the wife of Ushaym al-Dhababi be made an heir from the blood money of her husband Ushaym. And because qisas and diyah are such a right in which inheritance flows, such that a person is killed and he has two sons, one of them dies leaving a son, then qisas will be between the direct son and the grandson. So this [qisas and diyah] is established for all the heirs. And the marital relationship remains after death in a legal sense regarding inheritance, or these (qisas or diyah) are established after death attributed to their cause. And the cause is the inflicting of the wound. Commentary: According to us, spouses have a right in qisas and diyah. The evidence is that Ushaym al-Dhababi was killed by mistake, thus blood money became obligatory. The Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded that in that blood money, the wife of Ushaym should also be given inheritance. From this, it is known that the wife had a right in the blood money; therefore it was given to her. Similarly, in qisas, she will have a right. Then qisas and diyah are such things that inheritance flows in them, and when inheritance flows, then this right is established for all heirs. Question: What is the evidence that inheritance flows in these two? Answer: Zaid has two sons, Bakr and Khalid. An enemy kills Zaid, so the right of qisas is for Bakr and Khalid. Now Bakr dies and he has a son Sajid. Then in the right of qisas, Sajid stands in place of Bakr, and the right of qisas is now for Sajid and Khalid both. So from this, it is known that inheritance flows in qisas. And you said that the marital relationship ends with death? This is not absolutely correct; rather, regarding inheritance, the marital relationship remains in a legal sense after death. And when it remains, then spouses are also entitled to qisas and diyah. Or it can be answered that the cause of qisas or diyah is the wound that was inflicted before the occurrence of death, and at that time the marital relationship existed, and after death, qisas or diyah become established due to that same cause, so excluding spouses from other heirs would not be correct. And the argument of Malik and Shafi'i is unsuccessful. All heirs have the option regarding the slain: whether they exact qisas, or forgive their right, or make a compromise. And when it is established for all, then each of them is capable of exacting and forgiving, whether by pardon or compromise. And from the necessity of the fall of the right of some in qisas is the fall of the right of the rest in it, because it is indivisible. Translation: And when the right of qisas is established for all heirs, then each of them is able to exact qisas and to forfeit it by pardon or compromise. And for the fall of the right of some in qisas, it is necessary that the right of the rest in qisas falls, because qisas is indivisible. Commentary: From the above details, it is clear that the right of qisas is established for all heirs, so each of them also has the right to exact qisas or forgive their right or make a compromise. In any case, when some have forfeited the right of qisas, qisas must be completely dropped; otherwise division (tajzi) would be necessary while qisas is indivisible. If a person kills two men, and the heirs of one victim forgive qisas, the right of the heirs of the other victim for qisas will not fall. Contrary to the case when he kills two men and one of the two guardians forgives, because there two qisas are obligatory without any doubt due to the difference of the killing and the killed, while here [in the case of one victim] it is one due to the unity of both. And when qisas falls, the share of the remaining ones turns into wealth because qisas is prevented due to a meaning returning to the killer, and the forgiver has nothing of the wealth because he forfeited his right by his own action and consent. Translation: Contrary to the case when the killer has killed two persons and the guardian of one of the victims has forgiven, because there two qisas are obligatory without any doubt due to the difference of the killer and the killed, and here one qisas due to the unity of both (killer and killed). And when qisas falls, the share of the remaining ones changes into wealth because qisas is prevented due to a meaning that refers back to the killer, and the forgiver has nothing of the wealth because he forfeited his right by his own action and consent. Commentary: In the previous case, if one forgave, qisas ended completely. But if Zaid killed two persons, for example Bakr and Khalid, then it happened that the guardians of Bakr forgave him, then due to this forgiveness, the right of the guardians of Khalid will not fall; rather they retain the right to exact qisas.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether spouses (zawjayn) inherit qisas and diyah. The passage begins by stating the opposing view: Malik and Shafi'i hold that spouses do not inherit in qisas and diyah because the inheritance they refer to is the actual inheritance after death, not the right attached to the estate before death. In contrast, the Hanafi school holds that all heirs, including spouses, have a right. The Hanafi evidence is presented: a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered that the wife of Ushaym al-Dhababi inherit from her husband's blood money. Additionally, the Hanafis argue that qisas and diyah are rights in which inheritance flows (yajri fihi al-irth), illustrated by an example: if a man has two sons and one dies before the killer's prosecution, his son (grandson) inherits the right of qisas alongside the surviving son. The passage then addresses a potential objection that marriage ends at death, responding that the marital relationship remains legally (hukman) for inheritance purposes, or alternatively that the cause of qisas (the wound) occurred during the marriage. Thus, spouses cannot be excluded. The argument of Malik and Shafi'i is deemed unsuccessful (nam na huwa). Having established that all heirs hold the right, the text explains the consequences: each heir may exact qisas, forgive (afw), or compromise (sulh). Because qisas is indivisible (ghayr mutajazzi), if one heir forgives, the right of all others also falls. However, an exception is made where a killer murders two victims: forgiveness by one victim's heirs does not affect the other victim's heirs, as two distinct qisas obligations exist. In such a case, if one heir forgives, the share of the remaining heirs turns into monetary compensation (mal), because the qisas is prevented due to a cause (like flight or death of the killer). The forgiver receives nothing because he voluntarily forfeited his right.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional homicide or injury; right of the victim's heirs.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for unlawful homicide or injury.
وراثت (wirathah): Inheritance; transmission of rights and property from deceased to heirs.
عفو (afw): Pardon; voluntary forgiveness of the right to qisas by an heir.
صلح (sulh): Compromise; agreement to accept monetary compensation in lieu of qisas.
غیر متجزی (ghayr mutajazzi): Indivisible; cannot be split among multiple claimants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one heir forgives the right to qisas in a case of homicide, what happens to the rights of the other heirs according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The remaining heirs can still exact qisas on behalf of their share.
B) The right to qisas falls for all heirs because qisas is indivisible.
C) The forgiver must pay compensation to the other heirs.
D) The case is referred to the judge to decide.

Key Takeaway
All heirs, including spouses, share the right to qisas, and because qisas is indivisible, one heir's pardon cancels it for everyone.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
The Indivisibility of Qisas: One Heir's Forgiveness Extinguishes the Right for All
Ruling with talil on qisas indivisibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that qisas is indivisible and apply it to a scenario where one of multiple heirs forgives his share.

Core Idea
Qisas is indivisible: if one heir forgives, the entire right to retaliation falls for all heirs.

In Hanafi criminal law, when a person is murdered, the right to demand qisas (retaliation) belongs to all heirs jointly. But what happens if only one heir forgives? The passage you are about to study establishes a foundational principle: qisas is indivisible (ghayr mutajazzi). This means partial forgiveness is impossible – one heir's choice binds all. Understanding this rule is essential before looking at the exception for multiple victims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses the right of qisas (retaliatory execution) after intentional homicide. It states that qisas is wajib as a right of the heirs, but they may execute it, forgive (afw), or settle (sulh).
Qisas is a right of the heirs, not an obligation on them to execute.
2
Locate the principle of indivisibility
The text explicitly says: 'wa la yatajazzā' – qisas is indivisible. The key phrase is 'min darūrati suqūṭi ḥaqqi l-baʿḍi l-qiṣāṣ suqūṭu ḥaqqi l-bāqīna fīhi' (from the necessity of the fall of the right of some, the right of the rest in it falls).
Indivisibility means the right cannot be split; if one part falls, the whole falls.
3
Trace the reason (talil)
The author does not give an explicit illa but the logic is clear: qisas is a single, unified right that cannot be divided. If one heir drops his share, the killer's life becomes protected (ismah), making further execution impossible.
The consequent conversion to diyah is explained in the next part, but for now, understand the indivisibility.
4
Apply to a single-victim scenario
Consider a case: Zayd kills Amr. Amr has two heirs, Ali and Hassan. If Ali forgives qisas, the right to execute falls completely, even if Hassan wants retaliation. Hassan cannot demand separate qisas.
The only remaining right for Hassan is a monetary claim for his share of diyah.
5
Note the mufta bihi and cross-madhhab difference
This is the relied-upon Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah). Other schools like the Shafi'i may allow partial forgiveness, but the Hanafi school insists on indivisibility.
The practical difference: in a Shafi'i context, non-forgiving heirs could still execute qisas after partial forgiveness.

ترجمہ اور جب تمام ورثا کے لئے حق قصاص ثابت ہو گیا تو ان میں سے ہر ایک قصاص لینے اور عفو اور صلح کے طریقہ پر اسقاط پر قادر ہو گا اور قصاص میں بعض کا حق ساقط ہونے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ قصاص میں باقیوں کا حق ساقط ہو جائے اس لئے کہ قصاص غیر متجزی ہے۔ تشریح مذکورہ تفصیلات سے یہ بات معلوم ہو چکی ہے کہ حق قصاص تمام ورثاء کے لئے ثابت ہے تو ان میں سے ہر ایک کو یہ حق بھی ثابت ہوگا کہ وہ قصاص وصول کریں یا اپنا حق معاف کر دیں یا مصالحت کر لیں۔
بہر حال کسی بھی طرح ہو جب بعض نے حق قصاص ساقط کر دیا تو اب قصاص کو ساقط کرنا پڑیگا ور نہ قصاص میں تجزی لازم آئے گی

ایک شخص نے دو آدمیوں کو قتل کر دیا تو ایک مقتول کے ورثاء نے قصاص معاف کر دیا تو
دوسرے مقتول کے ورثاء کا حق قصاص ساقط نہ ہو گا
بخلاف ما اذا قتل رجلين وعفا احد الوليين لان الواجب هناك قصاصان من غير شبهة الاختلاف القتل والمقتول وههنا واحد لا تحادهما واذا سقط القصاص ينقلب نصيب الباقين مالا لانه امتنع مخراجع الى القاتل وليس للعافى شئ من المال لانه اسقط حقه بفعله ورضاه

ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ قاتل نے دو شخصوں کو قتل کیا ہو اور مقتولین میں سے کسی ایک کے ولی نے معاف کیا ہو اس لئے کہ وہاں دو قصاص واجب ہیں بغیر کسی شبہ کے قتل اور مقتول کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے اور یہاں ایک قصاص ہے ان دونوں (قتل و مقتول) کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے اور جب قصاص ساقط ہو گیا تو باقیوں کا حصہ مال سے بدل جائے گا اس لئے قصاص ممتنع ہوا ہے ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے جو قاتل کی جانب راجع ہیں اور معاف کرنے والے کے لئے کچھ مال نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے اپنا حق اپنے فعل اور اپنی رضامندی سے ساقط کر دیا

تشریح گزشتہ صورت میں اگر کسی ایک نے معاف کر دیا تو قصاص بالکل ختم ہو گیا لیکن اگر زید نے دو شخصوں کو قتل کیا ہو مثلا بکر کو اور خالد کو ، پھر ایسا ہوا کہ بکر کے اولیاء نے اس کو معاف کر دیا تو اس معافی کی وجہ سے خالد کے اولیاء کا حق ساقط نہ ہو گا بلکہ ان کو قصاص لینے کا حق باقی ہے۔

وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ گذشتہ والے مسئلہ میں قبل ایک ہے اور مقتول بھی ایک ہے اور دوسرے مسئلہ میں قتل دو ہیں اور مقتول دو ہیں تو ایک فعل یا ایک محل کی معافی سے دوسرا فعل یا دوسرا حل معاف نہ ہو گا بخلاف پہلے والے سٹار کے کہ وہاں فعل ومحل ایک ہے تو بعض کا عفو کل کا عضو ہو جائے گا۔ جب بعض نے معاف کر دیا تو اب قاتل کے اندر عصمت پیدا ہو گئی اور جب عصمت پیدا ہو گئی تو قصاص تو ساقط ہو گیا لیکن دیت واجب ہوئی جیسے خطاء کی صورت میں قاتل کے خاطی ہونے کی وجہ سے قاتل میں عصمت ہے جس کی وجہ سے اس کو قتل نہیں کیا جائے البه و واجب ہو گی ایسے ہی یہاں بھی ہے۔
دیت
اور جو ولی اپنا حق معاف کر چکا تھا اس کو دیت میں سے کچھ نہیں ملے گا اس لئے کہ اس نے اپنی رضا مندی اور اپنے فعل سے اپنے حق کو ساقط کیا ہے۔
And when qisas is established for all, then each of them is able to execute and drop it by forgiveness and settlement, and from the necessity of the fall of the right of some of them in qisas, the right of the rest in it falls because it is indivisible. Translation: And when the right of qisas is established for all heirs, then each of them becomes capable of taking qisas and dropping it by way of forgiveness and settlement, and for the fall of the right of some in qisas, it is necessary that the right of the rest in qisas falls because qisas is indivisible. Commentary: It has become clear from the mentioned details that the right of qisas is established for all heirs, so each of them also has this right to take qisas or forgive their right or make a settlement. In any case, when some have dropped the right of qisas, then qisas must be dropped; otherwise, division would become necessary in qisas, whereas qisas is indivisible. A person killed two men, and the heirs of one victim forgave qisas, then the right of the heirs of the other victim for qisas will not fall. Contrary to the case when he killed two men and one of the two wali forgave, because there two qisas are obligatory without any doubt due to the difference of killer and killed, and here it is one due to their unity. And when qisas falls, the share of the remaining becomes wealth because it is prevented due to a meaning that reverts to the killer, and the one who forgave has nothing of the wealth because he dropped his right by his own action and consent. Translation: Contrary to the case when the killer killed two persons and the wali of one of the victims forgave, because there two qisas are obligatory without any doubt due to the difference of the killing and the killed, and here it is one qisas due to the unity of both (killing and killed). And when qisas falls, the share of the remaining turns into wealth because qisas is prevented due to a meaning that goes back to the killer, and the forgiver has nothing of the wealth because he dropped his right by his action and his consent. Commentary: In the previous case, if one forgave, qisas completely ended. But if Zayd killed two persons, for example Bakr and Khalid, and it happened that Bakr's heirs forgave him, then due to that forgiveness, the right of Khalid's heirs will not fall; rather, they retain the right to take qisas. The reason for the difference is that in the previous case, the killer is one and the victim is one, and in the other case, the killings are two and the victims are two, so forgiveness of one act or one subject does not forgive the other act or subject, contrary to the first scenario where the act and subject are one, so the forgiveness of some becomes the forgiveness of all. When some forgave, then immunity (ismah) was created in the killer, and when immunity was created, qisas fell but diyah became obligatory, just as in the case of killing by mistake due to the killer being mistaken, there is immunity in the killer, because of which he is not killed, and diyah becomes obligatory; similarly here. Diyah and the wali who had already forgiven his right will not get anything from the diyah because he dropped his right by his own consent and his own action.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation (talil) on the indivisibility of qisas in Hanafi law. The author states that when qisas is established for all heirs, each heir has the right to execute it or drop it through forgiveness (afw) or settlement (sulh). However, because qisas is indivisible (ghayr mutajazzi), if one heir drops his right, the right of all other heirs also falls; it cannot be partially enforced. For example, if a killer is owed qisas by two heirs, and one forgives, the killer is no longer subject to qisas at all. The passage then gives an exception: if one killer kills two separate victims, the heirs of each victim have an independent right to qisas. So if the heirs of one victim forgive, it does not affect the rights of the other victim's heirs; they may still demand qisas. The reason (wajh al-farq) is that in the single-victim case, the act and the victim are one, so forgiveness of part is forgiveness of the whole. In the multiple-victim case, each killing is a separate act with a separate victim. The passage further explains that when qisas falls due to some heirs forgiving, the killer acquires immunity (ismah), and the remaining heirs' shares convert to a right to diyah (blood money). The forgiving heir gets nothing from the diyah because he voluntarily relinquished his right.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional homicide or wounding; the right of the victim's heirs to have the killer executed.
عفو (afw): Forgiveness of the right to qisas by the heirs, either freely or in exchange for diyah.
تجزّي (tajazzi): Divisibility; the quality of being divisible into parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a killer has two heirs (A and B), and A forgives his right to qisas, what happens to B's right?
A) B can still demand qisas
B) B's right also falls, but B is entitled to his share of diyah
C) B's right falls completely, and B gets nothing from qisas or diyah
D) B can demand qisas but only after paying A's share

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, qisas is indivisible: if any one heir forgives, the entire right to retaliation falls, and only monetary compensation (diyah) remains for the non-forgiving heirs.

Qisas — Retaliation

Exception: Separate Qisas for Multiple Victims – Forgiveness by One Victim's Heirs Does Not Affect Others
Exception to indivisibility: multiple victims scenario

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the single-victim case from the multiple-victim case and apply the rule that forgiveness by heirs of one victim does not affect the qisas right of another victim's heirs.

Core Idea
When a killer murders two separate persons, each victim's heirs have an independent qisas right; forgiveness by one set does not extinguish the other.

The previous lesson established that qisas is indivisible when there is one killer and one victim with multiple heirs. But what if one killer murders two separate individuals? The passage now clarifies an important exception: the indivisibility rule applies only within a single killing. When two separate murders occur, each victim's heirs have a separate and independent right to qisas. Forgiveness by one set of heirs does not affect the other set's right. Understanding this distinction prevents a serious error in applying qisas rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios compared
The passage contrasts: (1) one killer, one victim, multiple heirs – where indivisibility applies. (2) one killer, two victims, each with their own heirs – where qisas for each victim is separate.
The key factor is the identity of the act and the victim.
2
State the exception clearly
If Zayd kills Bakr and Khalid, and Bakr's heirs forgive Zayd, Khalid's heirs still have the right to demand qisas for Khalid's murder. The forgiveness does not transfer to the other killing.
Each killing is a separate legal event.
3
Analyze the reason (wajh al-farq)
The text says: because in the single-victim case, the killing and the killed are one, so the act and subject are unified. In the multiple-victim case, there are two killings and two victims, so the acts and subjects are distinct.
The unity of act and subject (ittihad al-fi'l wa al-mahall) is what triggers indivisibility.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Apply: Zayd kills two persons. Heirs of victim 1 forgive. Heirs of victim 2 can still demand execution. Zayd may be executed for the second murder but not for the first.
If executed, only the second murder is expiated; the first remains unpunished criminally but may require diyah from his estate? This is beyond the text.
5
Note the consequence for diyah
In the single-victim case, when qisas falls due to one heir's forgiveness, the remaining heirs get diyah and the forgiving heir gets nothing. In multiple-victim case, if the non-forgiving heirs execute qisas, the killer dies and no diyah is paid for that victim; for the victim whose heirs forgave, if qisas is not executed, there may be diyah from the killer's estate.
The text only mentions diyah in the single-victim context, but the principle extends.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional homicide; right of the victim's heirs.
عفو (afw): Forgiveness of qisas right.
اتحاد الفعل والمحل (ittihad al-fi'l wa al-mahall): Unity of act and subject; the reason for indivisibility in single-victim case.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Group Killing: All Participants Executed in Qisas
Ruling and proof that all participants in a group killing are executed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on group killing and explain why all participants are executed in qisas, using Umar's ruling and the principle of taghallub.

Core Idea
If a group intentionally kills one person, all are executed in qisas — multiplicity does not reduce the penalty.

When a group of people intentionally kills a single victim, a critical question arises: should only one of them be executed, or all? This lesson examines the Hanafi position, which holds that every participant in the killing is fully liable for qisas. The ruling is supported by the explicit precedent of Caliph Umar (ra) and by the rational consideration that group involvement is the common mode of homicide; allowing multiplicity to prevent qisas would defeat its deterrent purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a group intentionally killing one person (qatl al-amd). The Hanafi ruling: qisas is wajib on all participants — all are executed.
The ruling applies only when the killing is intentional (amd) and each participant contributes to the death.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The proof is two-fold: (1) the statement of Caliph Umar (ra): 'If the people of San'a' had conspired together against him, I would have killed them all.' (2) Rational reasoning: killing typically occurs through mutual assistance (taghallub), and qisas is meant to deter; if multiplicity blocked qisas, the deterrence would be lost.
Umar's statement is considered a qawl al-sahabi, a source of law in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
From Umar's words, the phrase 'قتلتهم' (I would have killed them) shows that all conspirators are subject to execution, regardless of their individual roles. The word 'تمالا' (conspired) indicates cooperative action, which is the basis for holding all liable.
The Hanafi usul principle: qawl al-sahabi is a proof (hujja) when not opposed by another sahabi, unless it contradicts qiyas jali, which is not the case here.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar holds that diyat (blood money) applies instead of qisas when multiple killers are involved. However, this is a weak (mardud) position. The text refutes it by emphasizing that the common mode of killing is through group cooperation, so qisas must apply to all to achieve its purpose.
Zufar's view is recorded in the nawadir (rare transmissions) and is not relied upon for fatwa.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that all participants are executed. This is the position of the majority of the Hanafi school, based on the zahir al-riwayah and the precedent of Umar.
Tarjih authority: the author of this text (likely al-Hidayah) gives preference to the majority view, supported by strong dalil.

كتاب الجنايات

قال واذا قتل جماعة واحدا عمدا اقتص من جميعهم لقول عمر رضى الله عنه فيه لو تمالا عليه اهل صنعاء لقتلتهم ولان القتل بطريق التغالب غالب والقصاص مزجرة للسفهاء فيجب تحقيقا لحكمة الاحياء

تشريح: مقتول ایک ہے اور قاتل متعدد ہیں تو سب کو قصاص میں قتل کر دیا جائے گا۔ حضرت فاروق اعظم کا یہی فیصلہ ہے اور چونکہ قتل عموماً ایسے ہی ہوتا ہے ایک کی چند لوگ مدد کرتے ہیں تو اگر قاتل کے تعدد کی وجہ سے قصاص کو چھوڑ دیا جائے تو پھر قصاص کا دروازہ بند ہو جائے گا۔ اور جو مقصود ہے یعنی نظام عالم کو برقرار رکھنا اور احیاء ناس یہ مقصود معطل ہو کر رہ جائے گا۔

تنبیہ: واقعہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ صنعاء میں زینب نامی ایک عورت تھی اس کا شوہر سفر میں پردیس گیا ہوا تھا اور اپنا ایک بیٹا اصیل نامی جو پہلی بیوی سے تھا اس کے پاس چھوڑ گیا۔ زینب کے چند آشنا پیدا ہو گئے مگر وہ اصیل سے تنگ آگئی تو زینب نے گرو گھنٹالوں سے مشورہ کیا تو سب کی یہ رائے قرار پائی کہ یہ لڑکا ہم کو فضیحت کرتا ہے۔ لہذا سب نے متفق ہو کر اس کو قتل کر کے چاہ عمران میں ڈال دیا اور یہ سب مع عورت کے سات آدمی تھے۔ پس جب وہ لڑکا گم ہو گیا تو یہی زینب چلانے لگی اور چلانے میں کہتی جاتی کہ الہی جس نے اصیل کو قتل کیا اس کا ناس ہو اور وہ پکڑا جائے اور اس وقت حضرت عمر کی طرف سے یعلی صنعاء کے حاکم تھے پس انہوں نے اس کے بارے میں لوگوں کو خطبہ سنایا کہ اس کی تحقیق و تفتیش کریں تو چند روز کے بعد پیر غمد ان کی جانب ایک شخص کا گذر ہوا اور وہاں مکھیوں کے ہجوم سے اس نے پتہ پایا تو اس نے یعلی کو خبر دی تو آپ لوگوں کو لے کر تشریف لے گئے تو عورت کے گرو گھنٹالوں میں سے ایک بولا کہ مجھے رسی میں لٹکاؤ پس اتر کر اصیل کی لاش کو کنویں کی کول میں چھپا دیا پھر وہ نکلا اور اس نے کہا کہ میں نے وہاں کچھ نہیں پایا تو دوسرے شخص نے کہا کہ مجھے اتارئیے پس وہ اتر کر لاش نکال لایا۔ پس آخر کار عورت نے اقرار کیا اور اس کے یاروں نے بھی اقرار کیا۔ یعلی نے اس کی تفصیل حضرت عمر کو لکھی ۔ انہوں نے اس کا یہ حکم صادر فرمایا کہ ان سب کو قتل کر دیا جائے اور فرمایا کہ اگر تمام اہل صنعاء بھی مل کر اس کام کو کرتے تو میں ان سب کو قتل کر دیتا۔
[Kitab al-Jinaayat] He said: If a group intentionally kills one person, qisas is executed from all of them due to the saying of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) concerning this: 'If the people of San'a' had conspired together against him, I would have killed them all.' And because killing generally occurs through mutual assistance, and qisas is a deterrent for the foolish, so it is obligatory to achieve the wisdom of preserving life. Explanation: The slain is one, and the killers are many, so all will be killed in qisas. This is the verdict of Umar the Great, and because killing usually occurs through the assistance of several individuals, if qisas is waived due to the multiplicity of killers, then the door of qisas would be closed, and the objective, i.e., maintaining the world's order and preservation of people, would be suspended. Note: The incident was that in San'a' there was a woman named Zaynab; her husband had traveled abroad and left his son Asil from his first wife with her. Zaynab had some acquaintances, but she became fed up with Asil, so she consulted her associates, and they all agreed that this boy brings them disgrace. So they all conspired to kill him and threw him into the well of 'Umran. They were seven men including the woman. When the boy went missing, Zaynab herself started crying and saying, 'O God, may the one who killed Asil be destroyed and caught.' At that time, Ya'la was the governor of San'a' on behalf of Umar. He addressed the people to investigate. After some days, a person passed by the well of Ghamdan and noticed a swarm of flies, so he informed Ya'la. He went with people, and one of the woman's accomplices said, 'Lower me with a rope,' and he hid Asil's body in the well's crevice, then came out saying he found nothing. Another said, 'Lower me,' and he brought out the body. Finally, the woman confessed, and her companions also confessed. Ya'la wrote the details to Umar, and he issued the order that all be killed, saying, 'If all the people of San'a' had collaborated in this act, I would have killed them all.'
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling when a group intentionally kills one person. The author begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: all members of the group are subject to qisas (retributive execution). The proof is twofold: (1) the precedent of Caliph Umar (ra), who ruled that even if the entire population of San'a' conspired to kill one person, he would execute them all; (2) rational reasoning: since group involvement (taghallub/cooperation) is the common mode of homicide, allowing multiplicity of killers to prevent qisas would defeat the purpose of qisas, which is to preserve life (ihya' al-nas). The commentary then narrates the historical incident of Zaynab and Asil to illustrate the practical application of this ruling. The text also implicitly addresses a potential objection: if only some of the killers are executed, the rest escape, so all must be executed to fully serve the deterrent purpose. This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school; Imam Zufar's view that diyat applies instead is refuted in the preceding lines (not fully reproduced here but mentioned in the OCR). The key lesson: in Hanafi law, qisas is not divisible; each participant is fully responsible for the death, and all must face execution.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retributive execution in homicide cases, where the killer is put to death as a legal consequence.
قتل عمد (qatl al-amd): Intentional killing with a weapon or instrument that is likely to cause death.
تغالب (taghallub): Overpowering through mutual assistance; the common mode of homicide where multiple actors cooperate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, if a group of five people intentionally kills one person, what is the ruling?
A) Only the one who struck the fatal blow is executed; the others pay diyat.
B) All five are executed in qisas, based on Umar's ruling.
C) They are all given a discretionary punishment (ta'zir), not qisas.
D) A lottery is held, and only one is executed.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, all participants in an intentional group killing are executed in qisas; multiplicity does not reduce the penalty.

One Killer Multiple Victims: Only One Execution
Ruling and dispute regarding qisas when one kills multiple victims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas when one kills multiple victims and explain the Hanafi proof (tamathul) in contrast to the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The killer's single execution satisfies all victims' qisas claims because life is indivisible and each victim's right is fully met.

When one person kills multiple people, a key question arises: can the killer be executed more than once, or do the heirs of additional victims deserve financial compensation? The Hanafi school holds that a single execution suffices for all victims, while Imam al-Shafi'i distinguishes based on the order of killings. This lesson explores the Hanafi proof rooted in the principle of equivalence (tamathul) and the indivisibility of life, and the practical difference between the two schools.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: one execution for all victims, no diyat. Note that even if only one heir appears, the execution extinguishes all rights.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize Imam al-Shafi'i's position: execution only for the first victim (if order known); for others, diyat. If order unknown, either execution with diyat division or lottery.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i argument: only one actual killing occurs from the killer, so equivalence (tamathul) fails for additional victims. The killer's single life cannot correspond to multiple lives.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Study the Hanafi rebuttal: the killer is fully responsible for each death (each victim suffers a fatal wound), so tamathul holds for each. Life is indivisible, so one execution satisfies all. Analogy to the first section (group killing one) supports this.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under Hanafi law, killer dies once, no extra financial burden. Under Shafi'i, the killer's estate may also owe diyat for 'extra' victims, or a lottery decides which heir gets qisas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا قتل واحد جماعة فحضر اولياء المقتولين قتل لجمعهم ولا شئ لهم غير ذلك فان حضر واحد منهم قتل له وسقط حق الباقين وقال الشافعى يقتل بالاول منهم ويجب للباقين المال وان اجتمعوا ولم يعرف الاول قتل لهم وقسمت الديات بينهم وقيل يقرع بينهم فيقتل لمن خرجت قرعته

تشريح: ایک شخص نے مثلا دس آدمیوں کو قتل کر رکھا ہے تو اگر تمام اولیاء جمع ہو جائیں تب بھی قصاص میں یہی ایک قاتل سب کے لئے ہوگا اور اس کے قتل سے سب کا قصاص ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر ان میں سے کوئی ایک حاضر ہوا اور قصاص لیا گیا تو بھی باقیوں کا حق ساقط ہو گیا اور کچھ مال کسی کو نہیں ملے گا اور امام شافعی کے یہاں مختلف اقوال ہیں: اگر قاتل نے ان سب مقتولین کو یکے بعد دیگرے قتل کیا ہو تو اول کے بدلہ میں قصاص ہے اور باقیوں کے بدلہ میں مال واجب ہوگا۔ اور اگر سب کو (ایکدم) قتل کیا ہو یا آگے پیچھے کیا ہو لیکن اول کا علم نہ ہو سکے تو سب کے لئے قتل کیا جائے گا اور پھر دیات کو ان سب کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا۔

-- قرعہ ڈالا جائے جس کا نام آجائے اس کے لئے قتل کر دیا جائے اور باقی کے لئے مال۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل، احناف کی دلیل

له ان الموجود من الواحد قتلات والذي تحقق في حقه قتل واحد فلا تماثل وهو القياس في الفصل الاول الا انه عرف بالشرع ولنا ان كل واحد منهم قاتل بوصف الكمال فجاء التماثل اصله الفصل الاول اذلو لم يكن كذلك لما وجب القصاص ولانه وجد من كل واحد منهم جرح صالح للا نزهاق فيضاف الى كل الذهو لا يتجزى ولان القصاص شرع مع المنافي لتحقيق الاحياء وقد حصل بقتله فاکتنی به
If one person kills a group, and the legal heirs (awliya') of the slain attend, the killer is executed for all of them, and they have nothing other than that. If only one of them attends, he is executed for that one, and the right of the others lapses. Al-Shafi'i said: He is executed for the first among them, and the others are due financial compensation (mal). If they all gather and the first is unknown, he is executed for all of them, and the diyats are divided among them. Some said: A lottery is drawn among them, and he is executed for the one whose lot comes out. Explanation: For example, one person has killed ten people. If all the heirs gather, still this one killer suffices for all, and his execution fulfills the qisas for all. If only one heir is present and qisas is taken, the rights of the others lapse and no financial compensation is given. Imam al-Shafi'i has different sayings: If the killer killed them one after another, there is qisas for the first and financial compensation for the rest. If he killed them all at once or successively but the first is unknown, he is executed for all, and the diyats are divided among them. Some say: A lottery is drawn, and he is executed for the one whose lot comes out. His (al-Shafi'i's) proof: from the one, multiple killings exist, but what is realized in his right is only one killing, so there is no equivalence (tamathul). This is the analogy (qiyas) in the first section, except that it is known by sacred law. Our proof: each of them (the victims) is a killer (i.e., the single killer is fully responsible for each death) with complete description, so equivalence (tamathul) occurs. Its original is the first section (i.e., group killing one), for if it were not so, qisas would not be obligatory. And because from each of them there is a wound suitable for causing death, so it is attributed to each, and it (the life) cannot be divided. And because qisas is legislated despite opposition (munafi) to achieve preservation of life (ihya'), and that has been achieved by his execution, so it suffices.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the reverse scenario: one killer, multiple victims. The Hanafi position is that the killer is executed only once for all victims, regardless of the number. All claims of qisas merge into a single execution. Even if only one heir appears, the execution extinguishes all rights, and no diyat is paid. Imam al-Shafi'i differs: he distinguishes between sequential killings (where only the first triggers qisas, and the rest require diyat) and simultaneous or unknown-order killings (where qisas is executed for all with diyat division, or a lottery determines which victim's qisas is fulfilled). The Hanafi proof is based on the principle of equivalence (mumathalah): just as multiple killers of one victim are all executed (section one), here one killer is executed once for all victims because each victim's right to qisas is fully represented by the killer's single life. The killer's single life corresponds to each victim's right, and since life is indivisible, one execution satisfies all. The purpose of qisas (preservation of life) is achieved by the execution itself; executing the killer multiple times is impossible. The Shafi'i reliance on sequentiality is rejected because the killer's culpability is complete for each victim regardless of order.

Key Terms
أولياء المقتولين (awliya' al-maqtulin): Legal heirs or guardians of the slain person(s) who have the right to demand qisas or diyat.
تماثل (tamathul): Equivalence between the killer and the victim in terms of freedom, religion, and legal capacity, necessary for qisas.
جرح صالح للانزهاق (jurh salih lil-inzihaq): A wound suitable for causing death; the act of wounding that led to death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if one person intentionally kills five people, what happens when the heirs of all five demand qisas?
A) The killer is executed once, and that satisfies all claims.
B) The killer is executed five times (once for each victim), but only if the order is known.
C) The killer is executed for the first victim, and the families of the other four receive diyat.
D) A lottery is held among the heirs, and only the winner gets qisas; the rest get nothing.

Key Takeaway
A single execution satisfies all qisas claims when one person kills multiple victims; no diyat is due.

One Killer of Multiple Victims: Qisas or Diya?
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over qisas when one kills many

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas when one person kills multiple victims and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of tamathul and qiyas.

Core Idea
One execution satisfies all heirs because the soul's departure is indivisible and qisas aims at preserving life.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: when one killer murders multiple victims, does a single execution fulfill the right of qisas for all? The Hanafi school answers yes, while Imam al-Shafi'i differentiates. Understanding the proofs on both sides—especially the role of qiyas and the hadith of 'Umar—sharpens your ability to reason in qisas cases.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds: one execution satisfies all heirs; no diya is owed.
The ruling applies regardless of how many heirs appear.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only the first victim's heirs receive qisas; the rest are entitled to diya.
The opponent distinguishes between sequential and simultaneous killings.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues from qiyas: one death cannot match multiple deaths, so tamathul is lacking.
He cites the general principle of equivalence (tamathul) in qisas.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by citing the opposite case (many killers, one victim) where qisas is established by hadith despite apparent lack of tamathul. They also argue that each heir's participation in the execution is complete, and the soul's departure is indivisible.
This is a qiyas on the established precedent.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In Hanafi, one execution ends all claims. In Shafi'i, heirs of later victims receive diya instead of qisas.
This directly affects the financial outcome for the heirs.

کی جانب سے قتل کیا جائے جس کا قرعہ نکلے۔ تشریح: ایک شخص نے مثلا دس آدمیوں کو قتل کر رکھا ہے تو اگر تمام اولیاء جمع ہو جائیں تب بھی قصاص میں یہی ایک قاتل سب کے لئے ہوگا اور اس کے قتل سے سب کا قصاص ادا بعد دیگرے قتل کیا ہو تو اول کے بدلہ میں قصاص ہے اور باقیوں کے بدلہ میں مال واجب ہوگا۔ اور اگر سب کو (ایک دم) قتل کیا ہو یا آگے پیچھے کیا ہو لیکن اول کا علم نہ ہو سکے تو سب کے لئے قتل کیا جائے گا اور پھر دیات کو ان سب کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا۔ -- قرعہ ڈالا جائے جس کا نام آجائے اس کے لئے قتل کر دیا جائے اور باقی کے لئے مال۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل، احناف کی دلیل: له ان الموجود من الواحد قتلات والذي تحقق في حقه قتل واحد فلا تماثل وهو القياس في الفصل الاول الا انه عرف بالشرع. ولنا ان كل واحد منهم قاتل بوصف الكمال فجاء التماثل اصله الفصل الاول اذلو لم يكن كذلك لما وجب القصاص ولانه وجد من كل واحد منهم جرح صالح للانزهاق فيضاف اليه الذهو لا يتجزى ولان القصاص شرع مع المنافي لتحقيق الاحياء وقد حصل بقتله فاكتفي به. ترجمہ: شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک قاتل کی جانب سے چند قتل موجود ہیں اور اس کے حق میں جو قتل متحقق ہوا وہ ایک قتل ہے تو تماثل نہیں ہوا اور فصل اول میں بھی یہی قیاس تھا مگر وہ شریعت سے معلوم ہوا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اولیاء میں سے ہر ایک وصف کمال کے ساتھ (قصاص میں) قتل کرنے والا ہے تو تماثل پیدا ہو گیا اور اس کی اصل فصل اول ہے اس لئے کہ اگر یہ بات نہ ہوتی تو قصاص نہ ہوتا اور اس لئے کہ ہر ولی کی جانب سے ایسا زخم پایا گیا جو روح نکالنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے تو خروج روح ان میں سے ہر ایک کی جانب مضاف ہوگا اس لئے کہ خروج روح غیر متجزا ہے اور اس لئے کہ قصاص منافی کے باوجود مشروع ہوا ہے احیاء کی تحقیق کیلئے اور تحقق احیاء حاصل ہو چکی ہے تو اس پر اکتفا کر لیا جائے گا۔ تشریح: امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ صرف قاتل کا قتل تمام اولیاء مقتولین کے لئے کافی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قاتل نے متعدد قتل کئے ہیں اور اس کا قتل صرف اسی کا قتل ہے حالانکہ قصاص میں مماثلت ہونی چاہیئے جو یہاں مفقود ہے۔ بلکہ پہلی صورت میں جب کہ مقتول ایک ہو اور قاتل متعدد ہوں قصاص نہ ہونا چاہیئے کیونکہ مماثلت مفقود ہے اور یہی قیاس کا تقاضہ ہے لیکن چونکہ وہ اض عمر فاروق کا فرمان وارد ہو گیا اس لئے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا گیا اور یہاں کوئی ایسی دلیل وارد نہیں ہوئی جو قیاس کے خلاف ہو۔ لہذا قیاس پر عمل کیا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب تمام اولیاء حاضر ہو گئے اور قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بعد انہوں نے خود یا ان کے وکیل نے اس کو مار کر قتل کیا تو دونوں صورتوں میں یہ سمجھا گیا کہ ہر ایک نے اپنا پورا حق قصاص علی سبیل الکمال حاصل کر لیا لہذا تماثل ہے اور جس طرح پہلی صورت میں مقتول ایک ہو اور قاتل متعدد ہوں یہی سمجھا گیا ہے کہ ہر قاتل نے وصف کمال کے ساتھ اس کو قتل کیا ہے ورنہ اس کے بغیر سب سے قصاص نہ لیا جاتا تو یہاں بھی ایسے ہی سمجھا جائے گا۔ اور ان میں سے ہر ایک زخم اس قابل ہے جو خروج روح کا سبب ہے تو انز باق روح کی اضافت ان سب کی جانب ہوگی اس لئے کہ جس طرح قصاص غیر متجزی ہے اس طرح خروج روح بھی غیر متجزی ہے نیز آدمی کے بدن کی چیر پھاڑ ممنوع ہے۔ اور ایسا کرنے والے کو حدیث میں ملعون قرار دیا گیا ہے مگر اس کے باوجود یہاں تحقیق احیاء کی غرض سے قصاص کو مشروع کیا گیا ہے بہر حال جو غرض ہے تحقیق احیاء وہ اس قاتل کو قتل کرنے سے حاصل ہو جاتی ہے اور جب مقصد حاصل ہو گیا تو اس پر اکتفاء کیا جائے گا اور قصاص کے علاوہ مال کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
And when one kills a group, and the heirs of the slain come, he is killed for all of them, and there is nothing for them besides that. If only one heir comes, he is killed for him, and the right of the rest falls. Al-Shafi'i said: He is killed for the first slain, and the rest are owed money. If they all come and the first is not known, he is killed for them and the blood money is divided among them. And it is said: lots are cast among them, and he is killed for the one whose lot emerges.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position is that one killer who murders multiple victims is executed once, and this execution satisfies the right of qisas for all heirs. If only one heir appears, the execution still drops the rights of the others; no diya is owed. Imam al-Shafi'i differentiates: if the killer murdered sequentially, only the first murder triggers qisas; the rest entitle heirs to diya. If simultaneous or unknown order, the killer is executed for all and diya divided—or by lot. The Shafi'i proof relies on qiyas (the principle of equivalence): one execution cannot match multiple deaths, so it is unjust to satisfy all heirs with one life. The Hanafi response uses qiyas on the well-known case where multiple killers execute one victim (which is established by hadith). Here, each heir participates fully in the killing (by themselves or proxy), so each achieves complete qisas. Moreover, the soul's departure is indivisible, akin to qisas itself, and shari'a intended qisas to preserve life; with execution, life is preserved for all, so no additional liability remains.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment by causing the death of the killer equal to the victim’s death, subject to strict equivalence.
تماثل (tamathul): Equivalence between the killer and the victim in terms of life, freedom, and religion, necessary for qisas to be valid.
دیت (diyah): Blood money compensation paid to the heirs of a murder victim when qisas is not executed (e.g., due to waiver or incapability).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if one person kills ten people and all ten heirs come together, what is the ruling?
A) The killer is executed once and this satisfies all ten heirs; no diya is owed.
B) The killer is executed separately for each victim (ten executions).
C) The killer pays diya to nine heirs and is executed for the first.
D) The killer chooses which heir receives qisas and pays others diya.

Key Takeaway
One execution of a multi-murderer satisfies the qisas rights of all victims' heirs in the Hanafi school, based on the indivisibility of death and the purpose of preserving life.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate

Death of the Killer Before Qisas Execution
Ruling with qiyas and cross-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas when the killer dies, explain the qiyas to the slave case, and compare the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Qisas drops upon the killer's death; the body no longer exists as the place of execution.

This lesson examines a fundamental rule in the law of qisas: what happens when the convicted killer dies before the penalty is exacted? The Hanafi school, relying on a clear analogy, holds that the obligation lapses completely unless diya had already been agreed. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, argues that the estate remains liable for either qisas (if possible) or diya. We will unpack the reasoning behind the Hanafi stance and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its original ruling
The act is qisas (retaliatory killing) which is wajib upon the killer. Determine what hukm it carries before the killer's death.
Qisas is a wajib penalty, not a recommended act.
2
State the change upon death
According to the matn, when the killer dies, qisas is dropped. Identify the reason given: loss of the place of execution (maḥall al-istīfā').
The obligation ceases because its object no longer exists.
3
Trace the qiyas to the slave case
The sharh compares this to a slave who commits a crime and then dies. In that case, the master's liability changes. Understand the analogy: as the slave's death prevents qisas, so the free killer's death prevents qisas.
The illa is the loss of the physical subject of execution.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Imam al-Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that either qisas or diya remains obligatory after death. Identify the basis of his disagreement: he ties the obligation to the estate, not solely to the body.
This ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference of ijtihad.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical outcome
The Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that no diya is due unless it was previously agreed or the original case allowed diya as an alternative. Confirm the ruling for fatwa purposes.
If only qisas was pending, the heirs of the victim get nothing from the estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس قاتل پر قصاص تھا وہ فوت ہو جائے تو قصاص ساقط ہو جاتا ہے. قال: ومن وجب عليه القصاص اذا مات سقط القصاص لفوات محل الاستيفاء فاشبه موت العبد الجاني اذا الواجب احدهما خلاف الشافعي. ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس کے اوپر قصاص واجب ہو جب وہ مر گیا تو قصاص ساقط ہو گیا محل استیفاء کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے تو مجرم غلام کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور اس میں شافعی کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک ان دونوں میں سے ایک واجب ہے۔ تشریح: جس قاتل پر قصاص واجب تھا اور دیت دینا طے نہیں ہوا تھا تو اگر وہ قاتل مرجائے تو قصاص بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا کیونکہ جس محل سے قصاص وصول ہوتا وہ چل ہی ختم ہو چکا ہے تو یہ بالکل ایسا ہے جیسے کوئی غلام جنایت کرے اور اس میں وہ غلام دینا پڑے لیکن دینے
The one upon whom qisas is obligatory, when he dies, qisas drops due to the loss of the place of execution, so it resembles the death of a slave who committed assault when one of two (qisas or diya?) is obligatory, unlike al-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from al-Quduri's matn, expanded by the sharh. The ruling: if the person liable for qisas dies before the penalty is exacted, the qisas obligation is dropped. The reason is that the 'place of execution' (مَحل الاستیفاء) has been lost—the living body of the killer no longer exists. The sharh compares this to the case of a slave who commits a crime (assault) and then dies; in that case, the master's liability (either surrendering the slave or paying diya) is affected. The analogy: just as death of a slave removes the option of qisas, so too the killer's death removes qisas. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that qisas or diya (one of them) remains obligatory after death. The Hanafi position is that qisas is purely physical and cannot be applied to a corpse, so it lapses. Note: if diya had already been agreed upon, the obligation would remain on the estate; but if only qisas was outstanding, it falls completely.

Key Terms
محل الاستيفاء (mahall al-istifa'): The physical body of the person upon whom the penalty (qisas) is to be executed.
عبد جاني (abd jani): A slave who commits a crime (e.g., murder or assault) that makes them liable for qisas or diya, with the master responsible for surrender or payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person who is liable for qisas dies before the execution, what happens?
A) Qisas drops completely; no diya is due unless previously agreed.
B) The heirs of the victim can still demand diya from the killer's estate.
C) The killer's body must be mutilated as a substitute.
D) The victim's heirs can choose another person to execute qisas on.

Key Takeaway
Qisas drops upon the killer's death; only an agreed diya survives.

Two Persons Cutting One Hand: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Qisas
Inter-madhhab dispute on qisas for joint amputation of a hand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects qisas when two persons jointly cut one hand and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
When two cut a hand, no qisas because the hand is divisible—unlike murder, which is indivisible.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on whether two persons who jointly cut off a man's hand are subject to retributive amputation. The Hanafi ruling is clear: no qisas on either; both pay half diya. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, analogizing to joint murder. To understand the Hanafi position, we must grasp the concept of divisibility (tajazzi) and the practical realities that distinguish hand-cutting from killing.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its basis
Identify the direct ruling from the matn: no qisas, half diya on each. Then note the two key reasons: the hand is divisible (mutajazzi) so each cutter only cuts part, destroying equivalence; and joint hand-cutting is rare because slow steps invite rescue, unlike joint murder which is common for fear of rescue.
The Hanafi position is built on two distinct arguments—one based on the nature of the hand (divisibility) and one on practical occurrence (commonness).
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both cutters' hands should be cut in qisas. His proof is qiyas: analogizing hand-cutting to homicide. In joint murder, both killers are executed; similarly, because limbs are subordinate to the soul, the same rule applies. The common illa is deterrence (zajr).
Al-Shafi'i's qiyas is based on a general principle (limbs follow the soul) and the shared goal of deterrence.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal via divisibility
The Hanafis argue that the hand is divisible (mutajazzi): each cutter only cuts part of the hand, so the cutting is attributed partially to each. Hence there is no exact equivalence (mumathala) between crime and punishment, which qisas requires. The soul is indivisible, so each killer fully causes death, allowing qisas on both.
Divisibility is the core fiqh concept: the hand can be split into portions, so the crime is partial; the soul cannot be split, so the crime is complete.
4
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal regarding commonness and rescue
The Hanafis further argue that joint murder is common because accomplices gather to prevent rescue, whereas joint hand-cutting is rare because it requires slow deliberate steps (holding the victim, positioning the knife) that would allow rescue to intervene. Thus the analogy fails because the situations are not comparable in practice.
This rebuttal shows that the Hanafis consider not just legal theory but also real-world circumstances in evaluating qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the operative ruling
The practical difference: Hanafis impose half diya on each cutter (total diya for hand is paid by both), while Shafi'is require both cutters to lose their hands. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the ruling of half diya, as preferred in al-Hidayah.
The dispute is legitimate ikhtilaf; students should recognize that both schools have consistent reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جب دو شخصوں نے ایک مرد کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا تو قصاص کسی پر نہیں بلکہ دونوں پر دیت ہے
قال واذا قطع رجلان يد رجل واحد فلا قصاص على واحد منهما وعليهما نصف الدية وقال الشافعي يقطع يداهما والمفرض اذا اخذ اسكينا وامراه على يده حتى انقطعت له الاعتبار بالا نفس والايدى تابعة لها اخذت حكمها او يجمع بينهما بجامع الزجر
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب دو شخصوں نے ایک مرد کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا تو ان دونوں میں سے کسی پر قصاص نہیں ہے اور ان دونوں پر آدھی دیت ہوگی۔ اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ دونوں کا ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ اور مسئلہ کا محل فرض جب کہ ان دونوں نے چھری پکڑی ہو اور اس کو اس کے ہاتھ پر چلایا ہو یہاں تک کہ ہاتھ کٹ جائے۔ شافعی کی دلیل انفس پر قیاس کرنا ہے اور ہاتھ انفس کے تابع ہیں تو ہاتھ انفس کا حکم لے گا یا ان دونوں کے درمیان جامع زجر کی وجہ سے جمع کیا جائے گا۔
تشریح زید اور بکر نے مل کر خالد کا ایک ہاتھ کاٹ دیا تو کیا حکم ہے؟ اس میں امام شافعی کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ زید اور بکر دونوں کا ہاتھ قصاص میں کاٹ دیا جائے کیونکہ اگر زید اور بکر دونوں مل کر خالد کو قتل کرتے تب بھی دونوں سے قصاص لیا جاتا۔ لہذا یہاں بھی دونوں سے ہاتھ کا قصاص لیا جائے گا۔ خلاصہ کلام امام شافعی نے ہاتھ کو نفس پر قیاس کیا ہے بالفاظ دیگر قطع ید کو قتل پر قیاس کیا ہے اور علت جامعہ مشترک کہ دونوں کے درمیان حکمت زجر ہے جو دونوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے بالفاظ دیگر اطراف انفس کے تابع ہیں اور تابع کا وہی حکم ہونا چاہیئے جو متبوع کا ہے۔ تنبیہ ہمارا اور امام شافعی کا اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ دونوں نے ایک چھری پکڑ کر اس کے ہاتھ پر چلائی ہو۔ ور نہ اگر دونوں نے الگ الگ چھری لے کر ایک نے ایک طرف سے اور دوسرے نے دوسری طرف سے کاٹنا شروع کیا یہاں تک کہ دونوں کی چھری مل گئی یعنی پورا ہاتھ کٹ گیا تو یہاں امام شافعی کے نزدیک بھی قصاص نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر یہی صورت حلق کاٹنے میں پیش آئی تو بالا اتفاق دونوں پر قصاص واجب ہوگا۔
احناف کی دلیل
ولنا ان كل واحد منهما قاطع بعض اليد لان الانقطاع حصل باعتماد بهما والمحل متجز فيضاف الى كل ض فلا مماثلة بخلاف النفس لان الانزهاق لا يتجزى
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک ہاتھ کے بعض حصہ کو کاٹنے والا ہے اس لئے انقطاع ان دونوں کے بوجھ سے حاصل ہوا ہے اور محل (ید) منجزی ہے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی جانب بعض کی اضافت کی جائے گی تو مماثلت نہیں ہوگی بخلاف نفس کے اس لئے کہ خروج روح غیر منجزی ہے۔ تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ زید اور بکر میں سے ہر ایک نے اس کا کچھ ہاتھ کاٹا ہے کیونکہ چھری پر دونوں کا ہاتھ ہے اور دونوں کے سہارے سے چھری سے کام کیا ہے اور خالد کا ہاتھ بھی قابل تجزی ہے لہذا یہ ضروری ہو گیا کہ یوں کہا جائے کہ پورا پورا ہاتھ کٹا تو مماثلت ختم ہو گئی حالانکہ قصاص کے اندر مماثلت ضروری ہے (كما مر) اور رہا مسئلہ قتل کا تو اس کی حقیقت ازهاق روح ہے جس کو غیر متجزی شمار کیا گیا ہے اور جب اس کو غیر متجزی شمار کیا گیا ہے تو ضروری ہے کہ ہر ایک کی جانب زهوق روح کی اضافت علی سبیل الکمال ہو۔ اور جب دونوں کی جانب کامل اضافت ہو گئی تو دونوں سے قصاص لیا جائے گا۔
امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب
ولان القتل بطريق الاجتماع غالب حذر الغوث والاجتماع على قطع اليد من المفصل في حيز الندرة لافتقاره الى مقدمات بطيئة فيلحقه الغوث
ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ قتل بطریق اجتماع کے طور پر غالب ہے فریادرس کے خوف سے اور اجتماع جوڑ سے ہاتھ کاٹنے پر نادر ہے اس کے محتاج ہونے کی وجہ سے ایسے مقدمات کی جانب جو دیر طلب ہیں تو اس کو فریادرس لاحق ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح یہاں سے مصنف امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ آپ کا قیاس مذکور صحیح نہیں اس لئے کہ مقیس علیہ اور مقیس کے درمیان مناسبت چاہیئے اور یہاں ان دونوں میں کوئی مناسبت نہیں ہے۔ کیسے؟ تو فرمایا اس لئے کہ مقیس علیہ قتل ہے اور اس میں عموما معاونین کا اجتماع ہوتا ہے تاکہ کوئی حمایتی آ کر قتل نہ ہونے دے اس لئے چند جمع ہو جاتے ہیں تا کہ کام جلدی ہو جائے۔ اور مقیس قطع ید ہے اور اس میں عموما لوگوں کا یعنی معاونین کا اجتماع نہیں ہوتا اس وجہ سے کہ جب جوڑ سے ہاتھ کٹے گا تو اس میں دیر لگے گی کیونکہ اس ہاتھ کو پکڑنے کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی جس کو کاٹنا ہے اور چھری چلانے کی وغیرہ وغیرہ اور جب معاونین کا اجتماع ہوگا ادھر یہ کام دیر طلب ہے تو ان کے شور وغیرہ سے مقطوع کا کوئی حمایتی آ کھڑا ہوگا جس سے یہ کام نہ ہو سکے گا تو ضرورت ہے کہ یہاں اجتماع نہ ہوتا کہ شور نہ ہو اور کام ہو سکے۔ خلاصہ کلام مقیس علیہ میں اجتماع ہے اور مقیس میں اجتماع نہیں ہے تو ان دونوں کے درمیان مناسبت نہیں ہے لہذا قیاس صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
When two persons cut off the hand of one man, then there is no qisas on either of them, and upon both is half the diya. The author (al-Quduri) said: And when two men cut the hand of one man, then there is no qisas on either of them, and upon both is half the diya. And al-Shafi'i said: Both their hands shall be cut. And the context is when both took a knife and together placed it on his hand until it was cut off. Al-Shafi'i's proof is to analogize to souls (anfus), and hands are subordinate to souls, so hands take the ruling of souls, or to combine them due to the common element of deterrence (zajr). Explanation: Zayd and Bakr together cut off Khalid's hand; what is the ruling? According to Imam al-Shafi'i, both Zayd and Bakr's hands should be cut in retribution, because if they had jointly killed Khalid, qisas would be taken from both. So here also, qisas of the hand should be taken from both. In summary, Imam al-Shafi'i analogized the hand to the soul. Our evidence: Each of them is a cutter of part of the hand, because the severance occurred by their combined force, and the locus (the hand) is divisible, so the cutting is attributed to each partially, thus there is no equivalence (mumathala), unlike the soul because the exit of the soul is indivisible. And because killing by joint action is common due to fear of rescue, whereas joint cutting of a hand from the joint is rare because it requires slow preparatory steps, so rescue would intervene. Thus the analogy is invalid.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the case of two persons jointly cutting off one hand of a man. The Hanafi ruling, as stated in the matn, is that neither of the two cutters is subject to qisas (retributive amputation); instead, they are jointly liable for half the diya (blood money). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both cutters should have their own hands cut in retaliation. The author first clarifies the scenario: both cutters hold a single knife together and apply it to the victim's hand until it is severed. If they used separate knives, even al-Shafi'i would not require qisas. The author then presents al-Shafi'i's evidence: he analogizes this case to joint homicide—if two people jointly kill one person, both are executed in qisas; similarly, since limbs are subordinate to the soul, the same rule should apply to hand-cutting. The common element justifying the analogy is deterrence (zajr). The Hanafi response consists of two parts. First, the hand is divisible (mutajazzi), meaning each cutter only severs part of it; the cutting is attributed to each partially, so there is no exact equivalence (mumathala) between the crime and the punishment. In contrast, the soul is indivisible, so each killer fully causes death, making qisas applicable to both. Second, the situations differ in practice: joint homicide is common because accomplices gather to overcome the victim's resistance, but joint hand-cutting from the joint is rare because it requires slow, deliberate steps that would allow time for rescue. Hence, the analogy fails for lack of a shared effective cause.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retributive punishment in kind, e.g., amputation of a hand for cutting a hand.
دية (diya): Financial compensation paid to the victim or heirs for bodily harm or homicide.
متجزي (mutajazzi): Divisible; capable of being split into parts. Here, the hand is considered divisible because the cut can be attributed to each participant partially.
زجر (zajr): Deterrence; the rationale for punishment to prevent future crimes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when two persons jointly cut off one hand of a man using one knife?
A) Both cutters are subject to qisas (their hands are cut).
B) Neither cutter is subject to qisas; both pay half the diya.
C) Only the primary cutter pays full diya.
D) The victim can choose between qisas and diya from both.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that no qisas applies when two persons cut one hand hinges on the hand's divisibility and the practical rarity of joint hand-cutting, distinguishing it from joint murder.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Qisas for Two Victims
Dispute: Hanafi refutes Shafi'i qiyas to rahn in qisas case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on qisas when one aggressor cuts the hands of two victims and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal of the Shafi'i analogy to rahn.

Core Idea
Qisas is ownership of the act, not the limb; multiple victims' rights coexist like creditors' claims in an estate.

When one aggressor severs the hands of two individuals, can both victims demand qisas? Imam Shafi'i holds that only one can get qisas, decided by lottery, analogizing to pawned property. The Hanafi school disagrees, arguing that qisas is a right to an action, not ownership of the limb itself, so multiple claims can coexist. This lesson walks through the two positions and the Hanafi critique of the Shafi'i analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Identify the Shafi'i ruling: lottery decides which victim gets qisas; the other receives diya. Understand their proof: analogy to rahn (pledge), where once an item is pawned, it cannot be re-pawned.
Shafi'i argues that the first claim on the hand prevents a second claim.
2
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: both victims are equal in entitlement to qisas. They share the right just as creditors share in an estate.
Hanafi holds that qisas is ownership of an action (malak al-fi'l), not of the person.
3
Analyse the Hanafi dalil
Examine the Hanafi proof: equality in cause (both hands cut) leads to equality in ruling. Compare to creditors with debts at different times who share equally in the deceased's estate.
Also note the distinction between malak al-fi'l and malak al-'ayn.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal
Understand why the Hanafi school says the Shafi'i analogy to rahn is qiyas ma' al-fariq (invalid analogy). The key difference: rahn establishes a right in the object itself, preventing a second claim, whereas qisas only establishes ownership of the act, not the limb.
Thus, multiple claims can accumulate in qisas because the locus (the aggressor's hand) remains free of ownership.

احناف کی دلیل اور امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب

ولنا انهما استويا في سبب الاستحقاق فيستويان في حكمه كالغريمين فى التركة والقصاص ملك الفعل يثبت مع المنافى فلا يظهرا لا فى حق الاستيفاء اما المحل فخلو عنه فلا يمنع ثبوت الثانى بخلاف الرهن لان الحق ثابت في المجل

ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ دونوں استحقاق کے سبب میں برابر ہیں تو یہ دونوں سبب کے حکم میں برابر ہوں گے جیسے دو قر ضخواہ ترکہ کے اندر اور قصاص ایک فعل کی ایسی ملکیت ہے جو منافی کے ساتھ ثابت ہوتی ہے تو یہ ملکیت صرف استیفاء کے حق میں ظاہر ہو گی بہر حال پس محل وہ ملک سے خالی ہے تو یہ ملک ثانی کے ثبوت کو نہیں روکے گی۔ بخلاف رہن کے اس لئے کہ حق استیفا محل کے اندر ثابت ہے۔ تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ چونکہ زید اور بکر دونوں کا ہاتھ کٹا ہے تو قصاص بھی دونوں کو ملنا چاہیئے کیونکہ سبب میں جب دونوں برابر ہیں تو حکم کے اندر بھی برابر ہوں گے اور اس کا وہی طریقہ ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ اس کی مثال بعینہ ایسی ہے کہ زید کے ذمہ بکر کے پچاس روپے قرض ہیں اور خالد کے چالیس اور ساجد کے چالیس اور یہ سب قرض مختلف زمانوں میں اس نے لئے ہیں اب زید کا انتقال ہوتا ہے اور مال چھوڑتا ہے تو اس ترکہ میں سب کا حق برابر ہے یہ نہیں دیکھا جائے گا کہ جس کا قرض پہلا ہو اسی کو حق متقدم حاصل ہو اسی طرح یہاں پر بھی یہ نہیں دیکھا جائے گا بلکہ صرف سبب کے اندر مساوات کی وجہ سے حکم کے اندر مساوات ثابت کر دی جائے گی۔

والـقـصـاص ملک الفعل .... الخ یہاں سے مصنف یہ بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ کور بہن کے مسئلہ پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔

دیکھئے قصاص میں ولی قصاص قاتل کا مالک نہیں ہوتا بلکہ صرف ولی کو اتنا حق ملتا ہے کہ وہ قصاص وصول کرے اگر چہ وہ قاتل کا مالک نہ ہو سکے گا کیونکہ قاتل آزاد ہے اور جو مرہون رہن رکھا گیا ہے وہ ملوک ہے اور مملوک کے اندر مرتہن کا حق مرہون کی ذات سے وابستہ ہو جاتا ہے اگر چہ وہ مالیت کے اعتبار سے ہوتا ہے لیکن بہر حال اس کے حق کا تعلق محل سے ہے کیونکہ مرتین محل ہی سے اپنا حق وصول کرے گا تو یہاں منافی سے یہی مراد ہے کہ قاتل ہونے کی وجہ سے مملوک نہیں ہو سکتا تو اس کا تقاضہ یہ تھا کہ اس کے خر ہونے کی وجہ سے ولی کو حق قصاص بھی نہ ملے مگر ہم نے منافی کے باوجود حق قصاص دیا لیکن قصاص کی حقیقت صرف ایک فعل کا مالک بنانا ہے محل اور ذات کی ملکیت اس میں ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ لہذا یہ ملک فعل صرف یہاں تک کام کرے گا کہ ولی قصاص اپنا حق وصول کر سکتا ہے۔ رہی قاتل کی ذات اور محل قصاص اس میں ولی قصاص کی کوئی ملکیت نہیں ہے جب یہ اصول ذہن نشین ہو گیا تو دوسرا اصول یہ سمجھئے کہ جس جگہ کسی کا حق محل میں ثابت نہ ہو صرف ملک فعل سے اس کا تعلق ہو تو وہاں ملک فعل کا اجتماع ہو سکتا ہے۔ اور جہاں حق کا تعلق محل سے وہاں ایک حق کے ثبوت کے بعد دوسرے کا حق ثابت نہیں ہو سکتا۔ لہذا ر ہن کا تعلق چونکہ محل سے ہے اس وجہ سے اب اس مرہون کو دوسرے کے پاس رہن نہیں رکھا جا سکتا اور قصاص کا تعلق ملک فعل سے ہے۔ جس میں ملکیت کے حق کا ثبوت دوسرے کا حق ثابت ہونے سے نہیں روکتا۔ خلاصه کلام امام شافعی کا مذکورہ مسئلہ میں قصاص کو رہن کے مسئلہ پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔

هذا من مزالت الاقدام ولم تجد هذا الاسلوب في الشروح

ایک مثال سے احناف کے مسلک کی تائید

وصار كما اذا قطع العبد يمينيهما على التعاقب فتستحق رقبته لهما ترجمہ اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے غلام نے ان دونوں کے ہاتھ کانٹے ہوں یکے بعد دیگرے تو ان دونوں کے لئے اس کی اردن کا استحقاق ہو گیا۔

تشریح اس مثال سے مصنف حنفیہ کے مسلک کی تائید فرماتے ہیں کہتے ہیں اگر کسی غلام نے زید اور بکر کا ہاتھ حسب سابق کاٹ دیا تو یہاں بھی دونوں کا استحقاق غلام کی گردن میں ثابت ہو گا یعنی یہ غلام ان دونوں کو دیدیا جائے گا لہذا اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہاں ایک کے اسے حق کا ثبوت دوسرے کے حق کے ثبوت سے مانع نہیں ہے اسی طرح پہلے مسئلے میں بھی ہو گا۔
And if both hands were cut at once, then in that case a lottery is drawn; whose name comes out, his hand is cut in retaliation, and the other is given the blood money for his hand, because in the case of succession, the first had already become entitled to the cutter's hand, so the right of the second cannot be established therein, just as on the basis of this principle, after a pledged item is pawned to one, it cannot be pawned again to another. And if it is a simultaneous case, then since the cutter's one hand cannot be the substitute for both their hands, whose hand should be cut in exchange? In that, a lottery is drawn, then his hand is cut in exchange, and the other is given the blood money. This is Imam Shafi'i's proof.

Our proof and answer to Imam Shafi'i's analogy:

And for us, they are equal in the cause of entitlement, so they are equal in its ruling, like two creditors in an estate. And qisas is ownership of an action, established despite inconsistency; it does not appear except in the right of execution. As for the locus, it is free from ownership, so it does not prevent the establishment of the second, unlike rahn, because the right is established in the locus.

Translation: And our proof is that these two are equal in the cause of entitlement, so they will be equal in the ruling of the cause, like two creditors in an estate. And qisas is an ownership of an action that is established despite inconsistency; so this ownership will only appear in the right of execution. In any case, the locus is devoid of ownership, so it will not prevent the establishment of the second ownership. Unlike rahn, because the right of execution is established in the locus. Commentary: This is our proof, the gist of which is that since both Zaid and Bakr's hands are cut, both should get qisas, because when they are equal in cause, they will also be equal in ruling. And its method is what we have explained. Its exact example is that Zaid owes fifty rupees to Bakr, forty to Khalid, and forty to Sajid, and he borrowed these debts at different times. Now Zaid dies and leaves property, then all have equal rights in that estate; it will not be considered that the one whose debt was earlier gets prior right. Similarly, here also it will not be considered, rather due to equality in cause, equality in ruling will be established.

'And qisas is ownership of action...' From here, the author wants to say that analogizing this issue to the issue of rahn is an analogy with a difference.

See, in qisas, the guardian of qisas does not own the killer; rather, the guardian only gets the right to execute qisas, although he cannot own the killer because the killer is free. And the pledged item is owned, and in the owned, the mortgagee's right attaches to the pawned item's essence, although it is in terms of value. But in any case, his right is related to the locus, because the mortgagee will collect his right from the locus. So here, the meaning of inconsistency is that due to being a killer, he cannot become owned, so its requirement was that due to his becoming free, the guardian should not get the right of qisas either, but we gave the right of qisas despite the inconsistency. But the reality of qisas is merely making one the owner of an action; ownership of the locus and the person is not established therein. Therefore, this ownership of action will only work to the extent that the guardian can execute his right. As for the killer's person and the locus of qisas, the guardian has no ownership. When this principle is understood, then understand the second principle: that where someone's right is not established in the locus, only the ownership of action relates, then the accumulation of ownership of action is possible. And where the right relates to the locus, after one right is established, another's right cannot be established. Therefore, since rahn's relation is to the locus, for that reason the pawned item cannot be pawned again to another. And qisas's relation is to ownership of action, in which the establishment of the right of ownership does not prevent the establishment of another's right. Summary: Imam Shafi'i's analogizing qisas to the issue of rahn in the mentioned issue is an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma' al-fariq).

This is from the slippery steps of feet, and you will not find this style in the commentaries.

Support for the Hanafi school with an example:

And it becomes as if a slave cut the right hands of both of them successively, then his neck becomes entitled to both of them. Translation: And it becomes as if a slave cut both their hands one after the other, then both of them become entitled to his neck.

Commentary: With this example, the author supports the Hanafi school. He says, if a slave cut Zaid and Bakr's hand according to the previous situation, then here also both would have entitlement to the slave's neck, meaning this slave will be given to both of them. Hence, it is learned that here the establishment of one's right does not prevent the establishment of another's right; similarly in the first issue.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents a legal dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding a case where a person cuts off the right hands of two individuals. Imam Shafi'i argues that only one hand can be cut in retaliation (qisas) because a single hand cannot compensate for two, so a lottery is drawn; the winner gets qisas and the loser gets blood money. He supports this by analogy to a pawned item: once pawned to one, it cannot be pawned to another, implying that the right of the first victim precludes the second's claim to qisas.

The Hanafi school responds with two arguments. First, both victims are equal in the cause of entitlement (both had their hands cut), so they should be equal in the ruling. Just as creditors with different debt timings share equally in the deceased's estate, here both victims share equally in the right to qisas. Second, the nature of qisas differs from rahn. Qisas is ownership of an action (malak al-fi'l), not ownership of a person or object. The right attaches only to the act of execution, not to the aggressor's person. Therefore, multiple rights can accumulate because the locus (the aggressor's hand) is free from prior ownership. In rahn, the right attaches to the object itself, preventing a second pledge. Thus, analogizing qisas to rahn is an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma' al-fariq).

The passage further supports the Hanafi position with an example: if a slave cuts both victims' hands, the slave's entire body (neck) is given to both victims jointly, showing that multiple claims can coexist without one preventing the other.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for bodily harm; here, cutting the aggressor's hand equal to the victim's hand.
دیت (diya): Blood money compensation paid to the victim or heirs when qisas is not applicable or is waived.
ملک الفعل (malak al-fi'l): Ownership of an action, i.e., the right to execute qisas by performing the act of retaliation, not ownership of the person or limb.
رہن (rahn): Pawn or mortgage; a contract where an asset is held as security for a debt.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma' al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because of a significant difference between the cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rebuttal, why is the Shafi'i analogy to rahn considered invalid (qiyas ma' al-fariq)?
A) Because rahn involves a dead object while qisas involves a living person.
B) Because qisas is ownership of an action, not ownership of a specific object.
C) Because the Quran explicitly allows multiple qisas claims.
D) Because the victims can agree to share the hand.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that qisas is ownership of the act of retaliation, not the limb, allowing multiple victims equal entitlement—unlike the Shafi'i view that analogizes to pawned property.

Qisas — Retaliation

Malak al-Fi'l: The Hanafi Foundation for Multiple Qisas Claims
Conceptual analysis: defining malak al-fi'l and its implications for qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of malak al-fi'l (ownership of action) and apply it to distinguish qisas from rahn in cases of multiple victims.

Core Idea
Qisas is ownership of the act of retaliation, not the limb, so multiple rights can coexist.

The concept of 'ownership of an action' (malak al-fi'l) is a distinctive Hanafi doctrine that shapes the school's approach to qisas. Unlike ownership of a physical object, this concept allows multiple rights to accumulate on the same locus. This lesson unpacks the definition, its contrast with rahn, and its application through the slave example in the text.

Guided Path
1
Define malak al-fi'l
Understand that malak al-fi'l means the right to perform a specific act—here, the act of retaliation in qisas. It is not ownership of the aggressor's person or limb.
The text says: 'القصاص ملك الفعل' (qisas is ownership of an action).
2
Contrast with ownership of an object (malak al-'ayn)
In rahn, the mortgagee's right is established in the object itself (haqq fi al-'ayn), which prevents a second claim. In qisas, the right is only to the act, not the object.
The text says: 'بخلاف الرهن لان الحق ثابت في المحل' (unlike rahn, because the right is established in the locus).
3
Apply the concept to the dispute
Because qisas is malak al-fi'l, both victims can have the right to execute the act of retaliation on the same aggressor, even if physically only one can be carried out. The right is equal in principle.
The slave example illustrates: the slave's neck becomes entitled to both victims, showing accumulation of claims.
4
Analyse the supporting example
The text gives an example: if a slave cuts both victims' hands, the slave's entire person (neck) is subject to both victims' claims. This shows that multiple malak al-fi'l rights can exist on one person.
This supports the Hanafi position that qisas rights can accumulate.
